# LazyFrame вҖ” Polars  documentation

[Skip to main content](#main-content)

Back to top Ctrl+K

Choose version

*   [GitHub](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars "GitHub")
    
*   [Discord](https://discord.gg/4UfP5cfBE7 "Discord")

LazyFrame[#](#lazyframe "Link to this heading")

================================================

This page gives an overview of all public LazyFrame methods.

_class_ polars.LazyFrame(

_data: FrameInitTypes | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_schema: SchemaDefinition | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_\*_,

_schema\_overrides: SchemaDict | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_strict: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_orient: Orientation | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_infer\_schema\_length: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= 100_,

_nan\_to\_null: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

)[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L190-L7714)

Representation of a Lazy computation graph/query against a DataFrame.

This allows for whole-query optimisation in addition to parallelism, and is the preferred (and highest-performance) mode of operation for polars.

Parameters:

**data**dict, Sequence, ndarray, Series, or pandas.DataFrame

Two-dimensional data in various forms; dict input must contain Sequences, Generators, or a `range`. Sequence may contain Series or other Sequences.

**schema**Sequence of str, (str,DataType) pairs, or a {str:DataType,} dict

The LazyFrame schema may be declared in several ways:

*   As a dict of {name:type} pairs; if type is None, it will be auto-inferred.
    
*   As a list of column names; in this case types are automatically inferred.
    
*   As a list of (name,type) pairs; this is equivalent to the dictionary form.
    

If you supply a list of column names that does not match the names in the underlying data, the names given here will overwrite them. The number of names given in the schema should match the underlying data dimensions.

**schema\_overrides**dict, default None

Support type specification or override of one or more columns; note that any dtypes inferred from the schema param will be overridden.

The number of entries in the schema should match the underlying data dimensions, unless a sequence of dictionaries is being passed, in which case a _partial_ schema can be declared to prevent specific fields from being loaded.

**strict**bool, default True

Throw an error if any `data` value does not exactly match the given or inferred data type for that column. If set to `False`, values that do not match the data type are cast to that data type or, if casting is not possible, set to null instead.

**orient**{вҖҳcolвҖҷ, вҖҳrowвҖҷ}, default None

Whether to interpret two-dimensional data as columns or as rows. If None, the orientation is inferred by matching the columns and data dimensions. If this does not yield conclusive results, column orientation is used.

**infer\_schema\_length**int or None

The maximum number of rows to scan for schema inference. If set to `None`, the full data may be scanned _(this can be slow)_. This parameter only applies if the input data is a sequence or generator of rows; other input is read as-is.

**nan\_to\_null**bool, default False

If the data comes from one or more numpy arrays, can optionally convert input data np.nan values to null instead. This is a no-op for all other input data.

Notes

Initialising `LazyFrame(...)` directly is equivalent to `DataFrame(...).lazy()`.

Examples

Constructing a LazyFrame directly from a dictionary:

\>>> data \= {"a": \[1, 2\], "b": \[3, 4\]}
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(data)
\>>> lf.collect()
shape: (2, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Notice that the dtypes are automatically inferred as Polars Int64:

\>>> lf.collect\_schema().dtypes()
\[Int64, Int64\]

To specify a more detailed/specific frame schema you can supply the `schema` parameter with a dictionary of (name,dtype) pairsвҖҰ

\>>> data \= {"col1": \[0, 2\], "col2": \[3, 7\]}
\>>> lf2 \= pl.LazyFrame(data, schema\={"col1": pl.Float32, "col2": pl.Int64})
\>>> lf2.collect()
shape: (2, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ col1 в”Ҷ col2 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ f32  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 0.0  в”Ҷ 3    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2.0  в”Ҷ 7    в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

вҖҰa sequence of (name,dtype) pairsвҖҰ

\>>> data \= {"col1": \[1, 2\], "col2": \[3, 4\]}
\>>> lf3 \= pl.LazyFrame(data, schema\=\[("col1", pl.Float32), ("col2", pl.Int64)\])
\>>> lf3.collect()
shape: (2, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ col1 в”Ҷ col2 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ f32  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1.0  в”Ҷ 3    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2.0  в”Ҷ 4    в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

вҖҰor a list of typed Series.

\>>> data \= \[\
...     pl.Series("col1", \[1, 2\], dtype\=pl.Float32),\
...     pl.Series("col2", \[3, 4\], dtype\=pl.Int64),\
... \]
\>>> lf4 \= pl.LazyFrame(data)
\>>> lf4.collect()
shape: (2, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ col1 в”Ҷ col2 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ f32  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1.0  в”Ҷ 3    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2.0  в”Ҷ 4    в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Constructing a LazyFrame from a numpy ndarray, specifying column names:

\>>> import numpy as np
\>>> data \= np.array(\[(1, 2), (3, 4)\], dtype\=np.int64)
\>>> lf5 \= pl.LazyFrame(data, schema\=\["a", "b"\], orient\="col")
\>>> lf5.collect()
shape: (2, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Constructing a LazyFrame from a list of lists, row orientation specified:

\>>> data \= \[\[1, 2, 3\], \[4, 5, 6\]\]
\>>> lf6 \= pl.LazyFrame(data, schema\=\["a", "b", "c"\], orient\="row")
\>>> lf6.collect()
shape: (2, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 4   в”Ҷ 5   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

| `fetch` | Collect a small number of rows for debugging purposes. |

approx\_n\_unique() вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L6043-L6073)

Approximate count of unique values.

Deprecated since version 0.20.11: Use `select(pl.all().approx_n_unique())` instead.

This is done using the HyperLogLog++ algorithm for cardinality estimation.

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[1, 2, 3, 4\],
...         "b": \[1, 2, 1, 1\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.approx\_n\_unique().collect()  
shape: (1, 2)

в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ u32 в”Ҷ u32 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў

bottom\_k(

_k: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
_,

_\*_,

_by: IntoExpr | Iterable\[IntoExpr\]_,

_reverse: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Sequence\[[bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] \= False_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L1584-L1657)

Return the `k` smallest rows.

Non-null elements are always preferred over null elements, regardless of the value of `reverse`. The output is not guaranteed to be in any particular order, call [`sort()`](api/polars.LazyFrame.sort.html#polars.LazyFrame.sort "polars.LazyFrame.sort")
 after this function if you wish the output to be sorted.

Parameters:

**k**

Number of rows to return.

**by**

Column(s) used to determine the bottom rows. Accepts expression input. Strings are parsed as column names.

**reverse**

Consider the `k` largest elements of the `by` column(s) (instead of the `k` smallest). This can be specified per column by passing a sequence of booleans.

See also

[`top_k`](api/polars.LazyFrame.top_k.html#polars.LazyFrame.top_k "polars.LazyFrame.top_k")

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \["a", "b", "a", "b", "b", "c"\],
...         "b": \[2, 1, 1, 3, 2, 1\],
...     }
... )

Get the rows which contain the 4 smallest values in column b.

\>>> lf.bottom\_k(4, by\="b").collect()
shape: (4, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Get the rows which contain the 4 smallest values when sorting on column a and b.

\>>> lf.bottom\_k(4, by\=\["a", "b"\]).collect()
shape: (4, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ

в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ

cache() вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L3290-L3296)

Cache the result once the execution of the physical plan hits this node.

It is not recommended using this as the optimizer likely can do a better job.

cast(

_dtypes: Mapping\[ColumnNameOrSelector | PolarsDataType, PolarsDataType | PythonDataType\] | PolarsDataType_,

_\*_,

_strict: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L3298-L3400)

Cast LazyFrame column(s) to the specified dtype(s).

Parameters:

**dtypes**

Mapping of column names (or selector) to dtypes, or a single dtype to which all columns will be cast.

**strict**

Throw an error if a cast could not be done (for instance, due to an overflow).

Examples

\>>> from datetime import date
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6.0, 7.0, 8.0\],
...         "ham": \[date(2020, 1, 2), date(2021, 3, 4), date(2022, 5, 6)\],
...     }
... )

Cast specific frame columns to the specified dtypes:

\>>> lf.cast({"foo": pl.Float32, "bar": pl.UInt8}).collect()
shape: (3, 3)

collect(

_\*_,

_type\_coercion: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_\_type\_check: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_predicate\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_projection\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_simplify\_expression: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_slice\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_comm\_subplan\_elim: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_comm\_subexpr\_elim: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_cluster\_with\_columns: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_collapse\_joins: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_no\_optimization: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_streaming: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_engine: EngineType \= 'cpu'_,

_background: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_\_check\_order: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_\_eager: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_\*\*\_kwargs: Any_,

) вҶ’ DataFrame | InProcessQuery[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L1903-L2125)

Materialize this LazyFrame into a DataFrame.

By default, all query optimizations are enabled. Individual optimizations may be disabled by setting the corresponding parameter to `False`.

Parameters:

**type\_coercion**

Do type coercion optimization.

**predicate\_pushdown**

Do predicate pushdown optimization.

**projection\_pushdown**

Do projection pushdown optimization.

**simplify\_expression**

Run simplify expressions optimization.

**slice\_pushdown**

Slice pushdown optimization.

**comm\_subplan\_elim**

Will try to cache branching subplans that occur on self-joins or unions.

**comm\_subexpr\_elim**

Common subexpressions will be cached and reused.

**cluster\_with\_columns**

Combine sequential independent calls to with\_columns

**collapse\_joins**

Collapse a join and filters into a faster join

**no\_optimization**

Turn off (certain) optimizations.

**streaming**

Process the query in batches to handle larger-than-memory data. If set to `False` (default), the entire query is processed in a single batch.

Warning

Streaming mode is considered **unstable**. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.

Note

Use [`explain()`](api/polars.LazyFrame.explain.html#polars.LazyFrame.explain "polars.LazyFrame.explain")
 to see if Polars can process the query in streaming mode.

**engine**

Select the engine used to process the query, optional. If set to `"cpu"` (default), the query is run using the polars CPU engine. If set to `"gpu"`, the GPU engine is used. Fine-grained control over the GPU engine, for example which device to use on a system with multiple devices, is possible by providing a [`GPUEngine`](api/polars.lazyframe.engine_config.GPUEngine.html#polars.lazyframe.engine_config.GPUEngine "polars.lazyframe.engine_config.GPUEngine")
 object with configuration options.

Note

GPU mode is considered **unstable**. Not all queries will run successfully on the GPU, however, they should fall back transparently to the default engine if execution is not supported.

Running with `POLARS_VERBOSE=1` will provide information if a query falls back (and why).

Note

The GPU engine does not support streaming, or running in the background. If either are enabled, then GPU execution is switched off.

**background**

Run the query in the background and get a handle to the query. This handle can be used to fetch the result or cancel the query.

Warning

Background mode is considered **unstable**. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.

Returns:

DataFrame

See also

[`explain`](api/polars.LazyFrame.explain.html#polars.LazyFrame.explain "polars.LazyFrame.explain")

Print the query plan that is evaluated with collect.

[`profile`](api/polars.LazyFrame.profile.html#polars.LazyFrame.profile "polars.LazyFrame.profile")

Collect the LazyFrame and time each node in the computation graph.

Collect multiple LazyFrames at the same time.

Set the size of streaming batches.

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \["a", "b", "a", "b", "b", "c"\],

...         "c": \[6, 5, 4, 3, 2, 1\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.group\_by("a").agg(pl.all().sum()).collect()

collect\_async(

_\*_,

_gevent: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_type\_coercion: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_\_type\_check: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_predicate\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_projection\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_simplify\_expression: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_no\_optimization: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_slice\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_comm\_subplan\_elim: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_comm\_subexpr\_elim: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_cluster\_with\_columns: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_collapse\_joins: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_streaming: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_\_check\_order: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

) вҶ’ Awaitable\[DataFrame\] | \_GeventDataFrameResult\[DataFrame\][\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L2165-L2313)

Collect DataFrame asynchronously in thread pool.

Warning

This functionality is considered **unstable**. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.

Collects into a DataFrame (like [`collect()`](api/polars.LazyFrame.collect.html#polars.LazyFrame.collect "polars.LazyFrame.collect")
) but, instead of returning a DataFrame directly, it is scheduled to be collected inside a thread pool, while this method returns almost instantly.

This can be useful if you use `gevent` or `asyncio` and want to release control to other greenlets/tasks while LazyFrames are being collected.

Parameters:

**gevent**

Return wrapper to `gevent.event.AsyncResult` instead of Awaitable

**type\_coercion**

Do type coercion optimization.

**predicate\_pushdown**

Do predicate pushdown optimization.

**projection\_pushdown**

Do projection pushdown optimization.

**simplify\_expression**

Run simplify expressions optimization.

**no\_optimization**

Turn off (certain) optimizations.

**slice\_pushdown**

Slice pushdown optimization.

**comm\_subplan\_elim**

Will try to cache branching subplans that occur on self-joins or unions.

**comm\_subexpr\_elim**

Common subexpressions will be cached and reused.

**cluster\_with\_columns**

Combine sequential independent calls to with\_columns

**collapse\_joins**

Collapse a join and filters into a faster join

**streaming**

Process the query in batches to handle larger-than-memory data. If set to `False` (default), the entire query is processed in a single batch.

Warning

Streaming mode is considered **unstable**. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.

Note

Use [`explain()`](api/polars.LazyFrame.explain.html#polars.LazyFrame.explain "polars.LazyFrame.explain")
 to see if Polars can process the query in streaming mode.

Returns:

If `gevent=False` (default) then returns an awaitable.

If `gevent=True` then returns wrapper that has a

`.get(block=True, timeout=None)` method.

See also

[`polars.collect_all`](../api/polars.collect_all.html#polars.collect_all "polars.collect_all")

Collect multiple LazyFrames at the same time.

[`polars.collect_all_async`](../api/polars.collect_all_async.html#polars.collect_all_async "polars.collect_all_async")

Collect multiple LazyFrames at the same time lazily.

Notes

In case of error `set_exception` is used on `asyncio.Future`/`gevent.event.AsyncResult` and will be reraised by them.

Examples

\>>> import asyncio
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \["a", "b", "a", "b", "b", "c"\],
...         "b": \[1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6\],
...         "c": \[6, 5, 4, 3, 2, 1\],
...     }
... )
\>>> async def main():
...     return await (
...         lf.group\_by("a", maintain\_order\=True)
...         .agg(pl.all().sum())
...         .collect\_async()
...     )
\>>> asyncio.run(main())
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 4   в”Ҷ 10  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 11  в”Ҷ 10  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

collect\_schema() вҶ’ Schema[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L2315-L2345)

Resolve the schema of this LazyFrame.

Examples

Determine the schema.

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6.0, 7.0, 8.0\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.collect\_schema()
Schema({'foo': Int64, 'bar': Float64, 'ham': String})

Access various properties of the schema.

\>>> schema \= lf.collect\_schema()
\>>> schema\["bar"\]
Float64
\>>> schema.names()
\['foo', 'bar', 'ham'\]
\>>> schema.dtypes()
\[Int64, Float64, String\]
\>>> schema.len()
3

_property_ columns_: [list](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#list "(in Python v3.13)")
\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
\]_[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L472-L512)

Get the column names.

Returns:

list of str

A list containing the name of each column in order.

Warning

Determining the column names of a LazyFrame requires resolving its schema, which is a potentially expensive operation. Using [`collect_schema()`](api/polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema.html#polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema "polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema")
 is the idiomatic way of resolving the schema. This property exists only for symmetry with the DataFrame class.

See also

[`collect_schema`](api/polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema.html#polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema "polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema")

`Schema.names`

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... ).select("foo", "bar")
\>>> lf.columns  
\['foo', 'bar'\]

count() вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L7565-L7584)

describe(

_percentiles: Sequence\[[float](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#float "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] | [float](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#float "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= (0.25, 0.5, 0.75)_,

_\*_,

_interpolation: RollingInterpolationMethod \= 'nearest'_,

) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L856-L1060)

Creates a summary of statistics for a LazyFrame, returning a DataFrame.

Parameters:

**percentiles**

One or more percentiles to include in the summary statistics. All values must be in the range `[0, 1]`.

**interpolation**{вҖҳnearestвҖҷ, вҖҳhigherвҖҷ, вҖҳlowerвҖҷ, вҖҳmidpointвҖҷ, вҖҳlinearвҖҷ}

Interpolation method used when calculating percentiles.

Returns:

DataFrame

Warning

*   This method does _not_ maintain the laziness of the frame, and will `collect` the final result. This could potentially be an expensive operation.
    
*   We do not guarantee the output of `describe` to be stable. It will show statistics that we deem informative, and may be updated in the future. Using `describe` programmatically (versus interactive exploration) is not recommended for this reason.
    

Notes

The median is included by default as the 50% percentile.

Examples

\>>> from datetime import date, time
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "float": \[1.0, 2.8, 3.0\],
...         "int": \[40, 50, None\],
...         "bool": \[True, False, True\],
...         "str": \["zz", "xx", "yy"\],
...         "date": \[date(2020, 1, 1), date(2021, 7, 5), date(2022, 12, 31)\],
...         "time": \[time(10, 20, 30), time(14, 45, 50), time(23, 15, 10)\],
...     }
... )

Show default frame statistics:

\>>> lf.describe()
shape: (9, 7)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ

Customize which percentiles are displayed, applying linear interpolation:

\>>> with pl.Config(tbl\_rows\=12):
...     lf.describe(
...         percentiles\=\[0.1, 0.3, 0.5, 0.7, 0.9\],
...         interpolation\="linear",
...     )
shape: (11, 7)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ statistic  в”Ҷ float    в”Ҷ int      в”Ҷ bool     в”Ҷ str  в”Ҷ date                в”Ҷ time     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---        в”Ҷ ---      в”Ҷ ---      в”Ҷ ---      в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---                 в”Ҷ ---      в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str        в”Ҷ f64      в”Ҷ f64      в”Ҷ f64      в”Ҷ str  в”Ҷ str                 в”Ҷ str      в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ count      в”Ҷ 3.0      в”Ҷ 2.0      в”Ҷ 3.0      в”Ҷ 3    в”Ҷ 3                   в”Ҷ 3        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null\_count в”Ҷ 0.0      в”Ҷ 1.0      в”Ҷ 0.0      в”Ҷ 0    в”Ҷ 0                   в”Ҷ 0        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ mean       в”Ҷ 2.266667 в”Ҷ 45.0     в”Ҷ 0.666667 в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ 2021-07-02 16:00:00 в”Ҷ 16:07:10 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ std        в”Ҷ 1.101514 в”Ҷ 7.071068 в”Ҷ null     в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null                в”Ҷ null     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ min        в”Ҷ 1.0      в”Ҷ 40.0     в”Ҷ 0.0      в”Ҷ xx   в”Ҷ 2020-01-01          в”Ҷ 10:20:30 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 10%        в”Ҷ 1.36     в”Ҷ 41.0     в”Ҷ null     в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ 2020-04-20          в”Ҷ 11:13:34 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 30%        в”Ҷ 2.08     в”Ҷ 43.0     в”Ҷ null     в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ 2020-11-26          в”Ҷ 12:59:42 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 50%        в”Ҷ 2.8      в”Ҷ 45.0     в”Ҷ null     в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ 2021-07-05          в”Ҷ 14:45:50 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 70%        в”Ҷ 2.88     в”Ҷ 47.0     в”Ҷ null     в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ 2022-02-07          в”Ҷ 18:09:34 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 90%        в”Ҷ 2.96     в”Ҷ 49.0     в”Ҷ null     в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ 2022-09-13          в”Ҷ 21:33:18 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ max        в”Ҷ 3.0      в”Ҷ 50.0     в”Ҷ 1.0      в”Ҷ zz   в”Ҷ 2022-12-31          в”Ҷ 23:15:10 в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

_classmethod_ deserialize(

_source: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Path | IOBase_,

_\*_,

_format: SerializationFormat \= 'binary'_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L408-L470)

Read a logical plan from a file to construct a LazyFrame.

Parameters:

**source**

Path to a file or a file-like object (by file-like object, we refer to objects that have a `read()` method, such as a file handler (e.g. via builtin `open` function) or `BytesIO`).

**format**

The format with which the LazyFrame was serialized. Options:

*   `"binary"`: Deserialize from binary format (bytes). This is the default.
    
*   `"json"`: Deserialize from JSON format (string).
    

Warning

This function uses [`pickle`](https://docs.python.org/3/library/pickle.html#module-pickle "(in Python v3.13)")
 if the logical plan contains Python UDFs, and as such inherits the security implications. Deserializing can execute arbitrary code, so it should only be attempted on trusted data.

See also

[`LazyFrame.serialize`](api/polars.LazyFrame.serialize.html#polars.LazyFrame.serialize "polars.LazyFrame.serialize")

Notes

Serialization is not stable across Polars versions: a LazyFrame serialized in one Polars version may not be deserializable in another Polars version.

Examples

\>>> import io
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame({"a": \[1, 2, 3\]}).sum()
\>>> bytes \= lf.serialize()
\>>> pl.LazyFrame.deserialize(io.BytesIO(bytes)).collect()
shape: (1, 1)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 6   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

drop(

_\*columns: ColumnNameOrSelector | Iterable\[ColumnNameOrSelector\]_,

_strict: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L5591-L5661)

Remove columns from the DataFrame.

Parameters:

**\*columns**

Names of the columns that should be removed from the dataframe. Accepts column selector input.

**strict**

Validate that all column names exist in the current schema, and throw an exception if any do not.

Examples

Drop a single column by passing the name of that column.

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6.0, 7.0, 8.0\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.drop("ham").collect()
shape: (3, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ f64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8.0 в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Drop multiple columns by passing a selector.

\>>> import polars.selectors as cs
\>>> lf.drop(cs.numeric()).collect()
shape: (3, 1)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Use positional arguments to drop multiple columns.

\>>> lf.drop("foo", "ham").collect()
shape: (3, 1)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ bar в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ f64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 6.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 7.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 8.0 в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

drop\_nans(

_subset: ColumnNameOrSelector | Collection\[ColumnNameOrSelector\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L6813-L6890)

Drop all rows that contain one or more NaN values.

The original order of the remaining rows is preserved.

Parameters:

**subset**

Column name(s) for which NaN values are considered; if set to `None` (default), use all columns (note that only floating-point columns can contain NaNs).

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[\-20.5, float("nan"), 80.0\],
...         "bar": \[float("nan"), 110.0, 25.5\],
...         "ham": \["xxx", "yyy", None\],
...     }
... )

The default behavior of this method is to drop rows where any single value in the row is NaN:

\>>> lf.drop\_nans().collect()
shape: (1, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ f64  в”Ҷ f64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 80.0 в”Ҷ 25.5 в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

This behaviour can be constrained to consider only a subset of columns, as defined by name, or with a selector. For example, dropping rows only if there is a NaN in the вҖңbarвҖқ column:

\>>> lf.drop\_nans(subset\=\["bar"\]).collect()
shape: (2, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar   в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ f64  в”Ҷ f64   в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ NaN  в”Ҷ 110.0 в”Ҷ yyy  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 80.0 в”Ҷ 25.5  в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Dropping a row only if _all_ values are NaN requires a different formulation:

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[float("nan"), float("nan"), float("nan"), float("nan")\],
...         "b": \[10.0, 2.5, float("nan"), 5.25\],
...         "c": \[65.75, float("nan"), float("nan"), 10.5\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.filter(~pl.all\_horizontal(pl.all().is\_nan())).collect()
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b    в”Ҷ c     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ f64 в”Ҷ f64  в”Ҷ f64   в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ NaN в”Ҷ 10.0 в”Ҷ 65.75 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ NaN в”Ҷ 2.5  в”Ҷ NaN   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ NaN в”Ҷ 5.25 в”Ҷ 10.5  в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

drop\_nulls(

_subset: ColumnNameOrSelector | Collection\[ColumnNameOrSelector\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L6892-L6969)

Drop all rows that contain one or more null values.

The original order of the remaining rows is preserved.

Parameters:

**subset**

Column name(s) for which null values are considered. If set to `None` (default), use all columns.

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6, None, 8\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", None\],
...     }
... )

The default behavior of this method is to drop rows where any single value in the row is null:

\>>> lf.drop\_nulls().collect()
shape: (1, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

This behaviour can be constrained to consider only a subset of columns, as defined by name or with a selector. For example, dropping rows if there is a null in any of the integer columns:

\>>> import polars.selectors as cs
\>>> lf.drop\_nulls(subset\=cs.integer()).collect()
shape: (2, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Dropping a row only if _all_ values are null requires a different formulation:

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[None, None, None, None\],
...         "b": \[1, 2, None, 1\],
...         "c": \[1, None, None, 1\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.filter(~pl.all\_horizontal(pl.all().is\_null())).collect()
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a    в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 1    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 2   в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 1    в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

_property_ dtypes_: [list](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#list "(in Python v3.13)")
\[[DataType](../api/polars.datatypes.DataType.html#polars.datatypes.DataType "polars.datatypes.DataType")\
\]_[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L514-L554)

Get the column data types.

Returns:

list of DataType

A list containing the data type of each column in order.

Warning

Determining the data types of a LazyFrame requires resolving its schema, which is a potentially expensive operation. Using [`collect_schema()`](api/polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema.html#polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema "polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema")
 is the idiomatic way to resolve the schema. This property exists only for symmetry with the DataFrame class.

See also

[`collect_schema`](api/polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema.html#polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema "polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema")

`Schema.dtypes`

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6.0, 7.0, 8.0\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.dtypes  
\[Int64, Float64, String\]

explain(

_\*_,

_format: ExplainFormat \= 'plain'_,

_optimized: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_type\_coercion: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_\_type\_check: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_predicate\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_projection\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_simplify\_expression: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_slice\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_comm\_subplan\_elim: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_comm\_subexpr\_elim: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_cluster\_with\_columns: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_collapse\_joins: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_streaming: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_tree\_format: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_\_check\_order: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

) вҶ’ [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L1062-L1177)

Create a string representation of the query plan.

Different optimizations can be turned on or off.

Parameters:

**format**{вҖҳplainвҖҷ, вҖҳtreeвҖҷ}

The format to use for displaying the logical plan.

**optimized**

Return an optimized query plan. Defaults to `True`. If this is set to `True` the subsequent optimization flags control which optimizations run.

**type\_coercion**

Do type coercion optimization.

**predicate\_pushdown**

Do predicate pushdown optimization.

**projection\_pushdown**

Do projection pushdown optimization.

**simplify\_expression**

Run simplify expressions optimization.

**slice\_pushdown**

Slice pushdown optimization.

**comm\_subplan\_elim**

Will try to cache branching subplans that occur on self-joins or unions.

**comm\_subexpr\_elim**

Common subexpressions will be cached and reused.

**cluster\_with\_columns**

Combine sequential independent calls to with\_columns

**collapse\_joins**

Collapse a join and filters into a faster join

**streaming**

Run parts of the query in a streaming fashion (this is in an alpha state)

Warning

Streaming mode is considered **unstable**. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.

**tree\_format**

Format the output as a tree.

Deprecated since version 0.20.30: Use `format="tree"` instead.

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \["a", "b", "a", "b", "b", "c"\],
...         "b": \[1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6\],
...         "c": \[6, 5, 4, 3, 2, 1\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.group\_by("a", maintain\_order\=True).agg(pl.all().sum()).sort(
...     "a"
... ).explain()  

explode(

_columns: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Expr | Sequence\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr\]_,

_\*more\_columns: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Expr_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L6680-L6722)

Explode the DataFrame to long format by exploding the given columns.

Parameters:

**columns**

Column names, expressions, or a selector defining them. The underlying columns being exploded must be of the `List` or `Array` data type.

**\*more\_columns**

Additional names of columns to explode, specified as positional arguments.

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "letters": \["a", "a", "b", "c"\],
...         "numbers": \[\[1\], \[2, 3\], \[4, 5\], \[6, 7, 8\]\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.explode("numbers").collect()
shape: (8, 2)

fetch(

 \= 500_,

 \= True_,

 \= True_,

 \= True_,

 \= True_,

 \= False_,

 \= True_,

 \= True_,

_comm\_subexpr\_elim: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_cluster\_with\_columns: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_collapse\_joins: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_streaming: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L3083-L3139)

Collect a small number of rows for debugging purposes.

Deprecated since version 1.0: Use [`collect()`](api/polars.LazyFrame.collect.html#polars.LazyFrame.collect "polars.LazyFrame.collect")
 instead, in conjunction with a call to [`head()`](../expressions/api/polars.head.html#polars.head "polars.head")
.\`

Warning

This is strictly a utility function that can help to debug queries using a smaller number of rows, and should _not_ be used in production code.

Notes

This is similar to a [`collect()`](api/polars.LazyFrame.collect.html#polars.LazyFrame.collect "polars.LazyFrame.collect")
 operation, but it overwrites the number of rows read by _every_ scan operation. Be aware that `fetch` does not guarantee the final number of rows in the DataFrame. Filters, join operations and fewer rows being available in the scanned data will all influence the final number of rows (joins are especially susceptible to this, and may return no data at all if `n_rows` is too small as the join keys may not be present).

fill\_nan(_value: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [float](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#float "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Expr | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
_) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L6376-L6417)

Fill floating point NaN values.

Parameters:

**value**

Value to fill the NaN values with.

Warning

Note that floating point NaNs (Not a Number) are not missing values. To replace missing values, use [`fill_null()`](api/polars.LazyFrame.fill_null.html#polars.LazyFrame.fill_null "polars.LazyFrame.fill_null")
.

See also

[`fill_null`](api/polars.LazyFrame.fill_null.html#polars.LazyFrame.fill_null "polars.LazyFrame.fill_null")

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[1.5, 2, float("nan"), 4\],
...         "b": \[0.5, 4, float("nan"), 13\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.fill\_nan(99).collect()
shape: (4, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a    в”Ҷ b    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ f64  в”Ҷ f64  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1.5  в”Ҷ 0.5  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2.0  в”Ҷ 4.0  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 99.0 в”Ҷ 99.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 4.0  в”Ҷ 13.0 в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

fill\_null(

_value: Any | Expr | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_strategy: FillNullStrategy | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_limit: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_\*_,

_matches\_supertype: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L6241-L6374)

Fill null values using the specified value or strategy.

Parameters:

**value**

Value used to fill null values.

**strategy**{None, вҖҳforwardвҖҷ, вҖҳbackwardвҖҷ, вҖҳminвҖҷ, вҖҳmaxвҖҷ, вҖҳmeanвҖҷ, вҖҳzeroвҖҷ, вҖҳoneвҖҷ}

Strategy used to fill null values.

**limit**

Number of consecutive null values to fill when using the вҖҳforwardвҖҷ or вҖҳbackwardвҖҷ strategy.

**matches\_supertype**

Fill all matching supertypes of the fill `value` literal.

See also

[`fill_nan`](api/polars.LazyFrame.fill_nan.html#polars.LazyFrame.fill_nan "polars.LazyFrame.fill_nan")

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[1, 2, None, 4\],
...         "b": \[0.5, 4, None, 13\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.fill\_null(99).collect()
shape: (4, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ f64  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 0.5  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 4.0  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 99  в”Ҷ 99.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 4   в”Ҷ 13.0 в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
\>>> lf.fill\_null(strategy\="forward").collect()

в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

filter(

_\*predicates: IntoExprColumn | Iterable\[IntoExprColumn\] | [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [list](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#list "(in Python v3.13)")
\[[bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] | np.ndarray\[Any, Any\]_,

_\*\*constraints: Any_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L3558-L3734)

Filter rows in the LazyFrame based on a predicate expression.

The original order of the remaining rows is preserved.

Rows where the filter predicate does not evaluate to True are discarded (this includes rows where the predicate evaluates as `null`).

Parameters:

**predicates**

Expression that evaluates to a boolean Series.

**constraints**

Column filters; use `name = value` to filter columns using the supplied value. Each constraint behaves the same as `pl.col(name).eq(value)`, and is implicitly joined with the other filter conditions using `&`.

See also

[`remove`](api/polars.LazyFrame.remove.html#polars.LazyFrame.remove "polars.LazyFrame.remove")

Notes

If you are transitioning from Pandas, and performing filter operations based on the comparison of two or more columns, please note that in Polars any comparison involving `null` values will result in a `null` result, _not_ boolean True or False. As a result, these rows will not be retained. Ensure that null values are handled appropriately to avoid unexpected behaviour (see examples below).

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3, None, 4, None, 0\],
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8, None, None, 9, 0\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c", None, "d", "e", "f"\],
...     }
... )

Filter on one condition:

\>>> lf.filter(pl.col("foo") \> 1).collect()
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7    в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8    в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 4   в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ d   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Filter on multiple conditions:

\>>> lf.filter((pl.col("foo") < 3) & (pl.col("ham") \== "a")).collect()
shape: (1, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Provide multiple filters using `*args` syntax:

\>>> lf.filter(
...     pl.col("foo") \== 1,
...     pl.col("ham") \== "a",
... ).collect()
shape: (1, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Provide multiple filters using `**kwargs` syntax:

\>>> lf.filter(foo\=1, ham\="a").collect()
shape: (1, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Filter on an OR condition:

\>>> lf.filter(
...     (pl.col("foo") \== 1) | (pl.col("ham") \== "c"),
... ).collect()
shape: (2, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Filter by comparing two columns against each other

\>>> lf.filter(
...     pl.col("foo") \== pl.col("bar"),
... ).collect()
shape: (1, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 0   в”Ҷ 0   в”Ҷ f   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

\>>> lf.filter(
...     pl.col("foo") != pl.col("bar"),
... ).collect()
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Notice how the row with `None` values is filtered out; using `ne_missing` ensures that null values compare equal, and we get similar behaviour to Pandas:

\>>> lf.filter(
...     pl.col("foo").ne\_missing(pl.col("bar")),
... ).collect()
shape: (5, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1    в”Ҷ 6    в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2    в”Ҷ 7    в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3    в”Ҷ 8    в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 4    в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ d   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 9    в”Ҷ e   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

first() вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L6019-L6041)

Get the first row of the DataFrame.

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[1, 3, 5\],
...         "b": \[2, 4, 6\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.first().collect()
shape: (1, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

gather\_every(_n: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
_, _offset: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= 0_) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L6199-L6239)

Take every nth row in the LazyFrame and return as a new LazyFrame.

Parameters:

**n**

Gather every _n_\-th row.

**offset**

Starting index.

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[1, 2, 3, 4\],
...         "b": \[5, 6, 7, 8\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.gather\_every(2).collect()

в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 5   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
\>>> lf.gather\_every(2, offset\=1).collect()

в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ

в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

group\_by(

_\*by: IntoExpr | Iterable\[IntoExpr\]_,

_maintain\_order: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_\*\*named\_by: IntoExpr_,

) вҶ’ LazyGroupBy[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L4029-L4135)

Start a group by operation.

Parameters:

**\*by**

Column(s) to group by. Accepts expression input. Strings are parsed as column names.

**maintain\_order**

Ensure that the order of the groups is consistent with the input data. This is slower than a default group by. Setting this to `True` blocks the possibility to run on the streaming engine.

**\*\*named\_by**

Additional columns to group by, specified as keyword arguments. The columns will be renamed to the keyword used.

Examples

Group by one column and call `agg` to compute the grouped sum of another column.

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \["a", "b", "a", "b", "c"\],
...         "b": \[1, 2, 1, 3, 3\],
...         "c": \[5, 4, 3, 2, 1\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.group\_by("a").agg(pl.col("b").sum()).collect()  
shape: (3, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 5   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Set `maintain_order=True` to ensure the order of the groups is consistent with the input.

\>>> lf.group\_by("a", maintain\_order\=True).agg(pl.col("c")).collect()
shape: (3, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ c         в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ ---       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ list\[i64\] в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ \[5, 3\]    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ \[4, 2\]    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ \[1\]       в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Group by multiple columns by passing a list of column names.

\>>> lf.group\_by(\["a", "b"\]).agg(pl.max("c")).collect()  
shape: (4, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 5   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Or use positional arguments to group by multiple columns in the same way. Expressions are also accepted.

\>>> lf.group\_by("a", pl.col("b") // 2).agg(
...     pl.col("c").mean()
... ).collect()  
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ f64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 0   в”Ҷ 4.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 3.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 1.0 в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

group\_by\_dynamic(

_index\_column: IntoExpr_,

_\*_,

_every: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | timedelta_,

_period: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | timedelta | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_offset: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | timedelta | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_include\_boundaries: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_closed: ClosedInterval \= 'left'_,

_label: Label \= 'left'_,

_group\_by: IntoExpr | Iterable\[IntoExpr\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_start\_by: StartBy \= 'window'_,

) вҶ’ LazyGroupBy[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L4273-L4606)

Group based on a time value (or index value of type Int32, Int64).

Time windows are calculated and rows are assigned to windows. Different from a normal group by is that a row can be member of multiple groups. By default, the windows look like:

*   \[start, start + period)\
    \
*   \[start + every, start + every + period)\
    \
*   \[start + 2\*every, start + 2\*every + period)\
    \
*   вҖҰ\
    \
\
where `start` is determined by `start_by`, `offset`, `every`, and the earliest datapoint. See the `start_by` argument description for details.\
\
Warning\
\
The index column must be sorted in ascending order. If `group_by` is passed, then the index column must be sorted in ascending order within each group.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**index\_column**\
\
Column used to group based on the time window. Often of type Date/Datetime. This column must be sorted in ascending order (or, if `group_by` is specified, then it must be sorted in ascending order within each group).\
\
In case of a dynamic group by on indices, dtype needs to be one of {Int32, Int64}. Note that Int32 gets temporarily cast to Int64, so if performance matters use an Int64 column.\
\
**every**\
\
interval of the window\
\
**period**\
\
length of the window, if None it will equal вҖҳeveryвҖҷ\
\
**offset**\
\
offset of the window, does not take effect if `start_by` is вҖҳdatapointвҖҷ. Defaults to zero.\
\
**include\_boundaries**\
\
Add the lower and upper bound of the window to the вҖң\_lower\_boundaryвҖқ and вҖң\_upper\_boundaryвҖқ columns. This will impact performance because itвҖҷs harder to parallelize\
\
**closed**{вҖҳleftвҖҷ, вҖҳrightвҖҷ, вҖҳbothвҖҷ, вҖҳnoneвҖҷ}\
\
Define which sides of the temporal interval are closed (inclusive).\
\
**label**{вҖҳleftвҖҷ, вҖҳrightвҖҷ, вҖҳdatapointвҖҷ}\
\
Define which label to use for the window:\
\
*   вҖҳleftвҖҷ: lower boundary of the window\
    \
*   вҖҳrightвҖҷ: upper boundary of the window\
    \
*   вҖҳdatapointвҖҷ: the first value of the index column in the given window. If you donвҖҷt need the label to be at one of the boundaries, choose this option for maximum performance\
    \
\
**group\_by**\
\
Also group by this column/these columns\
\
**start\_by**{вҖҳwindowвҖҷ, вҖҳdatapointвҖҷ, вҖҳmondayвҖҷ, вҖҳtuesdayвҖҷ, вҖҳwednesdayвҖҷ, вҖҳthursdayвҖҷ, вҖҳfridayвҖҷ, вҖҳsaturdayвҖҷ, вҖҳsundayвҖҷ}\
\
The strategy to determine the start of the first window by.\
\
*   вҖҳwindowвҖҷ: Start by taking the earliest timestamp, truncating it with `every`, and then adding `offset`. Note that weekly windows start on Monday.\
    \
*   вҖҳdatapointвҖҷ: Start from the first encountered data point.\
    \
*   a day of the week (only takes effect if `every` contains `'w'`):\
    \
    *   вҖҳmondayвҖҷ: Start the window on the Monday before the first data point.\
        \
    *   вҖҳtuesdayвҖҷ: Start the window on the Tuesday before the first data point.\
        \
    *   вҖҰ\
        \
    *   вҖҳsundayвҖҷ: Start the window on the Sunday before the first data point.\
        \
    \
    The resulting window is then shifted back until the earliest datapoint is in or in front of it.\
    \
\
Returns:\
\
LazyGroupBy\
\
Object you can call `.agg` on to aggregate by groups, the result of which will be sorted by `index_column` (but note that if `group_by` columns are passed, it will only be sorted within each group).\
\
See also\
\
[`rolling`](api/polars.LazyFrame.rolling.html#polars.LazyFrame.rolling "polars.LazyFrame.rolling")\
\
Notes\
\
1.  If youвҖҷre coming from pandas, then\
    \
    \# polars\
    df.group\_by\_dynamic("ts", every\="1d").agg(pl.col("value").sum())\
    \
    is equivalent to\
    \
    \# pandas\
    df.set\_index("ts").resample("D")\["value"\].sum().reset\_index()\
    \
    though note that, unlike pandas, polars doesnвҖҷt add extra rows for empty windows. If you need `index_column` to be evenly spaced, then please combine with [`DataFrame.upsample()`](../dataframe/api/polars.DataFrame.upsample.html#polars.DataFrame.upsample "polars.DataFrame.upsample")\
    .\
    \
2.  The `every`, `period` and `offset` arguments are created with the following string language:\
    \
    *   1ns (1 nanosecond)\
        \
    *   1us (1 microsecond)\
        \
    *   1ms (1 millisecond)\
        \
    *   1s (1 second)\
        \
    *   1m (1 minute)\
        \
    *   1h (1 hour)\
        \
    *   1d (1 calendar day)\
        \
    *   1w (1 calendar week)\
        \
    *   1mo (1 calendar month)\
        \
    *   1q (1 calendar quarter)\
        \
    *   1y (1 calendar year)\
        \
    *   1i (1 index count)\
        \
    \
    Or combine them: вҖң3d12h4m25sвҖқ # 3 days, 12 hours, 4 minutes, and 25 seconds\
    \
    By вҖңcalendar dayвҖқ, we mean the corresponding time on the next day (which may not be 24 hours, due to daylight savings). Similarly for вҖңcalendar weekвҖқ, вҖңcalendar monthвҖқ, вҖңcalendar quarterвҖқ, and вҖңcalendar yearвҖқ.\
    \
    In case of a group\_by\_dynamic on an integer column, the windows are defined by:\
    \
    *   вҖң1iвҖқ # length 1\
        \
    *   вҖң10iвҖқ # length 10\
        \
\
Examples\
\
\>>> from datetime import datetime\
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "time": pl.datetime\_range(\
...             start\=datetime(2021, 12, 16),\
...             end\=datetime(2021, 12, 16, 3),\
...             interval\="30m",\
...             eager\=True,\
...         ),\
...         "n": range(7),\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> lf.collect()\
shape: (7, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ time                в”Ҷ n   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---                 в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ 0   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 00:30:00 в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ 2   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 01:30:00 в”Ҷ 3   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 02:30:00 в”Ҷ 5   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 03:00:00 в”Ҷ 6   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Group by windows of 1 hour.\
\
\>>> lf.group\_by\_dynamic("time", every\="1h", closed\="right").agg(\
...     pl.col("n")\
... ).collect()\
shape: (4, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ time                в”Ҷ n         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---                 в”Ҷ ---       в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ list\[i64\] в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-15 23:00:00 в”Ҷ \[0\]       в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ \[1, 2\]    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ \[3, 4\]    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ \[5, 6\]    в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
The window boundaries can also be added to the aggregation result\
\
\>>> lf.group\_by\_dynamic(\
...     "time", every\="1h", include\_boundaries\=True, closed\="right"\
... ).agg(pl.col("n").mean()).collect()\
shape: (4, 4)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ \_lower\_boundary     в”Ҷ \_upper\_boundary     в”Ҷ time                в”Ҷ n   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---                 в”Ҷ ---                 в”Ҷ ---                 в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ f64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-15 23:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-15 23:00:00 в”Ҷ 0.0 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ 1.5 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ 3.5 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 03:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ 5.5 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
When closed=вҖқleftвҖқ, the window excludes the right end of interval: \[lower\_bound, upper\_bound)\
\
\>>> lf.group\_by\_dynamic("time", every\="1h", closed\="left").agg(\
...     pl.col("n")\
... ).collect()\
shape: (4, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ time                в”Ҷ n         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---                 в”Ҷ ---       в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ list\[i64\] в”Ӯ\

в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ \[0, 1\]    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ \[2, 3\]    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ \[4, 5\]    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 03:00:00 в”Ҷ \[6\]       в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
When closed=вҖқbothвҖқ the time values at the window boundaries belong to 2 groups.\
\
\>>> lf.group\_by\_dynamic("time", every\="1h", closed\="both").agg(\
...     pl.col("n")\
... ).collect()\
shape: (4, 2)\

Dynamic group bys can also be combined with grouping on normal keys\
\
\>>> lf \= lf.with\_columns(groups\=pl.Series(\["a", "a", "a", "b", "b", "a", "a"\]))\
\>>> lf.collect()\
shape: (7, 3)\

Dynamic group by on an index column\
\
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "idx": pl.int\_range(0, 6, eager\=True),\
...         "A": \["A", "A", "B", "B", "B", "C"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> lf.group\_by\_dynamic(\
...     "idx",\
...     every\="2i",\
...     period\="3i",\
...     include\_boundaries\=True,\
...     closed\="right",\
... ).agg(pl.col("A").alias("A\_agg\_list")).collect()\
shape: (4, 4)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\

\
Inspect a node in the computation graph.\
\
Print the value that this node in the computation graph evaluates to and pass on the value.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame({"foo": \[1, 1, \-2, 3\]})\
\>>> (\
...     lf.with\_columns(pl.col("foo").cum\_sum().alias("bar"))\
...     .inspect()  \# print the node before the filter\
...     .filter(pl.col("bar") \== pl.col("foo"))\
... )  \

Parameters:\
\
**other**\
\
Lazy DataFrame to join with.\
\
**on**\
\
Name(s) of the join columns in both DataFrames. If set, `left_on` and `right_on` should be None. This should not be specified if `how="cross"`.\
\
**how**{вҖҳinnerвҖҷ, вҖҳleftвҖҷ, вҖҳrightвҖҷ, вҖҳfullвҖҷ, вҖҳsemiвҖҷ, вҖҳantiвҖҷ, вҖҳcrossвҖҷ}\
\
Join strategy.\
\
*   _inner_\
    \
    Returns rows that have matching values in both tables\
    \
*   _left_\
    \
    Returns all rows from the left table, and the matched rows from the right table\
    \
*   _right_\
    \
    Returns all rows from the right table, and the matched rows from the left table\
    \
*   _full_\
    \
    Returns all rows when there is a match in either left or right table\
    \
*   _cross_\
    \
    Returns the Cartesian product of rows from both tables\
    \
*   _semi_\
    \
    Returns rows from the left table that have a match in the right table.\
    \
*   _anti_\
    \
    Returns rows from the left table that have no match in the right table.\
    \
\
**left\_on**\
\
Join column of the left DataFrame.\
\
**right\_on**\
\
Join column of the right DataFrame.\
\
**suffix**\
\
Suffix to append to columns with a duplicate name.\
\
**validate: {вҖҳm:mвҖҷ, вҖҳm:1вҖҷ, вҖҳ1:mвҖҷ, вҖҳ1:1вҖҷ}**\
\
Checks if join is of specified type.\
\
> *   _many\_to\_many_\
>     \
>     вҖңm:mвҖқ: default, does not result in checks\
>     \
> *   _one\_to\_one_\
>     \
>     вҖң1:1вҖқ: check if join keys are unique in both left and right datasets\
>     \
> *   _one\_to\_many_\
>     \
>     вҖң1:mвҖқ: check if join keys are unique in left dataset\
>     \
> *   _many\_to\_one_\
>     \
>     вҖңm:1вҖқ: check if join keys are unique in right dataset\
>     \
\
Note\
\
This is currently not supported by the streaming engine.\
\
**nulls\_equal**\
\
Join on null values. By default null values will never produce matches.\
\
**coalesce**\
\
Coalescing behavior (merging of join columns).\
\
*   None: -> join specific.\
    \
*   True: -> Always coalesce join columns.\
    \
*   False: -> Never coalesce join columns.\
    \
\
Note\
\
Joining on any other expressions than `col` will turn off coalescing.\
\
**maintain\_order**{вҖҳnoneвҖҷ, вҖҳleftвҖҷ, вҖҳrightвҖҷ, вҖҳleft\_rightвҖҷ, вҖҳright\_leftвҖҷ}\
\
Which DataFrame row order to preserve, if any. Do not rely on any observed ordering without explicitly setting this parameter, as your code may break in a future release. Not specifying any ordering can improve performance Supported for inner, left, right and full joins\
\
*   _none_\
    \
    No specific ordering is desired. The ordering might differ across Polars versions or even between different runs.\
    \
*   _left_\
    \
    Preserves the order of the left DataFrame.\
    \
*   _right_\
    \
    Preserves the order of the right DataFrame.\
    \
*   _left\_right_\
    \
    First preserves the order of the left DataFrame, then the right.\
    \
*   _right\_left_\
    \
    First preserves the order of the right DataFrame, then the left.\
    \
\
**allow\_parallel**\
\
Allow the physical plan to optionally evaluate the computation of both DataFrames up to the join in parallel.\
\
**force\_parallel**\
\
Force the physical plan to evaluate the computation of both DataFrames up to the join in parallel.\
\
See also\
\
[`join_asof`](api/polars.LazyFrame.join_asof.html#polars.LazyFrame.join_asof "polars.LazyFrame.join_asof")\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],\
...         "bar": \[6.0, 7.0, 8.0\],\
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> other\_lf \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "apple": \["x", "y", "z"\],\
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "d"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> lf.join(other\_lf, on\="ham").collect()\
shape: (2, 4)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ҷ apple в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ ---   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ f64 в”Ҷ str в”Ҷ str   в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ҷ a   в”Ҷ x     в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7.0 в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ y     в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> lf.join(other\_lf, on\="ham", how\="full").collect()\
shape: (4, 5)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ҷ apple в”Ҷ ham\_right в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---       в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ f64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ҷ str   в”Ҷ str       в”Ӯ\

в”Ӯ 1    в”Ҷ 6.0  в”Ҷ a    в”Ҷ x     в”Ҷ a         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2    в”Ҷ 7.0  в”Ҷ b    в”Ҷ y     в”Ҷ b         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ z     в”Ҷ d         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 3    в”Ҷ 8.0  в”Ҷ c    в”Ҷ null  в”Ҷ null      в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> lf.join(other\_lf, on\="ham", how\="left", coalesce\=True).collect()\
shape: (3, 4)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\

в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ҷ a   в”Ҷ x     в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7.0 в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ y     в”Ӯ\

в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ f64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7.0 в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> lf.join(other\_lf, on\="ham", how\="anti").collect()\

в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ\

\

в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ f64 в”Ҷ str в”Ҷ str   в”Ҷ str       в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
