в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ҷ a   в”Ҷ y     в”Ҷ b         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ҷ a   в”Ҷ z     в”Ҷ d         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7.0 в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ x     в”Ҷ a         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7.0 в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ y     в”Ҷ b         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7.0 в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ z     в”Ҷ d         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8.0 в”Ҷ c   в”Ҷ x     в”Ҷ a         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8.0 в”Ҷ c   в”Ҷ y     в”Ҷ b         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8.0 в”Ҷ c   в”Ҷ z     в”Ҷ d         в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
join\_asof(\
\
_other: LazyFrame_,\
\
_\*_,\
\
_left\_on: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr \= None_,\
\
_right\_on: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr \= None_,\
\
_on: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr \= None_,\
\
_by\_left: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Sequence\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_by\_right: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Sequence\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_by: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Sequence\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_strategy: AsofJoinStrategy \= 'backward'_,\
\
_suffix: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= '\_right'_,\
\
_tolerance: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [float](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#float "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | timedelta | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_allow\_parallel: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_force\_parallel: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= False_,\
\
_coalesce: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_allow\_exact\_matches: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_check\_sortedness: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L4608-L4979)\
\
Perform an asof join.\
\
This is similar to a left-join except that we match on nearest key rather than equal keys.\
\
Both DataFrames must be sorted by the `on` key (within each `by` group, if specified).\
\
For each row in the left DataFrame:\
\
> *   A вҖңbackwardвҖқ search selects the last row in the right DataFrame whose вҖҳonвҖҷ key is less than or equal to the leftвҖҷs key.\
>     \
> *   A вҖңforwardвҖқ search selects the first row in the right DataFrame whose вҖҳonвҖҷ key is greater than or equal to the leftвҖҷs key.\
>     \
>     A вҖңnearestвҖқ search selects the last row in the right DataFrame whose value is nearest to the leftвҖҷs key. String keys are not currently supported for a nearest search.\
>     \
\
The default is вҖңbackwardвҖқ.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**other**\
\
Lazy DataFrame to join with.\
\
**left\_on**\
\
Join column of the left DataFrame.\
\
**right\_on**\
\
Join column of the right DataFrame.\
\
**on**\
\
Join column of both DataFrames. If set, `left_on` and `right_on` should be None.\
\
**by**\
\
Join on these columns before doing asof join.\
\
**by\_left**\
\
Join on these columns before doing asof join.\
\
**by\_right**\
\
Join on these columns before doing asof join.\
\
**strategy**{вҖҳbackwardвҖҷ, вҖҳforwardвҖҷ, вҖҳnearestвҖҷ}\
\
Join strategy.\
\
**suffix**\
\
Suffix to append to columns with a duplicate name.\
\
**tolerance**\
\
Numeric tolerance. By setting this the join will only be done if the near keys are within this distance. If an asof join is done on columns of dtype вҖңDateвҖқ, вҖңDatetimeвҖқ, вҖңDurationвҖқ or вҖңTimeвҖқ, use either a datetime.timedelta object or the following string language:\
\
> *   1ns (1 nanosecond)\
>     \
> *   1us (1 microsecond)\
>     \
> *   1ms (1 millisecond)\
>     \
> *   1s (1 second)\
>     \
> *   1m (1 minute)\
>     \
> *   1h (1 hour)\
>     \
> *   1d (1 calendar day)\
>     \
> *   1w (1 calendar week)\
>     \
> *   1mo (1 calendar month)\
>     \
> *   1q (1 calendar quarter)\
>     \
> *   1y (1 calendar year)\
>     \
> \
> Or combine them: вҖң3d12h4m25sвҖқ # 3 days, 12 hours, 4 minutes, and 25 seconds\
> \
> By вҖңcalendar dayвҖқ, we mean the corresponding time on the next day (which may not be 24 hours, due to daylight savings). Similarly for вҖңcalendar weekвҖқ, вҖңcalendar monthвҖқ, вҖңcalendar quarterвҖқ, and вҖңcalendar yearвҖқ.\
\
**allow\_parallel**\
\
Allow the physical plan to optionally evaluate the computation of both DataFrames up to the join in parallel.\
\
**force\_parallel**\
\
Force the physical plan to evaluate the computation of both DataFrames up to the join in parallel.\
\
**coalesce**\
\
Coalescing behavior (merging of `on` / `left_on` / `right_on` columns):\
\
*   True: -> Always coalesce join columns.\
    \
*   False: -> Never coalesce join columns.\
    \
\
Note that joining on any other expressions than `col` will turn off coalescing.\
\
**allow\_exact\_matches**\
\
Whether exact matches are valid join predicates.\
\
*   If True, allow matching with the same `on` value\
    \
    (i.e. less-than-or-equal-to / greater-than-or-equal-to)\
    \
*   If False, donвҖҷt match the same `on` value\
    \
    (i.e., strictly less-than / strictly greater-than).\
    \
\
**check\_sortedness**\
\
Check the sortedness of the asof keys. If the keys are not sorted Polars will error, or in case of вҖҳbyвҖҷ argument raise a warning. This might become a hard error in the future.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> from datetime import date\
\>>> gdp \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "date": pl.date\_range(\
...             date(2016, 1, 1),\
...             date(2020, 1, 1),\
...             "1y",\
...             eager\=True,\
...         ),\
...         "gdp": \[4164, 4411, 4566, 4696, 4827\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> gdp.collect()\
shape: (5, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ gdp  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---        в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2016-01-01 в”Ҷ 4164 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2017-01-01 в”Ҷ 4411 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2018-01-01 в”Ҷ 4566 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2020-01-01 в”Ҷ 4827 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
\>>> population \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "date": \[date(2016, 3, 1), date(2018, 8, 1), date(2019, 1, 1)\],\
...         "population": \[82.19, 82.66, 83.12\],\
...     }\
... ).sort("date")\
\>>> population.collect()\
shape: (3, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ population в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ f64        в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 82.19      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 82.66      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 83.12      в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Note how the dates donвҖҷt quite match. If we join them using `join_asof` and `strategy='backward'`, then each date from `population` which doesnвҖҷt have an exact match is matched with the closest earlier date from `gdp`:\
\
\>>> population.join\_asof(gdp, on\="date", strategy\="backward").collect()\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ population в”Ҷ gdp  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ f64        в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 82.19      в”Ҷ 4164 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 82.66      в”Ҷ 4566 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 83.12      в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Note how:\
\
*   date `2016-03-01` from `population` is matched with `2016-01-01` from `gdp`;\
    \
*   date `2018-08-01` from `population` is matched with `2018-01-01` from `gdp`.\
    \
\
You can verify this by passing `coalesce=False`:\
\
\>>> population.join\_asof(\
...     gdp, on\="date", strategy\="backward", coalesce\=False\
... ).collect()\
shape: (3, 4)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ population в”Ҷ date\_right в”Ҷ gdp  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ f64        в”Ҷ date       в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 82.19      в”Ҷ 2016-01-01 в”Ҷ 4164 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 82.66      в”Ҷ 2018-01-01 в”Ҷ 4566 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 83.12      в”Ҷ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
If we instead use `strategy='forward'`, then each date from `population` which doesnвҖҷt have an exact match is matched with the closest later date from `gdp`:\
\
\>>> population.join\_asof(gdp, on\="date", strategy\="forward").collect()\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ population в”Ҷ gdp  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ f64        в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 82.19      в”Ҷ 4411 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 82.66      в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 83.12      в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Note how:\
\
*   date `2016-03-01` from `population` is matched with `2017-01-01` from `gdp`;\
    \
*   date `2018-08-01` from `population` is matched with `2019-01-01` from `gdp`.\
    \
\
Finally, `strategy='nearest'` gives us a mix of the two results above, as each date from `population` which doesnвҖҷt have an exact match is matched with the closest date from `gdp`, regardless of whether itвҖҷs earlier or later:\
\
\>>> population.join\_asof(gdp, on\="date", strategy\="nearest").collect()\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ population в”Ҷ gdp  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ f64        в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 82.19      в”Ҷ 4164 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 82.66      в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 83.12      в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Note how:\
\
*   date `2016-03-01` from `population` is matched with `2016-01-01` from `gdp`;\
    \
*   date `2018-08-01` from `population` is matched with `2019-01-01` from `gdp`.\
    \
\
They `by` argument allows joining on another column first, before the asof join. In this example we join by `country` first, then asof join by date, as above.\
\
\>>> gdp\_dates \= pl.date\_range(  \# fmt: skip\
...     date(2016, 1, 1), date(2020, 1, 1), "1y", eager\=True\
... )\
\>>> gdp2 \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "country": \["Germany"\] \* 5 + \["Netherlands"\] \* 5,\
...         "date": pl.concat(\[gdp\_dates, gdp\_dates\]),\
...         "gdp": \[4164, 4411, 4566, 4696, 4827, 784, 833, 914, 910, 909\],\
...     }\
... ).sort("country", "date")\
\>>>\
\>>> gdp2.collect()\
shape: (10, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ country     в”Ҷ date       в”Ҷ gdp  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---         в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str         в”Ҷ date       в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2016-01-01 в”Ҷ 4164 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2017-01-01 в”Ҷ 4411 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2018-01-01 в”Ҷ 4566 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2020-01-01 в”Ҷ 4827 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2016-01-01 в”Ҷ 784  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2017-01-01 в”Ҷ 833  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2018-01-01 в”Ҷ 914  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 910  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2020-01-01 в”Ҷ 909  в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> pop2 \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "country": \["Germany"\] \* 3 + \["Netherlands"\] \* 3,\
...         "date": \[\
...             date(2016, 3, 1),\
...             date(2018, 8, 1),\
...             date(2019, 1, 1),\
...             date(2016, 3, 1),\
...             date(2018, 8, 1),\
...             date(2019, 1, 1),\
...         \],\
...         "population": \[82.19, 82.66, 83.12, 17.11, 17.32, 17.40\],\
...     }\
... ).sort("country", "date")\
\>>>\
\>>> pop2.collect()\
shape: (6, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ country     в”Ҷ date       в”Ҷ population в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---         в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str         в”Ҷ date       в”Ҷ f64        в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 82.19      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 82.66      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 83.12      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 17.11      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 17.32      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 17.4       в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> pop2.join\_asof(gdp2, by\="country", on\="date", strategy\="nearest").collect()\
shape: (6, 4)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ country     в”Ҷ date       в”Ҷ population в”Ҷ gdp  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---         в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str         в”Ҷ date       в”Ҷ f64        в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 82.19      в”Ҷ 4164 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 82.66      в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 83.12      в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 17.11      в”Ҷ 784  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 17.32      в”Ҷ 910  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 17.4       в”Ҷ 910  в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
join\_where(\
\
_other: LazyFrame_,\
\
_\*predicates: Expr | Iterable\[Expr\]_,\
\
_suffix: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= '\_right'_,\
\
) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L5252-L5332)\
\
Perform a join based on one or multiple (in)equality predicates.\
\
This performs an inner join, so only rows where all predicates are true are included in the result, and a row from either DataFrame may be included multiple times in the result.\
\
Note\
\
The row order of the input DataFrames is not preserved.\
\
Warning\
\
This functionality is experimental. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**other**\
\
DataFrame to join with.\
\
**\*predicates**\
\
(In)Equality condition to join the two tables on. When a column name occurs in both tables, the proper suffix must be applied in the predicate.\
\
**suffix**\
\
Suffix to append to columns with a duplicate name.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> east \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "id": \[100, 101, 102\],\
...         "dur": \[120, 140, 160\],\
...         "rev": \[12, 14, 16\],\
...         "cores": \[2, 8, 4\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> west \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "t\_id": \[404, 498, 676, 742\],\
...         "time": \[90, 130, 150, 170\],\
...         "cost": \[9, 13, 15, 16\],\
...         "cores": \[4, 2, 1, 4\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> east.join\_where(\
...     west,\
...     pl.col("dur") < pl.col("time"),\
...     pl.col("rev") < pl.col("cost"),\
... ).collect()\
shape: (5, 8)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ id  в”Ҷ dur в”Ҷ rev в”Ҷ cores в”Ҷ t\_id в”Ҷ time в”Ҷ cost в”Ҷ cores\_right в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64   в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ i64         в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 100 в”Ҷ 120 в”Ҷ 12  в”Ҷ 2     в”Ҷ 498  в”Ҷ 130  в”Ҷ 13   в”Ҷ 2           в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 100 в”Ҷ 120 в”Ҷ 12  в”Ҷ 2     в”Ҷ 676  в”Ҷ 150  в”Ҷ 15   в”Ҷ 1           в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 100 в”Ҷ 120 в”Ҷ 12  в”Ҷ 2     в”Ҷ 742  в”Ҷ 170  в”Ҷ 16   в”Ҷ 4           в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 101 в”Ҷ 140 в”Ҷ 14  в”Ҷ 8     в”Ҷ 676  в”Ҷ 150  в”Ҷ 15   в”Ҷ 1           в”Ӯ\

...     }\
... )\

\
map\_batches(\
\
_function: Callable\[\[DataFrame\], DataFrame\]_,\
\
_\*_,\
\
_predicate\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_projection\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_slice\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_no\_optimizations: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= False_,\
\
_schema: [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | SchemaDict \= None_,\
\
_validate\_output\_schema: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_streamable: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= False_,\
\
) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L7047-L7143)\
\
Apply a custom function.\
\
It is important that the function returns a Polars DataFrame.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**function**\
\
Lambda/ function to apply.\
\
**predicate\_pushdown**\
\
Allow predicate pushdown optimization to pass this node.\
\
**projection\_pushdown**\
\
Allow projection pushdown optimization to pass this node.\
\
**slice\_pushdown**\
\
Allow slice pushdown optimization to pass this node.\
\
**no\_optimizations**\
\
Turn off all optimizations past this point.\
\
**schema**\
\
Output schema of the function, if set to `None` we assume that the schema will remain unchanged by the applied function.\
\
**validate\_output\_schema**\
\
It is paramount that polarsвҖҷ schema is correct. This flag will ensure that the output schema of this function will be checked with the expected schema. Setting this to `False` will not do this check, but may lead to hard to debug bugs.\
\
**streamable**\
\
Whether the function that is given is eligible to be running with the streaming engine. That means that the function must produce the same result when it is executed in batches or when it is be executed on the full dataset.\
\
Warning\
\
The `schema` of a `LazyFrame` must always be correct. It is up to the caller of this function to ensure that this invariant is upheld.\
\
It is important that the optimization flags are correct. If the custom function for instance does an aggregation of a column, `predicate_pushdown` should not be allowed, as this prunes rows and will influence your aggregation results.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> lf \= (  \
...     pl.LazyFrame(\
...         {\
...             "a": pl.int\_range(\-100\_000, 0, eager\=True),\
...             "b": pl.int\_range(0, 100\_000, eager\=True),\
...         }\
...     )\
...     .map\_batches(lambda x: 2 \* x, streamable\=True)\
...     .collect(streaming\=True)\
... )\
shape: (100\_000, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ a       в”Ҷ b      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---     в”Ҷ ---    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64     в”Ҷ i64    в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ -200000 в”Ҷ 0      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ -199998 в”Ҷ 2      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ -199996 в”Ҷ 4      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ -199994 в”Ҷ 6      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ вҖҰ       в”Ҷ вҖҰ      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ -8      в”Ҷ 199992 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ -6      в”Ҷ 199994 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ -4      в”Ҷ 199996 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ -2      в”Ҷ 199998 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\

melt(\
\
_id\_vars: ColumnNameOrSelector | Sequence\[ColumnNameOrSelector\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_value\_vars: ColumnNameOrSelector | Sequence\[ColumnNameOrSelector\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_variable\_name: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_value\_name: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_\*_,\
\
_streamable: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L7586-L7634)\
\
Unpivot a DataFrame from wide to long format.\
\
Optionally leaves identifiers set.\
\
This function is useful to massage a DataFrame into a format where one or more columns are identifier variables (id\_vars) while all other columns, considered measured variables (value\_vars), are вҖңunpivotedвҖқ to the row axis leaving just two non-identifier columns, вҖҳvariableвҖҷ and вҖҳvalueвҖҷ.\
\
Deprecated since version 1.0.0: Please use [`unpivot()`](api/polars.LazyFrame.unpivot.html#polars.LazyFrame.unpivot "polars.LazyFrame.unpivot")\
 instead.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**id\_vars**\
\
Column(s) or selector(s) to use as identifier variables.\
\
**value\_vars**\
\
Column(s) or selector(s) to use as values variables; if `value_vars` is empty all columns that are not in `id_vars` will be used.\
\
**variable\_name**\
\
Name to give to the `variable` column. Defaults to вҖңvariableвҖқ\
\
**value\_name**\
\
Name to give to the `value` column. Defaults to вҖңvalueвҖқ\
\
**streamable**\
\
Allow this node to run in the streaming engine. If this runs in streaming, the output of the unpivot operation will not have a stable ordering.\
\
merge\_sorted(\
\
_other: LazyFrame_,\
\
_key: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
_,\
\
) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L7227-L7299)\
\
Take two sorted DataFrames and merge them by the sorted key.\
\
The output of this operation will also be sorted. It is the callers responsibility that the frames are sorted in ascending order by that key otherwise the output will not make sense.\
\
The schemas of both LazyFrames must be equal.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**other**\
\
Other DataFrame that must be merged\
\
**key**\
\
Key that is sorted.\
\
Notes\
\
No guarantee is given over the output row order when the key is equal between the both dataframes.\
\
The key must be sorted in ascending order.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df0 \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {"name": \["steve", "elise", "bob"\], "age": \[42, 44, 18\]}\
... ).sort("age")\
\>>> df0.collect()\
shape: (3, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ name  в”Ҷ age в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---   в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str   в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ bob   в”Ҷ 18  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ steve в”Ҷ 42  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ elise в”Ҷ 44  в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> df1 \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {"name": \["anna", "megan", "steve", "thomas"\], "age": \[21, 33, 42, 20\]}\
... ).sort("age")\
\>>> df1.collect()\
shape: (4, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ name   в”Ҷ age в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---    в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str    в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ thomas в”Ҷ 20  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ anna   в”Ҷ 21  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ megan  в”Ҷ 33  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ steve  в”Ҷ 42  в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> df0.merge\_sorted(df1, key\="age").collect()\

в”Ӯ str    в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\

в”Ӯ anna   в”Ҷ 21  в”Ӯ\

pipe(\
\
_function: Callable\[Concatenate\[LazyFrame, P\], T\]_,\
\
_\*args: P.args_,\
\
_\*\*kwargs: P.kwargs_,\
\
) вҶ’ T[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L785-L854)\
\
Offers a structured way to apply a sequence of user-defined functions (UDFs).\
\
Parameters:\
\
**function**\
\
Callable; will receive the frame as the first parameter, followed by any given args/kwargs.\
\
**\*args**\
\
Arguments to pass to the UDF.\
\
**\*\*kwargs**\
\
Keyword arguments to pass to the UDF.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> def cast\_str\_to\_int(lf: pl.LazyFrame, col\_name: str) \-> pl.LazyFrame:\
...     return lf.with\_columns(pl.col(col\_name).cast(pl.Int64))\
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "a": \[1, 2, 3, 4\],\
...         "b": \["10", "20", "30", "40"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> lf.pipe(cast\_str\_to\_int, col\_name\="b").collect()\
shape: (4, 2)\

в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\

profile(\
\
_\*_,\
\
_type\_coercion: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_\_type\_check: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_predicate\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_projection\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_simplify\_expression: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_no\_optimization: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= False_,\
\
_slice\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_comm\_subplan\_elim: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_comm\_subexpr\_elim: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_cluster\_with\_columns: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_collapse\_joins: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_show\_plot: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= False_,\
\
_truncate\_nodes: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= 0_,\
\
_figsize: [tuple](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#tuple "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[[int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
, [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] \= (18, 8)_,\
\
_streaming: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= False_,\
\
_engine: EngineType \= 'cpu'_,\
\
_\_check\_order: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_\*\*\_kwargs: Any_,\
\
) вҶ’ [tuple](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#tuple "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[DataFrame, DataFrame\][\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L1659-L1857)\
\
Profile a LazyFrame.\
\
This will run the query and return a tuple containing the materialized DataFrame and a DataFrame that contains profiling information of each node that is executed.\
\
The units of the timings are microseconds.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**type\_coercion**\
\
Do type coercion optimization.\
\
**predicate\_pushdown**\
\
Do predicate pushdown optimization.\
\
**projection\_pushdown**\
\
Do projection pushdown optimization.\
\
**simplify\_expression**\
\
Run simplify expressions optimization.\
\
**no\_optimization**\
\
Turn off (certain) optimizations.\
\
**slice\_pushdown**\
\
Slice pushdown optimization.\
\
**comm\_subplan\_elim**\
\
Will try to cache branching subplans that occur on self-joins or unions.\
\
**comm\_subexpr\_elim**\
\
Common subexpressions will be cached and reused.\
\
**cluster\_with\_columns**\
\
Combine sequential independent calls to with\_columns\
\
**collapse\_joins**\
\
Collapse a join and filters into a faster join\
\
**show\_plot**\
\
Show a gantt chart of the profiling result\
\
**truncate\_nodes**\
\
Truncate the label lengths in the gantt chart to this number of characters.\
\
**figsize**\
\
matplotlib figsize of the profiling plot\
\
**streaming**\
\
Run parts of the query in a streaming fashion (this is in an alpha state)\
\
**engine**\
\
Select the engine used to process the query, optional. If set to `"cpu"` (default), the query is run using the polars CPU engine. If set to `"gpu"`, the GPU engine is used. Fine-grained control over the GPU engine, for example which device to use on a system with multiple devices, is possible by providing a [`GPUEngine`](api/polars.lazyframe.engine_config.GPUEngine.html#polars.lazyframe.engine_config.GPUEngine "polars.lazyframe.engine_config.GPUEngine")\
 object with configuration options.\
\
Note\
\
GPU mode is considered **unstable**. Not all queries will run successfully on the GPU, however, they should fall back transparently to the default engine if execution is not supported.\
\
Running with `POLARS_VERBOSE=1` will provide information if a query falls back (and why).\
\
Note\
\
The GPU engine does not support streaming, if streaming is enabled then GPU execution is switched off.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "a": \["a", "b", "a", "b", "b", "c"\],\
...         "b": \[1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6\],\
...         "c": \[6, 5, 4, 3, 2, 1\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> lf.group\_by("a", maintain\_order\=True).agg(pl.all().sum()).sort(\
...     "a"\
... ).profile()  \
(shape: (3, 3)\
 в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
 в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ\
 в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\

 в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
 в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 4   в”Ҷ 10  в”Ӯ\
 в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 11  в”Ҷ 10  в”Ӯ\
 в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ\
 в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ,\
 shape: (3, 3)\
 в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
 в”Ӯ node                    в”Ҷ start в”Ҷ end  в”Ӯ\

quantile(\
\
_quantile: [float](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#float "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr_,\
\
_interpolation: RollingInterpolationMethod \= 'nearest'_,\
\
) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L6644-L6678)\
\
Aggregate the columns in the LazyFrame to their quantile value.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**quantile**\
\
Quantile between 0.0 and 1.0.\
\
**interpolation**{вҖҳnearestвҖҷ, вҖҳhigherвҖҷ, вҖҳlowerвҖҷ, вҖҳmidpointвҖҷ, вҖҳlinearвҖҷ}\
\
Interpolation method.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "a": \[1, 2, 3, 4\],\

в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\

remote(\
\
_context: pc.ComputeContext | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_plan\_type: pc.\_typing.PlanTypePreference \= 'dot'_,\
\
) вҶ’ pc.LazyFrameExt[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L7636-L7694)\
\
Run a query remotely on Polars Cloud.\
\
This allows you to run Polars remotely on one or more workers via several strategies for distributed compute.\
\
Read more in the [Announcement post](https://pola.rs/posts/polars-cloud-what-we-are-building/)\
\
Parameters:\
\
**context**\
\
Compute context in which queries are executed. If none given, it will take the default context.\
\
**plan\_type**\
\
Whether to give a dot diagram of a plain text version of logical plan.\
\
Examples\
\
Run a query on a cloud instance.\
\
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(\[1, 2, 3\]).sum()\
\>>> in\_progress \= lf.remote().collect()  \
\>>> \# do some other work\
\>>> in\_progress.await\_result()  \
shape: (1, 1)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ column\_0 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64      в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 6        в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Run a query distributed.\
\
\>>> lf \= (\
...     pl.scan\_parquet("s3://my\_bucket/").group\_by("key").agg(pl.sum("values"))\
... )\
\>>> in\_progress \= lf.remote().distributed().collect()  \
\>>> in\_progress.await\_result()  \
shape: (1, 1)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ column\_0 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64      в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 6        в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
remove(\
\
_\*predicates: IntoExprColumn | Iterable\[IntoExprColumn\] | [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [list](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#list "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[[bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] | np.ndarray\[Any, Any\]_,\
\
_\*\*constraints: Any_,\
\
) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L3736-L3888)\
\
Remove rows, dropping those that match the given predicate expression(s).\
\
The original order of the remaining rows is preserved.\
\
Rows where the filter predicate does not evaluate to True are retained (this includes rows where the predicate evaluates as `null`).\
\
Parameters:\
\
**predicates**\
\
Expression that evaluates to a boolean Series.\
\
**constraints**\
\
Column filters; use `name = value` to filter columns using the supplied value. Each constraint behaves the same as `pl.col(name).eq(value)`, and is implicitly joined with the other filter conditions using `&`.\
\
See also\
\
[`filter`](api/polars.LazyFrame.filter.html#polars.LazyFrame.filter "polars.LazyFrame.filter")\
\
Notes\
\
If you are transitioning from Pandas, and performing filter operations based on the comparison of two or more columns, please note that in Polars any comparison involving `null` values will result in a `null` result, _not_ boolean True or False. As a result, these rows will not be removed. Ensure that null values are handled appropriately to avoid unexpected behaviour (see examples below).\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "foo": \[2, 3, None, 4, 0\],\
...         "bar": \[5, 6, None, None, 0\],\
...         "ham": \["a", "b", None, "c", "d"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\
Remove rows matching a condition:\
\
\>>> lf.remove(\
...     pl.col("bar") \>= 5,\
... ).collect()\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 4    в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ c    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 0    в”Ҷ 0    в”Ҷ d    в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Discard rows based on multiple conditions, combined with and/or operators:\
\
\>>> lf.remove(\
...     (pl.col("foo") \>= 0) & (pl.col("bar") \>= 0),\
... ).collect()\
shape: (2, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 4    в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ c    в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
\>>> lf.remove(\
...     (pl.col("foo") \>= 0) | (pl.col("bar") \>= 0),\
... ).collect()\
shape: (1, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Provide multiple constraints using `*args` syntax:\
\
\>>> lf.remove(\
...     pl.col("ham").is\_not\_null(),\
...     pl.col("bar") \>= 0,\
... ).collect()\
shape: (2, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 4    в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ c    в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Provide constraints(s) using `**kwargs` syntax:\
\
\>>> lf.remove(foo\=0, bar\=0).collect()\
shape: (4, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2    в”Ҷ 5    в”Ҷ a    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 3    в”Ҷ 6    в”Ҷ b    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 4    в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ c    в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Remove rows by comparing two columns against each other; in this case, we remove rows where the two columns are not equal (using `ne_missing` to ensure that null values compare equal):\
\
\>>> lf.remove(\
...     pl.col("foo").ne\_missing(pl.col("bar")),\
... ).collect()\
shape: (2, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 0    в”Ҷ 0    в”Ҷ d    в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
rename(\
\
_mapping: [dict](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#dict "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
, [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] | [Callable](https://docs.python.org/3/library/typing.html#typing.Callable "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
\], [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
\]_,\
\
_\*_,\
\
_strict: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L5663-L5721)\
\
Rename column names.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**mapping**\
\
Key value pairs that map from old name to new name, or a function that takes the old name as input and returns the new name.\
\
**strict**\
\
Validate that all column names exist in the current schema, and throw an exception if any do not. (Note that this parameter is a no-op when passing a function to `mapping`).\
\
Notes\
\
If existing names are swapped (e.g. вҖҳAвҖҷ points to вҖҳBвҖҷ and вҖҳBвҖҷ points to вҖҳAвҖҷ), polars will block projection and predicate pushdowns at this node.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],\
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8\],\
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> lf.rename({"foo": "apple"}).collect()\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ apple в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---   в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64   в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1     в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2     в”Ҷ 7   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 3     в”Ҷ 8   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> lf.rename(lambda column\_name: "c" + column\_name\[1:\]).collect()\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ coo в”Ҷ car в”Ҷ cam в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
reverse() вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L5723-L5747)\
\
Reverse the DataFrame.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(\
...     {\
...         "key": \["a", "b", "c"\],\
...         "val": \[1, 2, 3\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> lf.reverse().collect()\
shape: (3, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ key в”Ҷ val в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
rolling(\
\
_index\_column: IntoExpr_,\
\
_\*_,\
\
_period: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | timedelta_,\
\
_offset: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | timedelta | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_closed: ClosedInterval \= 'right'_,\
\
_group\_by: IntoExpr | Iterable\[IntoExpr\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
) вҶ’ LazyGroupBy[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L4137-L4271)\
\
Create rolling groups based on a temporal or integer column.\
\
Different from a `group_by_dynamic` the windows are now determined by the individual values and are not of constant intervals. For constant intervals use [`LazyFrame.group_by_dynamic()`](api/polars.LazyFrame.group_by_dynamic.html#polars.LazyFrame.group_by_dynamic "polars.LazyFrame.group_by_dynamic")\
.\
\
If you have a time series `<t_0, t_1, ..., t_n>`, then by default the windows created will be\
\
> *   (t\_0 - period, t\_0\]\
>     \
> *   (t\_1 - period, t\_1\]\
>     \
> *   вҖҰ\
>     \
> *   (t\_n - period, t\_n\]\
>     \
\
whereas if you pass a non-default `offset`, then the windows will be\
\
> *   (t\_0 + offset, t\_0 + offset + period\]
>     
> *   (t\_1 + offset, t\_1 + offset + period\]
>     
> *   вҖҰ
>     
> *   (t\_n + offset, t\_n + offset + period\]
>     

The `period` and `offset` arguments are created either from a timedelta, or by using the following string language:

*   1ns (1 nanosecond)
    
*   1us (1 microsecond)
    
*   1ms (1 millisecond)
    
*   1s (1 second)
    
*   1m (1 minute)
    
*   1h (1 hour)
    
*   1d (1 calendar day)
    
*   1w (1 calendar week)
    
*   1mo (1 calendar month)
    
*   1q (1 calendar quarter)
    
*   1y (1 calendar year)
    
*   1i (1 index count)
    

Or combine them: вҖң3d12h4m25sвҖқ # 3 days, 12 hours, 4 minutes, and 25 seconds

By вҖңcalendar dayвҖқ, we mean the corresponding time on the next day (which may not be 24 hours, due to daylight savings). Similarly for вҖңcalendar weekвҖқ, вҖңcalendar monthвҖқ, вҖңcalendar quarterвҖқ, and вҖңcalendar yearвҖқ.

Parameters:

**index\_column**

Column used to group based on the time window. Often of type Date/Datetime. This column must be sorted in ascending order (or, if `group_by` is specified, then it must be sorted in ascending order within each group).

In case of a rolling group by on indices, dtype needs to be one of {UInt32, UInt64, Int32, Int64}. Note that the first three get temporarily cast to Int64, so if performance matters use an Int64 column.

**period**

Length of the window - must be non-negative.

**offset**

Offset of the window. Default is `-period`.

**closed**{вҖҳrightвҖҷ, вҖҳleftвҖҷ, вҖҳbothвҖҷ, вҖҳnoneвҖҷ}

Define which sides of the temporal interval are closed (inclusive).

**group\_by**

Also group by this column/these columns

Returns:

LazyGroupBy

Object you can call `.agg` on to aggregate by groups, the result of which will be sorted by `index_column` (but note that if `group_by` columns are passed, it will only be sorted within each group).

See also

[`group_by_dynamic`](api/polars.LazyFrame.group_by_dynamic.html#polars.LazyFrame.group_by_dynamic "polars.LazyFrame.group_by_dynamic")

Examples

\>>> dates \= \[\
...     "2020-01-01 13:45:48",\
...     "2020-01-01 16:42:13",\
...     "2020-01-01 16:45:09",\
...     "2020-01-02 18:12:48",\
...     "2020-01-03 19:45:32",\
...     "2020-01-08 23:16:43",\
... \]
\>>> df \= pl.LazyFrame({"dt": dates, "a": \[3, 7, 5, 9, 2, 1\]}).with\_columns(
...     pl.col("dt").str.strptime(pl.Datetime).set\_sorted()
... )
\>>> out \= (
...     df.rolling(index\_column\="dt", period\="2d")
...     .agg(
...         pl.sum("a").alias("sum\_a"),
...         pl.min("a").alias("min\_a"),
...         pl.max("a").alias("max\_a"),
...     )
...     .collect()
... )
\>>> out
shape: (6, 4)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ dt                  в”Ҷ sum\_a в”Ҷ min\_a в”Ҷ max\_a в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---                 в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ i64   в”Ҷ i64   в”Ҷ i64   в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 2020-01-01 13:45:48 в”Ҷ 3     в”Ҷ 3     в”Ҷ 3     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2020-01-01 16:42:13 в”Ҷ 10    в”Ҷ 3     в”Ҷ 7     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2020-01-01 16:45:09 в”Ҷ 15    в”Ҷ 3     в”Ҷ 7     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2020-01-02 18:12:48 в”Ҷ 24    в”Ҷ 3     в”Ҷ 9     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2020-01-03 19:45:32 в”Ҷ 11    в”Ҷ 2     в”Ҷ 9     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2020-01-08 23:16:43 в”Ҷ 1     в”Ҷ 1     в”Ҷ 1     в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

_property_ schema_: Schema_[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L556-L589)

Get an ordered mapping of column names to their data type.

Warning

Resolving the schema of a LazyFrame is a potentially expensive operation. Using [`collect_schema()`](api/polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema.html#polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema "polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema")
 is the idiomatic way to resolve the schema. This property exists only for symmetry with the DataFrame class.

See also

[`collect_schema`](api/polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema.html#polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema "polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema")

`Schema`

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6.0, 7.0, 8.0\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.schema  
Schema({'foo': Int64, 'bar': Float64, 'ham': String})

select(

_\*exprs: IntoExpr | Iterable\[IntoExpr\]_,

_\*\*named\_exprs: IntoExpr_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L3890-L3997)

Select columns from this LazyFrame.

Parameters:

**\*exprs**

Column(s) to select, specified as positional arguments. Accepts expression input. Strings are parsed as column names, other non-expression inputs are parsed as literals.

**\*\*named\_exprs**

Additional columns to select, specified as keyword arguments. The columns will be renamed to the keyword used.

Examples

Pass the name of a column to select that column.

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.select("foo").collect()
shape: (3, 1)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Multiple columns can be selected by passing a list of column names.

\>>> lf.select(\["foo", "bar"\]).collect()
shape: (3, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Multiple columns can also be selected using positional arguments instead of a list. Expressions are also accepted.

\>>> lf.select(pl.col("foo"), pl.col("bar") + 1).collect()
shape: (3, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 9   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Use keyword arguments to easily name your expression inputs.

\>>> lf.select(
...     threshold\=pl.when(pl.col("foo") \> 2).then(10).otherwise(0)
... ).collect()
shape: (3, 1)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ threshold в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i32       в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 0         в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 0         в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 10        в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Expressions with multiple outputs can be automatically instantiated as Structs by enabling the setting `Config.set_auto_structify(True)`:

\>>> with pl.Config(auto\_structify\=True):
...     lf.select(
...         is\_odd\=(pl.col(pl.Int64) % 2 \== 1).name.suffix("\_is\_odd"),
...     ).collect()
shape: (3, 1)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ is\_odd       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---          в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ struct\[2\]    в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ {true,false} в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ {false,true} в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ {true,false} в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

select\_seq(

_\*exprs: IntoExpr | Iterable\[IntoExpr\]_,

_\*\*named\_exprs: IntoExpr_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L3999-L4027)

Select columns from this LazyFrame.

This will run all expression sequentially instead of in parallel. Use this when the work per expression is cheap.

Parameters:

**\*exprs**

Column(s) to select, specified as positional arguments. Accepts expression input. Strings are parsed as column names, other non-expression inputs are parsed as literals.

**\*\*named\_exprs**

Additional columns to select, specified as keyword arguments. The columns will be renamed to the keyword used.

See also

[`select`](../expressions/api/polars.select.html#polars.select "polars.select")

serialize(

_file: IOBase | [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Path | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_\*_,

_format: SerializationFormat \= 'binary'_,

) вҶ’ [bytes](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#bytes "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L721-L783)

Serialize the logical plan of this LazyFrame to a file or string in JSON format.

Parameters:

**file**

File path to which the result should be written. If set to `None` (default), the output is returned as a string instead.

**format**

The format in which to serialize. Options:

*   `"binary"`: Serialize to binary format (bytes). This is the default.
    
*   `"json"`: Serialize to JSON format (string) (deprecated).
    

See also

[`LazyFrame.deserialize`](api/polars.LazyFrame.deserialize.html#polars.LazyFrame.deserialize "polars.LazyFrame.deserialize")

Notes

Serialization is not stable across Polars versions: a LazyFrame serialized in one Polars version may not be deserializable in another Polars version.

Examples

Serialize the logical plan into a binary representation.

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame({"a": \[1, 2, 3\]}).sum()
\>>> bytes \= lf.serialize()

The bytes can later be deserialized back into a LazyFrame.

\>>> import io
\>>> pl.LazyFrame.deserialize(io.BytesIO(bytes)).collect()
shape: (1, 1)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 6   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

set\_sorted(

_column: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
_,

_\*_,

_descending: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L7301-L7330)

Flag a column as sorted.

This can speed up future operations.

Parameters:

**column**

Column that is sorted

**descending**

Whether the column is sorted in descending order.

Warning

This can lead to incorrect results if the data is NOT sorted!! Use with care!

shift(

_n: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 | IntoExprColumn \= 1_,

_\*_,

_fill\_value: IntoExpr | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L5749-L5825)

Shift values by the given number of indices.

Parameters:

**n**

Number of indices to shift forward. If a negative value is passed, values are shifted in the opposite direction instead.

**fill\_value**

Fill the resulting null values with this value. Accepts scalar expression input. Non-expression inputs are parsed as literals.

Notes

This method is similar to the `LAG` operation in SQL when the value for `n` is positive. With a negative value for `n`, it is similar to `LEAD`.

Examples

By default, values are shifted forward by one index.

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[1, 2, 3, 4\],
...         "b": \[5, 6, 7, 8\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.shift().collect()
shape: (4, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a    в”Ҷ b    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 1    в”Ҷ 5    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2    в”Ҷ 6    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3    в”Ҷ 7    в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Pass a negative value to shift in the opposite direction instead.

\>>> lf.shift(\-2).collect()
shape: (4, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a    в”Ҷ b    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 3    в”Ҷ 7    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 4    в”Ҷ 8    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Specify `fill_value` to fill the resulting null values.

\>>> lf.shift(\-2, fill\_value\=100).collect()
shape: (4, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 4   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 100 в”Ҷ 100 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 100 в”Ҷ 100 в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L1179-L1277)

Show a plot of the query plan.

Note that Graphviz must be installed to render the visualization (if not already present, you can download it here: [https://graphviz.org/download](https://graphviz.org/download)
).

Parameters:

**optimized**

Optimize the query plan.

**show**

Show the figure.

**output\_path**

Write the figure to disk.

**raw\_output**

Return dot syntax. This cannot be combined with `show` and/or `output_path`.

**figsize**

Passed to matplotlib if `show == True`.

**type\_coercion**

Do type coercion optimization.

**predicate\_pushdown**

Do predicate pushdown optimization.

**projection\_pushdown**

Do projection pushdown optimization.

**simplify\_expression**

Run simplify expressions optimization.

**slice\_pushdown**

Slice pushdown optimization.

**comm\_subplan\_elim**

Will try to cache branching subplans that occur on self-joins or unions.

**comm\_subexpr\_elim**

Common subexpressions will be cached and reused.

**cluster\_with\_columns**

Combine sequential independent calls to with\_columns.

**collapse\_joins**

Collapse a join and filters into a faster join.

**streaming**

Run parts of the query in a streaming fashion (this is in an alpha state).

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \["a", "b", "a", "b", "b", "c"\],
...         "b": \[1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6\],
...         "c": \[6, 5, 4, 3, 2, 1\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.group\_by("a", maintain\_order\=True).agg(pl.all().sum()).sort(
...     "a"
... ).show\_graph()

[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L2688-L2906)

Evaluate the query in streaming mode and write to a CSV file.

Warning

Streaming mode is considered **unstable**. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.

This allows streaming results that are larger than RAM to be written to disk.

Parameters:

**path**

File path to which the file should be written.

**include\_bom**

Whether to include UTF-8 BOM in the CSV output.

**include\_header**

Whether to include header in the CSV output.

**separator**

Separate CSV fields with this symbol.

**line\_terminator**

String used to end each row.

**quote\_char**

Byte to use as quoting character.

**batch\_size**

Number of rows that will be processed per thread.

**datetime\_format**

A format string, with the specifiers defined by the [chrono](https://docs.rs/chrono/latest/chrono/format/strftime/index.html)
 Rust crate. If no format specified, the default fractional-second precision is inferred from the maximum timeunit found in the frameвҖҷs Datetime cols (if any).

**date\_format**

A format string, with the specifiers defined by the [chrono](https://docs.rs/chrono/latest/chrono/format/strftime/index.html)
 Rust crate.

**time\_format**

A format string, with the specifiers defined by the [chrono](https://docs.rs/chrono/latest/chrono/format/strftime/index.html)
 Rust crate.

**float\_scientific**

Whether to use scientific form always (true), never (false), or automatically (None) for `Float32` and `Float64` datatypes.

**float\_precision**

Number of decimal places to write, applied to both `Float32` and `Float64` datatypes.

**null\_value**

A string representing null values (defaulting to the empty string).

**quote\_style**{вҖҳnecessaryвҖҷ, вҖҳalwaysвҖҷ, вҖҳnon\_numericвҖҷ, вҖҳneverвҖҷ}

Determines the quoting strategy used.

*   necessary (default): This puts quotes around fields only when necessary. They are necessary when fields contain a quote, delimiter or record terminator. Quotes are also necessary when writing an empty record (which is indistinguishable from a record with one empty field). This is the default.
    
*   always: This puts quotes around every field. Always.
    
*   never: This never puts quotes around fields, even if that results in invalid CSV data (e.g.: by not quoting strings containing the separator).
    
*   non\_numeric: This puts quotes around all fields that are non-numeric. Namely, when writing a field that does not parse as a valid float or integer, then quotes will be used even if they aren\`t strictly necessary.
    

**maintain\_order**

Maintain the order in which data is processed. Setting this to `False` will be slightly faster.

**type\_coercion**

Do type coercion optimization.

**predicate\_pushdown**

Do predicate pushdown optimization.

**projection\_pushdown**

Do projection pushdown optimization.

**simplify\_expression**

Run simplify expressions optimization.

**slice\_pushdown**

Slice pushdown optimization.

**collapse\_joins**

Collapse a join and filters into a faster join

**no\_optimization**

Turn off (certain) optimizations.

**storage\_options**

Options that indicate how to connect to a cloud provider.

The cloud providers currently supported are AWS, GCP, and Azure. See supported keys here:

*   [aws](https://docs.rs/object_store/latest/object_store/aws/enum.AmazonS3ConfigKey.html)
    
*   [gcp](https://docs.rs/object_store/latest/object_store/gcp/enum.GoogleConfigKey.html)
    
*   [azure](https://docs.rs/object_store/latest/object_store/azure/enum.AzureConfigKey.html)
    
*   Hugging Face (`hf://`): Accepts an API key under the `token` parameter: `{'token': '...'}`, or by setting the `HF_TOKEN` environment variable.
    

If `storage_options` is not provided, Polars will try to infer the information from environment variables.

**credential\_provider**

Provide a function that can be called to provide cloud storage credentials. The function is expected to return a dictionary of credential keys along with an optional credential expiry time.

Warning

This functionality is considered **unstable**. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.

**retries**

Number of retries if accessing a cloud instance fails.

**sync\_on\_close: { None, вҖҳdataвҖҷ, вҖҳallвҖҷ }**

Sync to disk when before closing a file.

*   `None` does not sync.
    
*   `data` syncs the file contents.
    
*   `all` syncs the file contents and metadata.
    

Returns:

DataFrame

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.scan\_csv("/path/to/my\_larger\_than\_ram\_file.csv")  
\>>> lf.sink\_csv("out.csv")

*   [aws](https://docs.rs/object_store/latest/object_store/aws/enum.AmazonS3ConfigKey.html)
    
*   [gcp](https://docs.rs/object_store/latest/object_store/gcp/enum.GoogleConfigKey.html)
    
*   [azure](https://docs.rs/object_store/latest/object_store/azure/enum.AzureConfigKey.html)

 \= True_,

_type\_coercion: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_\_type\_check: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_predicate\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_projection\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_simplify\_expression: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_slice\_pushdown: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_collapse\_joins: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

_no\_optimization: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_storage\_options: [dict](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#dict "(in Python v3.13)")
\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
, Any\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_credential\_provider: CredentialProviderFunction | Literal\['auto'\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= 'auto'_,

_retries: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= 2_,

 \= None_,

) вҶ’ [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L2908-L3042)

Evaluate the query in streaming mode and write to an NDJSON file.

Warning

Streaming mode is considered **unstable**. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.

This allows streaming results that are larger than RAM to be written to disk.

Parameters:

**path**

File path to which the file should be written.

**maintain\_order**

Maintain the order in which data is processed. Setting this to `False` will be slightly faster.

**type\_coercion**

Do type coercion optimization.

**predicate\_pushdown**

Do predicate pushdown optimization.

**projection\_pushdown**

Do projection pushdown optimization.

**simplify\_expression**

Run simplify expressions optimization.

**slice\_pushdown**

Slice pushdown optimization.

**collapse\_joins**

Collapse a join and filters into a faster join

**no\_optimization**

Turn off (certain) optimizations.

**storage\_options**

Options that indicate how to connect to a cloud provider.

The cloud providers currently supported are AWS, GCP, and Azure. See supported keys here:

*   [aws](https://docs.rs/object_store/latest/object_store/aws/enum.AmazonS3ConfigKey.html)
    
*   [gcp](https://docs.rs/object_store/latest/object_store/gcp/enum.GoogleConfigKey.html)
    
*   [azure](https://docs.rs/object_store/latest/object_store/azure/enum.AzureConfigKey.html)
    
*   Hugging Face (`hf://`): Accepts an API key under the `token` parameter: `{'token': '...'}`, or by setting the `HF_TOKEN` environment variable.
    

If `storage_options` is not provided, Polars will try to infer the information from environment variables.

**credential\_provider**

Provide a function that can be called to provide cloud storage credentials. The function is expected to return a dictionary of credential keys along with an optional credential expiry time.

Warning

This functionality is considered **unstable**. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.

**retries**

Number of retries if accessing a cloud instance fails.

**sync\_on\_close: { None, вҖҳdataвҖҷ, вҖҳallвҖҷ }**

Sync to disk when before closing a file.

*   `None` does not sync.
    
*   `data` syncs the file contents.
    
*   `all` syncs the file contents and metadata.
    

Returns:

DataFrame

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.scan\_csv("/path/to/my\_larger\_than\_ram\_file.csv")  
\>>> lf.sink\_ndjson("out.ndjson")

[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L2347-L2545)

Evaluate the query in streaming mode and write to a Parquet file.

Warning

Streaming mode is considered **unstable**. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.

This allows streaming results that are larger than RAM to be written to disk.

Parameters:

**path**

File path to which the file should be written.

**compression**{вҖҳlz4вҖҷ, вҖҳuncompressedвҖҷ, вҖҳsnappyвҖҷ, вҖҳgzipвҖҷ, вҖҳlzoвҖҷ, вҖҳbrotliвҖҷ, вҖҳzstdвҖҷ}

Choose вҖңzstdвҖқ for good compression performance. Choose вҖңlz4вҖқ for fast compression/decompression. Choose вҖңsnappyвҖқ for more backwards compatibility guarantees when you deal with older parquet readers.

**compression\_level**

The level of compression to use. Higher compression means smaller files on disk.

*   вҖңgzipвҖқ : min-level: 0, max-level: 10.
    
*   вҖңbrotliвҖқ : min-level: 0, max-level: 11.
    
*   вҖңzstdвҖқ : min-level: 1, max-level: 22.
    

**statistics**

Write statistics to the parquet headers. This is the default behavior.

Possible values:

*   `True`: enable default set of statistics (default). Some statistics may be disabled.
    
*   `False`: disable all statistics
    
*   вҖңfullвҖқ: calculate and write all available statistics. Cannot be combined with `use_pyarrow`.
    
*   `{ "statistic-key": True / False, ... }`. Cannot be combined with `use_pyarrow`. Available keys:
    
    *   вҖңminвҖқ: column minimum value (default: `True`)
        
    *   вҖңmaxвҖқ: column maximum value (default: `True`)
        
    *   вҖңdistinct\_countвҖқ: number of unique column values (default: `False`)
        
    *   вҖңnull\_countвҖқ: number of null values in column (default: `True`)
        

**row\_group\_size**

Size of the row groups in number of rows. If None (default), the chunks of the `DataFrame` are used. Writing in smaller chunks may reduce memory pressure and improve writing speeds.

**data\_page\_size**

Size limit of individual data pages. If not set defaults to 1024 \* 1024 bytes

**maintain\_order**

Maintain the order in which data is processed. Setting this to `False` will be slightly faster.

**type\_coercion**

Do type coercion optimization.

**predicate\_pushdown**

Do predicate pushdown optimization.

**projection\_pushdown**

Do projection pushdown optimization.

**simplify\_expression**

Run simplify expressions optimization.

**slice\_pushdown**

Slice pushdown optimization.

**collapse\_joins**

Collapse a join and filters into a faster join

**no\_optimization**

Turn off (certain) optimizations.

**storage\_options**

Options that indicate how to connect to a cloud provider.

The cloud providers currently supported are AWS, GCP, and Azure. See supported keys here:

*   [aws](https://docs.rs/object_store/latest/object_store/aws/enum.AmazonS3ConfigKey.html)
    
*   [gcp](https://docs.rs/object_store/latest/object_store/gcp/enum.GoogleConfigKey.html)
    
*   [azure](https://docs.rs/object_store/latest/object_store/azure/enum.AzureConfigKey.html)
    
*   Hugging Face (`hf://`): Accepts an API key under the `token` parameter: `{'token': '...'}`, or by setting the `HF_TOKEN` environment variable.
    

If `storage_options` is not provided, Polars will try to infer the information from environment variables.

**credential\_provider**

Provide a function that can be called to provide cloud storage credentials. The function is expected to return a dictionary of credential keys along with an optional credential expiry time.

Warning

This functionality is considered **unstable**. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.

**retries**

Number of retries if accessing a cloud instance fails.

**sync\_on\_close: { None, вҖҳdataвҖҷ, вҖҳallвҖҷ }**

Sync to disk when before closing a file.

*   `None` does not sync.
    
*   `data` syncs the file contents.
    
*   `all` syncs the file contents and metadata.
    

Returns:

DataFrame

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.scan\_csv("/path/to/my\_larger\_than\_ram\_file.csv")  
\>>> lf.sink\_parquet("out.parquet")

 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L5827-L5862)

Get a slice of this DataFrame.

Parameters:

**offset**

Start index. Negative indexing is supported.

**length**

Length of the slice. If set to `None`, all rows starting at the offset will be selected.

Examples

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \["x", "y", "z"\],
...         "b": \[1, 3, 5\],
...         "c": \[2, 4, 6\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.slice(1, 2).collect()

в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ y   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ z   в”Ҷ 5   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

sort(

_by: IntoExpr | Iterable\[IntoExpr\]_,

_\*more\_by: IntoExpr_,

_descending: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Sequence\[[bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] \= False_,

_nulls\_last: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Sequence\[[bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] \= False_,

_maintain\_order: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_multithreaded: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L1305-L1423)

Sort the LazyFrame by the given columns.

Parameters:

**by**

Column(s) to sort by. Accepts expression input, including selectors. Strings are parsed as column names.

**\*more\_by**

Additional columns to sort by, specified as positional arguments.

**descending**

Sort in descending order. When sorting by multiple columns, can be specified per column by passing a sequence of booleans.

**nulls\_last**

Place null values last; can specify a single boolean applying to all columns or a sequence of booleans for per-column control.

**maintain\_order**

Whether the order should be maintained if elements are equal. Note that if `true` streaming is not possible and performance might be worse since this requires a stable search.

**multithreaded**

Sort using multiple threads.

Examples

Pass a single column name to sort by that column.

\>>> lf \= pl.LazyFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[1, 2, None\],
...         "b": \[6.0, 5.0, 4.0\],
...         "c": \["a", "c", "b"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> lf.sort("a").collect()
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a    в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ f64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 4.0 в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 1    в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2    в”Ҷ 5.0 в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Sorting by expressions is also supported.

\>>> lf.sort(pl.col("a") + pl.col("b") \* 2, nulls\_last\=True).collect()
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a    в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ f64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 2    в”Ҷ 5.0 в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 1    в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 4.0 в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Sort by multiple columns by passing a list of columns.

\>>> lf.sort(\["c", "a"\], descending\=True).collect()
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a    в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ f64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 2    в”Ҷ 5.0 в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 4.0 в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 1    в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Or use positional arguments to sort by multiple columns in the same way.

\>>> lf.sort("c", "a", descending\=\[False, True\]).collect()
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a    в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ 1    в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 4.0 в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2    в”Ҷ 5.0 в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

sql(

_query: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
_,

_\*_,

_table\_name: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= 'self'_,

) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L1425-L1507)

Execute a SQL query against the LazyFrame.

Added in version 0.20.23.

Warning

This functionality is considered **unstable**, although it is close to being considered stable. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.

Parameters:

**query**

SQL query to execute.

**table\_name**

Optionally provide an explicit name for the table that represents the calling frame (defaults to вҖңselfвҖқ).

See also

[`SQLContext`](../sql/python_api.html#polars.SQLContext "polars.SQLContext")

Notes

*   The calling frame is automatically registered as a table in the SQL context under the name вҖңselfвҖқ. If you want access to the DataFrames and LazyFrames found in the current globals, use the top-level [`pl.sql`](../expressions/api/polars.sql.html#polars.sql "polars.sql")
    .
    
*   More control over registration and execution behaviour is available by using the [`SQLContext`](../sql/python_api.html#polars.SQLContext "polars.SQLContext")
     object.
    

Examples

\>>> lf1 \= pl.LazyFrame({"a": \[1, 2, 3\], "b": \[6, 7, 8\], "c": \["z", "y", "x"\]})
\>>> lf2 \= pl.LazyFrame({"a": \[3, 2, 1\], "d": \[125, \-654, 888\]})

Query the LazyFrame using SQL:

\>>> lf1.sql("SELECT c, b FROM self WHERE a > 1").collect()
shape: (2, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ y   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ x   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Apply SQL transforms (aliasing вҖңselfвҖқ to вҖңframeвҖқ) then filter natively (you can freely mix SQL and native operations):

\>>> lf1.sql(
...     query\='''
...         SELECT
...             a,
...             (a % 2 == 0) AS a\_is\_even,
...             (b::float4 / 2) AS "b/2",
...             CONCAT\_WS(':', c, c, c) AS c\_c\_c
...         FROM frame
...         ORDER BY a
...     ''',
...     table\_name\="frame",
... ).filter(~pl.col("c\_c\_c").str.starts\_with("x")).collect()
shape: (2, 4)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ a\_is\_even в”Ҷ b/2 в”Ҷ c\_c\_c в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ ---       в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ ---   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ bool      в”Ҷ f32 в”Ҷ str   в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ false     в”Ҷ 3.0 в”Ҷ z:z:z в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ true      в”Ҷ 3.5 в”Ҷ y:y:y в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

std(_ddof: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= 1_) вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/lazyframe/frame.py#L6419-L6457)

Aggregate the columns in the LazyFrame to their standard deviation value.

Parameters:

**ddof**

вҖңDelta Degrees of FreedomвҖқ: the divisor used in the calculation is N - ddof, where N represents the number of elements. By default ddof is 1.

...     {
...         "a": \[1, 2, 3, 4\],
...         "b": \[1, 2, 1, 1\],
...     }
