_classmethod_ deserialize(

_source: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Path | IOBase_,

_\*_,

_format: SerializationFormat \= 'binary'_,

) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L433-L491)

Read a serialized DataFrame from a file.

Parameters:

**source**

Path to a file or a file-like object (by file-like object, we refer to objects that have a `read()` method, such as a file handler (e.g. via builtin `open` function) or `BytesIO`).

**format**

The format with which the DataFrame was serialized. Options:

*   `"binary"`: Deserialize from binary format (bytes). This is the default.
    
*   `"json"`: Deserialize from JSON format (string).
    

See also

[`DataFrame.serialize`](api/polars.DataFrame.serialize.html#polars.DataFrame.serialize "polars.DataFrame.serialize")

Notes

Serialization is not stable across Polars versions: a LazyFrame serialized in one Polars version may not be deserializable in another Polars version.

Examples

\>>> import io
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame({"a": \[1, 2, 3\], "b": \[4.0, 5.0, 6.0\]})
\>>> bytes \= df.serialize()
\>>> pl.DataFrame.deserialize(io.BytesIO(bytes))
shape: (3, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ f64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 4.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 5.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

drop(

_\*columns: ColumnNameOrSelector | Iterable\[ColumnNameOrSelector\]_,

_strict: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L8114-L8197)

Remove columns from the dataframe.

Parameters:

**\*columns**

Names of the columns that should be removed from the dataframe. Accepts column selector input.

**strict**

Validate that all column names exist in the current schema, and throw an exception if any do not.

Examples

Drop a single column by passing the name of that column.

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6.0, 7.0, 8.0\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.drop("ham")
shape: (3, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ f64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8.0 в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Drop multiple columns by passing a list of column names.

\>>> df.drop(\["bar", "ham"\])
shape: (3, 1)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Drop multiple columns by passing a selector.

\>>> import polars.selectors as cs
\>>> df.drop(cs.numeric())
shape: (3, 1)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Use positional arguments to drop multiple columns.

\>>> df.drop("foo", "ham")
shape: (3, 1)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ bar в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ f64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 6.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 7.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 8.0 в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

drop\_in\_place(_name: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
_) вҶ’ Series[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L8199-L8231)

Drop a single column in-place and return the dropped column.

Parameters:

**name**

Name of the column to drop.

Returns:

Series

The dropped column.

Examples

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.drop\_in\_place("ham")
shape: (3,)
Series: 'ham' \[str\]
\[\
    "a"\
    "b"\
    "c"\
\]

drop\_nans(

_subset: ColumnNameOrSelector | Collection\[ColumnNameOrSelector\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L6101-L6176)

Drop all rows that contain one or more NaN values.

The original order of the remaining rows is preserved.

Parameters:

**subset**

Column name(s) for which NaN values are considered; if set to `None` (default), use all columns (note that only floating-point columns can contain NaNs).

Examples

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[\-20.5, float("nan"), 80.0\],
...         "bar": \[float("nan"), 110.0, 25.5\],
...         "ham": \["xxx", "yyy", None\],
...     }
... )

The default behavior of this method is to drop rows where any single value in the row is NaN:

\>>> df.drop\_nans()
shape: (1, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ f64  в”Ҷ f64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 80.0 в”Ҷ 25.5 в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

This behaviour can be constrained to consider only a subset of columns, as defined by name, or with a selector. For example, dropping rows only if there is a NaN in the вҖңbarвҖқ column:

\>>> df.drop\_nans(subset\=\["bar"\])
shape: (2, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar   в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ f64  в”Ҷ f64   в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ NaN  в”Ҷ 110.0 в”Ҷ yyy  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 80.0 в”Ҷ 25.5  в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Dropping a row only if _all_ values are NaN requires a different formulation:

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[float("nan"), float("nan"), float("nan"), float("nan")\],
...         "b": \[10.0, 2.5, float("nan"), 5.25\],
...         "c": \[65.75, float("nan"), float("nan"), 10.5\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.filter(~pl.all\_horizontal(pl.all().is\_nan()))
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b    в”Ҷ c     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ f64 в”Ҷ f64  в”Ҷ f64   в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ NaN в”Ҷ 10.0 в”Ҷ 65.75 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ NaN в”Ҷ 2.5  в”Ҷ NaN   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ NaN в”Ҷ 5.25 в”Ҷ 10.5  в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

drop\_nulls(

_subset: ColumnNameOrSelector | Collection\[ColumnNameOrSelector\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L6178-L6284)

Drop all rows that contain null values.

The original order of the remaining rows is preserved.

Parameters:

**subset**

Column name(s) for which null values are considered. If set to `None` (default), use all columns.

Examples

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6, None, 8\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", None\],
...     }
... )

The default behavior of this method is to drop rows where any single value of the row is null.

\>>> df.drop\_nulls()
shape: (1, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

This behaviour can be constrained to consider only a subset of columns, as defined by name or with a selector. For example, dropping rows if there is a null in any of the integer columns:

\>>> import polars.selectors as cs
\>>> df.drop\_nulls(subset\=cs.integer())
shape: (2, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Below are some additional examples that show how to drop null values based on other conditions.

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[None, None, None, None\],
...         "b": \[1, 2, None, 1\],
...         "c": \[1, None, None, 1\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df
shape: (4, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a    в”Ҷ b    в”Ҷ c    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 1    в”Ҷ 1    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 2    в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 1    в”Ҷ 1    в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Drop a row only if all values are null:

\>>> df.filter(~pl.all\_horizontal(pl.all().is\_null()))
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a    в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 1    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 2   в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 1    в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Drop a column if all values are null:

\>>> df\[\[s.name for s in df if not (s.null\_count() \== df.height)\]\]
shape: (4, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ b    в”Ҷ c    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1    в”Ҷ 1    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2    в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 1    в”Ҷ 1    в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

_property_ dtypes_: [list](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#list "(in Python v3.13)")
\[[DataType](../api/polars.datatypes.DataType.html#polars.datatypes.DataType "polars.datatypes.DataType")\
\]_[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L854-L893)

Get the column data types.

The data types can also be found in column headers when printing the DataFrame.

Returns:

list of DataType

A list containing the data type of each column in order.

See also

[`schema`](api/polars.DataFrame.schema.html#polars.DataFrame.schema "polars.DataFrame.schema")

Examples

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6.0, 7.0, 8.0\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.dtypes
\[Int64, Float64, String\]
\>>> df
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ f64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7.0 в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8.0 в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

equals(

_other: DataFrame_,

_\*_,

_null\_equal: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= True_,

) вҶ’ [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L5882-L5918)

Check whether the DataFrame is equal to another DataFrame.

Parameters:

**other**

DataFrame to compare with.

**null\_equal**

Consider null values as equal.

See also

[`polars.testing.assert_frame_equal`](../api/polars.testing.assert_frame_equal.html#polars.testing.assert_frame_equal "polars.testing.assert_frame_equal")

Examples

\>>> df1 \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6.0, 7.0, 8.0\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df2 \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[3, 2, 1\],
...         "bar": \[8.0, 7.0, 6.0\],
...         "ham": \["c", "b", "a"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df1.equals(df1)
True
\>>> df1.equals(df2)
False

estimated\_size(_unit: SizeUnit \= 'b'_) вҶ’ [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [float](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#float "(in Python v3.13)")
[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L4626-L4669)

Return an estimation of the total (heap) allocated size of the `DataFrame`.

Estimated size is given in the specified unit (bytes by default).

This estimation is the sum of the size of its buffers, validity, including nested arrays. Multiple arrays may share buffers and bitmaps. Therefore, the size of 2 arrays is not the sum of the sizes computed from this function. In particular, \[`StructArray`\]вҖҷs size is an upper bound.

When an array is sliced, its allocated size remains constant because the buffer unchanged. However, this function will yield a smaller number. This is because this function returns the visible size of the buffer, not its total capacity.

FFI buffers are included in this estimation.

Parameters:

**unit**{вҖҳbвҖҷ, вҖҳkbвҖҷ, вҖҳmbвҖҷ, вҖҳgbвҖҷ, вҖҳtbвҖҷ}

Scale the returned size to the given unit.

Notes

For data with Object dtype, the estimated size only reports the pointer size, which is a huge underestimation.

Examples

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "x": list(reversed(range(1\_000\_000))),
...         "y": \[v / 1000 for v in range(1\_000\_000)\],
...         "z": \[str(v) for v in range(1\_000\_000)\],
...     },
...     schema\=\[("x", pl.UInt32), ("y", pl.Float64), ("z", pl.String)\],
... )
\>>> df.estimated\_size()
17888890
\>>> df.estimated\_size("mb")
17.0601749420166

explode(

_columns: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Expr | Sequence\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr\]_,

_\*more\_columns: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Expr_,

) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L8672-L8729)

Explode the dataframe to long format by exploding the given columns.

Parameters:

**columns**

Column names, expressions, or a selector defining them. The underlying columns being exploded must be of the `List` or `Array` data type.

**\*more\_columns**

Additional names of columns to explode, specified as positional arguments.

Returns:

DataFrame

Examples

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "letters": \["a", "a", "b", "c"\],
...         "numbers": \[\[1\], \[2, 3\], \[4, 5\], \[6, 7, 8\]\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df
shape: (4, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ letters в”Ҷ numbers   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---     в”Ҷ ---       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str     в”Ҷ list\[i64\] в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a       в”Ҷ \[1\]       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ a       в”Ҷ \[2, 3\]    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b       в”Ҷ \[4, 5\]    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c       в”Ҷ \[6, 7, 8\] в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
\>>> df.explode("numbers")
shape: (8, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ letters в”Ҷ numbers в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---     в”Ҷ ---     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str     в”Ҷ i64     в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a       в”Ҷ 1       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ a       в”Ҷ 2       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ a       в”Ҷ 3       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b       в”Ҷ 4       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b       в”Ҷ 5       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c       в”Ҷ 6       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c       в”Ҷ 7       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c       в”Ҷ 8       в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

extend(

_other: DataFrame_,

) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L8052-L8112)

Extend the memory backed by this `DataFrame` with the values from `other`.

Different from `vstack` which adds the chunks from `other` to the chunks of this `DataFrame`, `extend` appends the data from `other` to the underlying memory locations and thus may cause a reallocation.

If this does not cause a reallocation, the resulting data structure will not have any extra chunks and thus will yield faster queries.

Prefer `extend` over `vstack` when you want to do a query after a single append. For instance, during online operations where you add `n` rows and rerun a query.

Prefer `vstack` over `extend` when you want to append many times before doing a query. For instance, when you read in multiple files and want to store them in a single `DataFrame`. In the latter case, finish the sequence of `vstack` operations with a `rechunk`.

Parameters:

**other**

DataFrame to vertically add.

Warning

This method modifies the dataframe in-place. The dataframe is returned for convenience only.

See also

[`vstack`](api/polars.DataFrame.vstack.html#polars.DataFrame.vstack "polars.DataFrame.vstack")

Examples

\>>> df1 \= pl.DataFrame({"foo": \[1, 2, 3\], "bar": \[4, 5, 6\]})
\>>> df2 \= pl.DataFrame({"foo": \[10, 20, 30\], "bar": \[40, 50, 60\]})
\>>> df1.extend(df2)
shape: (6, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 5   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 10  в”Ҷ 40  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 20  в”Ҷ 50  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 30  в”Ҷ 60  в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

fill\_nan(_value: Expr | [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [float](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#float "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
_) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L8626-L8670)

Fill floating point NaN values by an Expression evaluation.

Parameters:

**value**

Value with which to replace NaN values.

Returns:

DataFrame

DataFrame with NaN values replaced by the given value.

Warning

Note that floating point NaNs (Not a Number) are not missing values. To replace missing values, use [`fill_null()`](api/polars.DataFrame.fill_null.html#polars.DataFrame.fill_null "polars.DataFrame.fill_null")
.

See also

[`fill_null`](api/polars.DataFrame.fill_null.html#polars.DataFrame.fill_null "polars.DataFrame.fill_null")

Examples

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[1.5, 2, float("nan"), 4\],
...         "b": \[0.5, 4, float("nan"), 13\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.fill\_nan(99)
shape: (4, 2)

в”Ӯ 1.5  в”Ҷ 0.5  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2.0  в”Ҷ 4.0  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 99.0 в”Ҷ 99.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 4.0  в”Ҷ 13.0 в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Parameters:

filter(

_\*predicates: IntoExprColumn | Iterable\[IntoExprColumn\] | [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [list](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#list "(in Python v3.13)")
\[[bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] | np.ndarray\[Any, Any\]_,

_\*\*constraints: Any_,

) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L4935-L5101)

Filter rows, retaining those that match the given predicate expression(s).

The original order of the remaining rows is preserved.

Only rows where the predicate resolves as True are retained; when the predicate result is False (or null), the row is discarded.

Parameters:

**predicates**

Expression(s) that evaluate to a boolean Series.

**constraints**

Column filters; use `name = value` to filter columns by the supplied value. Each constraint will behave the same as `pl.col(name).eq(value)`, and be implicitly joined with the other filter conditions using `&`.

See also

[`remove`](api/polars.DataFrame.remove.html#polars.DataFrame.remove "polars.DataFrame.remove")

Notes

If you are transitioning from Pandas, and performing filter operations based on the comparison of two or more columns, please note that in Polars any comparison involving `null` values will result in a `null` result, _not_ boolean True or False. As a result, these rows will not be retained. Ensure that null values are handled appropriately to avoid unexpected behaviour (see examples below).

Examples

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3, None, 4, None, 0\],
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8, None, None, 9, 0\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c", None, "d", "e", "f"\],
...     }
... )

Filter rows matching a condition:

\>>> df.filter(pl.col("foo") \> 1)
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7    в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8    в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 4   в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ d   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Filter on multiple conditions, combined with and/or operators:

\>>> df.filter(
...     (pl.col("foo") < 3) & (pl.col("ham") \== "a"),
... )
shape: (1, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

\>>> df.filter(
...     (pl.col("foo") \== 1) | (pl.col("ham") \== "c"),
... )
shape: (2, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Provide multiple filters using `*args` syntax:

\>>> df.filter(
...     pl.col("foo") <= 2,
...     ~pl.col("ham").is\_in(\["b", "c"\]),
... )
shape: (2, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 0   в”Ҷ 0   в”Ҷ f   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Provide multiple filters using `**kwargs` syntax:

\>>> df.filter(foo\=2, ham\="b")
shape: (1, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Filter by comparing two columns against each other:

\>>> df.filter(
...     pl.col("foo") \== pl.col("bar"),
... )
shape: (1, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 0   в”Ҷ 0   в”Ҷ f   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

\>>> df.filter(
...     pl.col("foo") != pl.col("bar"),
... )
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Notice how the row with `None` values is filtered out. In order to keep the same behavior as pandas, use:

\>>> df.filter(
...     pl.col("foo").ne\_missing(pl.col("bar")),
... )
shape: (5, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ 9    в”Ҷ e   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

_property_ flags_: [dict](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#dict "(in Python v3.13)")
\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
, [dict](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#dict "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
, [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
\]\]_[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L895-L905)

Get flags that are set on the columns of this DataFrame.

Returns:

dict

Mapping from column names to column flags.

fold(_operation: Callable\[\[Series, Series\], Series\]_) вҶ’ Series[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L10663-L10754)

Apply a horizontal reduction on a DataFrame.

This can be used to effectively determine aggregations on a row level, and can be applied to any DataType that can be supercast (cast to a similar parent type).

An example of the supercast rules when applying an arithmetic operation on two DataTypes are for instance:

*   Int8 + String = String
    
*   Float32 + Int64 = Float32
    
*   Float32 + Float64 = Float64
    

Parameters:

**operation**

function that takes two `Series` and returns a `Series`.

Examples

A horizontal sum operation:

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[2, 1, 3\],
...         "b": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "c": \[1.0, 2.0, 3.0\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.fold(lambda s1, s2: s1 + s2)
shape: (3,)
Series: 'a' \[f64\]
\[\
    4.0\
    5.0\
    9.0\
\]

A horizontal minimum operation:

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame({"a": \[2, 1, 3\], "b": \[1, 2, 3\], "c": \[1.0, 2.0, 3.0\]})
\>>> df.fold(lambda s1, s2: s1.zip\_with(s1 < s2, s2))
shape: (3,)
Series: 'a' \[f64\]
\[\
    1.0\
    1.0\
    3.0\
\]

A horizontal string concatenation:

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \["foo", "bar", None\],
...         "b": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "c": \[1.0, 2.0, 3.0\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.fold(lambda s1, s2: s1 + s2)
shape: (3,)
Series: 'a' \[str\]
\[\
    "foo11.0"\
    "bar22.0"\
    null\
\]

A horizontal boolean or, similar to a row-wise .any():

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[False, False, True\],
...         "b": \[False, True, False\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.fold(lambda s1, s2: s1 | s2)
shape: (3,)
Series: 'a' \[bool\]
\[\
        false\
        true\
        true\
\]

glimpse(

_\*_,

_max\_items\_per\_column: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= 10_,

_max\_colname\_length: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= 50_,

_return\_as\_string: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

) вҶ’ [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L5269-L5354)

Return a dense preview of the DataFrame.

The formatting shows one line per column so that wide dataframes display cleanly. Each line shows the column name, the data type, and the first few values.

Parameters:

**max\_items\_per\_column**

Maximum number of items to show per column.

**max\_colname\_length**

Maximum length of the displayed column names; values that exceed this value are truncated with a trailing ellipsis.

**return\_as\_string**

If True, return the preview as a string instead of printing to stdout.

See also

[`describe`](api/polars.DataFrame.describe.html#polars.DataFrame.describe "polars.DataFrame.describe")
, [`head`](../expressions/api/polars.head.html#polars.head "polars.head")
, [`tail`](../expressions/api/polars.tail.html#polars.tail "polars.tail")

Examples

\>>> from datetime import date
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \[1.0, 2.8, 3.0\],
...         "b": \[4, 5, None\],
...         "c": \[True, False, True\],
...         "d": \[None, "b", "c"\],
...         "e": \["usd", "eur", None\],
...         "f": \[date(2020, 1, 1), date(2021, 1, 2), date(2022, 1, 1)\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.glimpse()
Rows: 3
Columns: 6
$ a  <f64> 1.0, 2.8, 3.0
$ b  <i64> 4, 5, None
$ c <bool> True, False, True
$ d  <str> None, 'b', 'c'
$ e  <str> 'usd', 'eur', None
$ f <date> 2020-01-01, 2021-01-02, 2022-01-01

group\_by(

_\*by: IntoExpr | Iterable\[IntoExpr\]_,

_maintain\_order: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_\*\*named\_by: IntoExpr_,

) вҶ’ GroupBy[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L6467-L6614)

Start a group by operation.

Parameters:

**\*by**

Column(s) to group by. Accepts expression input. Strings are parsed as column names.

**maintain\_order**

Ensure that the order of the groups is consistent with the input data. This is slower than a default group by. Settings this to `True` blocks the possibility to run on the streaming engine.

Note

Within each group, the order of rows is always preserved, regardless of this argument.

**\*\*named\_by**

Additional columns to group by, specified as keyword arguments. The columns will be renamed to the keyword used.

Returns:

GroupBy

Object which can be used to perform aggregations.

Examples

Group by one column and call `agg` to compute the grouped sum of another column.

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "a": \["a", "b", "a", "b", "c"\],
...         "b": \[1, 2, 1, 3, 3\],
...         "c": \[5, 4, 3, 2, 1\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.group\_by("a").agg(pl.col("b").sum())  
shape: (3, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 5   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Set `maintain_order=True` to ensure the order of the groups is consistent with the input.

\>>> df.group\_by("a", maintain\_order\=True).agg(pl.col("c"))
shape: (3, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ c         в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ ---       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ list\[i64\] в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ \[5, 3\]    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ \[4, 2\]    в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ \[1\]       в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Group by multiple columns by passing a list of column names.

\>>> df.group\_by(\["a", "b"\]).agg(pl.max("c"))  
shape: (4, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 5   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Or use positional arguments to group by multiple columns in the same way. Expressions are also accepted.

\>>> df.group\_by("a", pl.col("b") // 2).agg(pl.col("c").mean())  
shape: (3, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ f64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 0   в”Ҷ 4.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 3.0 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 1.0 в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

The `GroupBy` object returned by this method is iterable, returning the name and data of each group.

\>>> for name, data in df.group\_by("a"):  
...     print(name)
...     print(data)
('a',)
shape: (2, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 5   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
('b',)
shape: (2, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
('c',)
shape: (1, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

group\_by\_dynamic(

_index\_column: IntoExpr_,

_\*_,

_every: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | timedelta_,

_period: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | timedelta | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_offset: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | timedelta | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_include\_boundaries: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_closed: ClosedInterval \= 'left'_,

_label: Label \= 'left'_,

_group\_by: IntoExpr | Iterable\[IntoExpr\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_start\_by: StartBy \= 'window'_,

) вҶ’ DynamicGroupBy[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L6770-L7085)

Group based on a time value (or index value of type Int32, Int64).

Time windows are calculated and rows are assigned to windows. Different from a normal group by is that a row can be member of multiple groups. By default, the windows look like:

*   \[start, start + period)\
    \
*   \[start + every, start + every + period)\
    \
*   \[start + 2\*every, start + 2\*every + period)\
    \
*   вҖҰ\
    \
\
where `start` is determined by `start_by`, `offset`, `every`, and the earliest datapoint. See the `start_by` argument description for details.\
\
Warning\
\
The index column must be sorted in ascending order. If `group_by` is passed, then the index column must be sorted in ascending order within each group.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**index\_column**\
\
Column used to group based on the time window. Often of type Date/Datetime. This column must be sorted in ascending order (or, if `group_by` is specified, then it must be sorted in ascending order within each group).\
\
In case of a dynamic group by on indices, dtype needs to be one of {Int32, Int64}. Note that Int32 gets temporarily cast to Int64, so if performance matters use an Int64 column.\
\
**every**\
\
interval of the window\
\
**period**\
\
length of the window, if None it will equal вҖҳeveryвҖҷ\
\
**offset**\
\
offset of the window, does not take effect if `start_by` is вҖҳdatapointвҖҷ. Defaults to zero.\
\
**include\_boundaries**\
\
Add the lower and upper bound of the window to the вҖң\_lower\_boundaryвҖқ and вҖң\_upper\_boundaryвҖқ columns. This will impact performance because itвҖҷs harder to parallelize\
\
**closed**{вҖҳleftвҖҷ, вҖҳrightвҖҷ, вҖҳbothвҖҷ, вҖҳnoneвҖҷ}\
\
Define which sides of the temporal interval are closed (inclusive).\
\
**label**{вҖҳleftвҖҷ, вҖҳrightвҖҷ, вҖҳdatapointвҖҷ}\
\
Define which label to use for the window:\
\
*   вҖҳleftвҖҷ: lower boundary of the window\
    \
*   вҖҳrightвҖҷ: upper boundary of the window\
    \
*   вҖҳdatapointвҖҷ: the first value of the index column in the given window. If you donвҖҷt need the label to be at one of the boundaries, choose this option for maximum performance\
    \
\
**group\_by**\
\
Also group by this column/these columns\
\
**start\_by**{вҖҳwindowвҖҷ, вҖҳdatapointвҖҷ, вҖҳmondayвҖҷ, вҖҳtuesdayвҖҷ, вҖҳwednesdayвҖҷ, вҖҳthursdayвҖҷ, вҖҳfridayвҖҷ, вҖҳsaturdayвҖҷ, вҖҳsundayвҖҷ}\
\
The strategy to determine the start of the first window by.\
\
*   вҖҳwindowвҖҷ: Start by taking the earliest timestamp, truncating it with `every`, and then adding `offset`. Note that weekly windows start on Monday.\
    \
*   вҖҳdatapointвҖҷ: Start from the first encountered data point.\
    \
*   a day of the week (only takes effect if `every` contains `'w'`):\
    \
    *   вҖҳmondayвҖҷ: Start the window on the Monday before the first data point.\
        \
    *   вҖҳtuesdayвҖҷ: Start the window on the Tuesday before the first data point.\
        \
    *   вҖҰ\
        \
    *   вҖҳsundayвҖҷ: Start the window on the Sunday before the first data point.\
        \
    \
    The resulting window is then shifted back until the earliest datapoint is in or in front of it.\
    \
\
Returns:\
\
DynamicGroupBy\
\
Object you can call `.agg` on to aggregate by groups, the result of which will be sorted by `index_column` (but note that if `group_by` columns are passed, it will only be sorted within each group).\
\
See also\
\
[`rolling`](api/polars.DataFrame.rolling.html#polars.DataFrame.rolling "polars.DataFrame.rolling")\
\
Notes\
\
1.  If youвҖҷre coming from pandas, then\
    \
    \# polars\
    df.group\_by\_dynamic("ts", every\="1d").agg(pl.col("value").sum())\
    \
    is equivalent to\
    \
    \# pandas\
    df.set\_index("ts").resample("D")\["value"\].sum().reset\_index()\
    \
    though note that, unlike pandas, polars doesnвҖҷt add extra rows for empty windows. If you need `index_column` to be evenly spaced, then please combine with [`DataFrame.upsample()`](api/polars.DataFrame.upsample.html#polars.DataFrame.upsample "polars.DataFrame.upsample")\
    .\
    \
2.  The `every`, `period` and `offset` arguments are created with the following string language:\
    \
    *   1ns (1 nanosecond)\
        \
    *   1us (1 microsecond)\
        \
    *   1ms (1 millisecond)\
        \
    *   1s (1 second)\
        \
    *   1m (1 minute)\
        \
    *   1h (1 hour)\
        \
    *   1d (1 calendar day)\
        \
    *   1w (1 calendar week)\
        \
    *   1mo (1 calendar month)\
        \
    *   1q (1 calendar quarter)\
        \
    *   1y (1 calendar year)\
        \
    *   1i (1 index count)\
        \
    \
    Or combine them: вҖң3d12h4m25sвҖқ # 3 days, 12 hours, 4 minutes, and 25 seconds\
    \
    By вҖңcalendar dayвҖқ, we mean the corresponding time on the next day (which may not be 24 hours, due to daylight savings). Similarly for вҖңcalendar weekвҖқ, вҖңcalendar monthвҖқ, вҖңcalendar quarterвҖқ, and вҖңcalendar yearвҖқ.\
    \
    In case of a group\_by\_dynamic on an integer column, the windows are defined by:\
    \
    *   вҖң1iвҖқ # length 1\
        \
    *   вҖң10iвҖқ # length 10\
        \
\
Examples\
\
\>>> from datetime import datetime\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "time": pl.datetime\_range(\
...             start\=datetime(2021, 12, 16),\
...             end\=datetime(2021, 12, 16, 3),\
...             interval\="30m",\
...             eager\=True,\
...         ),\
...         "n": range(7),\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df\
shape: (7, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ time                в”Ҷ n   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---                 в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ 0   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 00:30:00 в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ 2   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 01:30:00 в”Ҷ 3   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 02:30:00 в”Ҷ 5   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 03:00:00 в”Ҷ 6   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Group by windows of 1 hour.\
\
\>>> df.group\_by\_dynamic("time", every\="1h", closed\="right").agg(pl.col("n"))\
shape: (4, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ time                в”Ҷ n         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---                 в”Ҷ ---       в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ list\[i64\] в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-15 23:00:00 в”Ҷ \[0\]       в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ \[1, 2\]    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ \[3, 4\]    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ \[5, 6\]    в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
The window boundaries can also be added to the aggregation result\
\
\>>> df.group\_by\_dynamic(\
...     "time", every\="1h", include\_boundaries\=True, closed\="right"\
... ).agg(pl.col("n").mean())\
shape: (4, 4)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ \_lower\_boundary     в”Ҷ \_upper\_boundary     в”Ҷ time                в”Ҷ n   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---                 в”Ҷ ---                 в”Ҷ ---                 в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ f64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-15 23:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-15 23:00:00 в”Ҷ 0.0 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ 1.5 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ 3.5 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 03:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ 5.5 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
When closed=вҖқleftвҖқ, the window excludes the right end of interval: \[lower\_bound, upper\_bound)\
\
\>>> df.group\_by\_dynamic("time", every\="1h", closed\="left").agg(pl.col("n"))\
shape: (4, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ time                в”Ҷ n         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---                 в”Ҷ ---       в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ list\[i64\] в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ \[0, 1\]    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ \[2, 3\]    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ \[4, 5\]    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 03:00:00 в”Ҷ \[6\]       в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
When closed=вҖқbothвҖқ the time values at the window boundaries belong to 2 groups.\
\
\>>> df.group\_by\_dynamic("time", every\="1h", closed\="both").agg(pl.col("n"))\
shape: (4, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ time                в”Ҷ n         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---                 в”Ҷ ---       в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ list\[i64\] в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ \[0, 1, 2\] в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ \[2, 3, 4\] в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ \[4, 5, 6\] в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 03:00:00 в”Ҷ \[6\]       в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Dynamic group bys can also be combined with grouping on normal keys\
\
\>>> df \= df.with\_columns(groups\=pl.Series(\["a", "a", "a", "b", "b", "a", "a"\]))\
\>>> df\
shape: (7, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ time                в”Ҷ n   в”Ҷ groups в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---                 в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ ---    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str    в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ 0   в”Ҷ a      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 00:30:00 в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ a      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ 2   в”Ҷ a      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 01:30:00 в”Ҷ 3   в”Ҷ b      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ 4   в”Ҷ b      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 02:30:00 в”Ҷ 5   в”Ҷ a      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2021-12-16 03:00:00 в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a      в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> df.group\_by\_dynamic(\
...     "time",\
...     every\="1h",\
...     closed\="both",\
...     group\_by\="groups",\
...     include\_boundaries\=True,\
... ).agg(pl.col("n"))\
shape: (6, 5)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ groups в”Ҷ \_lower\_boundary     в”Ҷ \_upper\_boundary     в”Ҷ time                в”Ҷ n         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---    в”Ҷ ---                 в”Ҷ ---                 в”Ҷ ---                 в”Ҷ ---       в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str    в”Ҷ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ list\[i64\] в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ a      в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 00:00:00 в”Ҷ \[0, 1, 2\] в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ a      в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ \[2\]       в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ a      в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 03:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ \[5, 6\]    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ a      в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 03:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 04:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 03:00:00 в”Ҷ \[6\]       в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ b      в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 01:00:00 в”Ҷ \[3, 4\]    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ b      в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 03:00:00 в”Ҷ 2021-12-16 02:00:00 в”Ҷ \[4\]       в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Dynamic group by on an index column\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "idx": pl.int\_range(0, 6, eager\=True),\
...         "A": \["A", "A", "B", "B", "B", "C"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> (\
...     df.group\_by\_dynamic(\
...         "idx",\
...         every\="2i",\
...         period\="3i",\
...         include\_boundaries\=True,\
...         closed\="right",\
...     ).agg(pl.col("A").alias("A\_agg\_list"))\
... )\
shape: (4, 4)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ \_lower\_boundary в”Ҷ \_upper\_boundary в”Ҷ idx в”Ҷ A\_agg\_list      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---             в”Ҷ ---             в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ ---             в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64             в”Ҷ i64             в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ list\[str\]       в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ -2              в”Ҷ 1               в”Ҷ -2  в”Ҷ \["A", "A"\]      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 0               в”Ҷ 3               в”Ҷ 0   в”Ҷ \["A", "B", "B"\] в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2               в”Ҷ 5               в”Ҷ 2   в”Ҷ \["B", "B", "C"\] в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 4               в”Ҷ 7               в”Ҷ 4   в”Ҷ \["C"\]           в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
hash\_rows(\
\
_seed: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= 0_,\
\
_seed\_1: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_seed\_2: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_seed\_3: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
) вҶ’ Series[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L11360-L11411)\
\
Hash and combine the rows in this DataFrame.\
\
The hash value is of type `UInt64`.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**seed**\
\
Random seed parameter. Defaults to 0.\
\
**seed\_1**\
\
Random seed parameter. Defaults to `seed` if not set.\
\
**seed\_2**\
\
Random seed parameter. Defaults to `seed` if not set.\
\
**seed\_3**\
\
Random seed parameter. Defaults to `seed` if not set.\
\
Notes\
\
This implementation of `hash_rows` does not guarantee stable results across different Polars versions. Its stability is only guaranteed within a single version.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "foo": \[1, None, 3, 4\],\
...         "ham": \["a", "b", None, "d"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.hash\_rows(seed\=42)  \
shape: (4,)\
Series: '' \[u64\]\
\[\
    10783150408545073287\
    1438741209321515184\
    10047419486152048166\
    2047317070637311557\
\]\
\
head(_n: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= 5_) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L5956-L6006)\
\
Get the first `n` rows.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**n**\
\
Number of rows to return. If a negative value is passed, return all rows except the last `abs(n)`.\
\
See also\
\
[`tail`](../expressions/api/polars.tail.html#polars.tail "polars.tail")\
, [`glimpse`](api/polars.DataFrame.glimpse.html#polars.DataFrame.glimpse "polars.DataFrame.glimpse")\
, [`slice`](api/polars.DataFrame.slice.html#polars.DataFrame.slice "polars.DataFrame.slice")\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3, 4, 5\],\
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8, 9, 10\],\
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c", "d", "e"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.head(3)\
shape: (3, 3)\

\

\
Series to stack.\
\
**in\_place**\
\
Modify in place.\
\

\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],\
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8\],\
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],\
...     }\
... )\

\>>> df.hstack(\[x\])\
shape: (3, 4)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ҷ apple в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ ---   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ҷ i64   в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ҷ 10    в”Ӯ\

insert\_column(_index: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
_, _column: IntoExprColumn_) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L4862-L4933)\
\
Insert a Series at a certain column index.\
\
This operation is in place.\
\

\
**index**\
\
Index at which to insert the new column.\
\
**column**\
\
`Series` or expression to insert.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame({"foo": \[1, 2, 3\], "bar": \[4, 5, 6\]})\
\>>> s \= pl.Series("baz", \[97, 98, 99\])\
\>>> df.insert\_column(1, s)\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ baz в”Ҷ bar в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 97  в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 98  в”Ҷ 5   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 99  в”Ҷ 6   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "a": \[1, 2, 3, 4\],\
...         "b": \[0.5, 4, 10, 13\],\
...         "c": \[True, True, False, True\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> s \= pl.Series("d", \[\-2.5, 15, 20.5, 0\])\
\>>> df.insert\_column(3, s)\
shape: (4, 4)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b    в”Ҷ c     в”Ҷ d    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ f64  в”Ҷ bool  в”Ҷ f64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 0.5  в”Ҷ true  в”Ҷ -2.5 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 4.0  в”Ҷ true  в”Ҷ 15.0 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 10.0 в”Ҷ false в”Ҷ 20.5 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 4   в”Ҷ 13.0 в”Ҷ true  в”Ҷ 0.0  в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\

is\_empty() вҶ’ [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\

Returns `True` if the DataFrame contains no rows.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame({"foo": \[1, 2, 3\], "bar": \[4, 5, 6\]})\
\>>> df.is\_empty()\

\>>> df.filter(pl.col("foo") \> 99).is\_empty()\
True\

в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
item(_row: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_, _column: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_) вҶ’ [Any](https://docs.python.org/3/library/typing.html#typing.Any "(in Python v3.13)")\
[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L1524-L1573)\
\
Return the DataFrame as a scalar, or return the element at the given row/column.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**row**\
\
Optional row index.\
\
**column**\
\
Optional column index or name.\
\
See also\
\
[`row`](api/polars.DataFrame.row.html#polars.DataFrame.row "polars.DataFrame.row")\
\
Get the values of a single row, either by index or by predicate.\
\
Notes\
\
If row/col not provided, this is equivalent to `df[0,0]`, with a check that the shape is (1,1). With row/col, this is equivalent to `df[row,col]`.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame({"a": \[1, 2, 3\], "b": \[4, 5, 6\]})\
\>>> df.select((pl.col("a") \* pl.col("b")).sum()).item()\
32\
\>>> df.item(1, 1)\
5\
\>>> df.item(2, "b")\
6\
\
iter\_columns() вҶ’ Iterator\[Series\][\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L11204-L11258)\
\
Returns an iterator over the columns of this DataFrame.\
\
Yields:\
\
Series\
\
Notes\
\
Consider whether you can use [`all()`](../expressions/api/polars.all.html#polars.all "polars.all")\
 instead. If you can, it will be more efficient.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "a": \[1, 3, 5\],\
...         "b": \[2, 4, 6\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> \[s.name for s in df.iter\_columns()\]\
\['a', 'b'\]\
\
If youвҖҷre using this to modify a dataframeвҖҷs columns, e.g.\
\
\>>> \# Do NOT do this\
\>>> pl.DataFrame(column \* 2 for column in df.iter\_columns())\
shape: (3, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 6   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 10  в”Ҷ 12  в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
then consider whether you can use [`all()`](../expressions/api/polars.all.html#polars.all "polars.all")\
 instead:\
\
\>>> df.select(pl.all() \* 2)\
shape: (3, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 6   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 10  в”Ҷ 12  в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
iter\_rows(\
\
_\*_,\
\
_named: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= False_,\
\
_buffer\_size: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= 512_,\
\
) вҶ’ Iterator\[[tuple](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#tuple "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[Any, ...\]\] | Iterator\[[dict](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#dict "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
, Any\]\][\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L11129-L11202)\
\
Returns an iterator over the DataFrame of rows of python-native values.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**named**\
\
Return dictionaries instead of tuples. The dictionaries are a mapping of column name to row value. This is more expensive than returning a regular tuple, but allows for accessing values by column name.\
\
**buffer\_size**\
\
Determines the number of rows that are buffered internally while iterating over the data; you should only modify this in very specific cases where the default value is determined not to be a good fit to your access pattern, as the speedup from using the buffer is significant (~2-4x). Setting this value to zero disables row buffering (not recommended).\
\
Returns:\
\
iterator of tuples (default) or dictionaries (if named) of python row values\
\
Warning\
\
Row iteration is not optimal as the underlying data is stored in columnar form; where possible, prefer export via one of the dedicated export/output methods that deals with columnar data.\
\
See also\
\
[`rows`](api/polars.DataFrame.rows.html#polars.DataFrame.rows "polars.DataFrame.rows")\
\
Materialises all frame data as a list of rows (potentially expensive).\
\
[`rows_by_key`](api/polars.DataFrame.rows_by_key.html#polars.DataFrame.rows_by_key "polars.DataFrame.rows_by_key")\
\
Materialises frame data as a key-indexed dictionary.\
\
Notes\
\
If you have `ns`\-precision temporal values you should be aware that Python natively only supports up to `Ојs`\-precision; `ns`\-precision values will be truncated to microseconds on conversion to Python. If this matters to your use-case you should export to a different format (such as Arrow or NumPy).\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "a": \[1, 3, 5\],\
...         "b": \[2, 4, 6\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> \[row\[0\] for row in df.iter\_rows()\]\
\[1, 3, 5\]\
\>>> \[row\["b"\] for row in df.iter\_rows(named\=True)\]\
\[2, 4, 6\]\
\
iter\_slices(_n\_rows: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= 10000_) вҶ’ Iterator\[DataFrame\][\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L11260-L11306)\
\
Returns a non-copying iterator of slices over the underlying DataFrame.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**n\_rows**\
\
Determines the number of rows contained in each DataFrame slice.\
\
See also\
\
[`iter_rows`](api/polars.DataFrame.iter_rows.html#polars.DataFrame.iter_rows "polars.DataFrame.iter_rows")\
\
Row iterator over frame data (does not materialise all rows).\
\
[`partition_by`](api/polars.DataFrame.partition_by.html#polars.DataFrame.partition_by "polars.DataFrame.partition_by")\
\
Split into multiple DataFrames, partitioned by groups.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> from datetime import date\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     data\={\
...         "a": range(17\_500),\
...         "b": date(2023, 1, 1),\
...         "c": "klmnoopqrstuvwxyz",\
...     },\
...     schema\_overrides\={"a": pl.Int32},\
... )\
\>>> for idx, frame in enumerate(df.iter\_slices()):\
...     print(f"{type(frame).\_\_name\_\_}:\[{idx}\]:{len(frame)}")\
DataFrame:\[0\]:10000\
DataFrame:\[1\]:7500\
\
Using `iter_slices` is an efficient way to chunk-iterate over DataFrames and any supported frame export/conversion types; for example, as RecordBatches:\
\
\>>> for frame in df.iter\_slices(n\_rows\=15\_000):\
...     record\_batch \= frame.to\_arrow().to\_batches()\[0\]\
...     print(f"{record\_batch.schema}\\n<< {len(record\_batch)}")\
a: int32\
b: date32\[day\]\
c: large\_string\
<< 15000\
a: int32\
b: date32\[day\]\
c: large\_string\
<< 2500\
\
join(\
\
_other: DataFrame_,\
\
_on: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr | Sequence\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_how: JoinStrategy \= 'inner'_,\
\
_\*_,\
\
_left\_on: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr | Sequence\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_right\_on: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr | Sequence\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_suffix: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= '\_right'_,\
\
_validate: JoinValidation \= 'm:m'_,\
\
_nulls\_equal: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= False_,\
\
_coalesce: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_maintain\_order: MaintainOrderJoin | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L7538-L7765)\
\
Join in SQL-like fashion.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**other**\
\
DataFrame to join with.\
\
**on**\
\
Name(s) of the join columns in both DataFrames. If set, `left_on` and `right_on` should be None. This should not be specified if `how="cross"`.\
\
**how**{вҖҳinnerвҖҷ, вҖҳleftвҖҷ, вҖҳrightвҖҷ, вҖҳfullвҖҷ, вҖҳsemiвҖҷ, вҖҳantiвҖҷ, вҖҳcrossвҖҷ}\
\
Join strategy.\
\
*   _inner_\
    \
    Returns rows that have matching values in both tables\
    \
*   _left_\
    \
    Returns all rows from the left table, and the matched rows from the right table\
    \
*   _right_\
    \
    Returns all rows from the right table, and the matched rows from the left table\
    \
*   _full_\
    \
    Returns all rows when there is a match in either left or right table\
    \
*   _cross_\
    \
    Returns the Cartesian product of rows from both tables\
    \
*   _semi_\
    \
    Returns rows from the left table that have a match in the right table.\
    \
*   _anti_\
    \
    Returns rows from the left table that have no match in the right table.\
    \
\
**left\_on**\
\
Name(s) of the left join column(s).\
\
**right\_on**\
\
Name(s) of the right join column(s).\
\
**suffix**\
\
Suffix to append to columns with a duplicate name.\
\
**validate: {вҖҳm:mвҖҷ, вҖҳm:1вҖҷ, вҖҳ1:mвҖҷ, вҖҳ1:1вҖҷ}**\
\
Checks if join is of specified type.\
\
> *   _many\_to\_many_\
>     \
>     вҖңm:mвҖқ: default, does not result in checks\
>     \
> *   _one\_to\_one_\
>     \
>     вҖң1:1вҖқ: check if join keys are unique in both left and right datasets\
>     \
> *   _one\_to\_many_\
>     \
>     вҖң1:mвҖқ: check if join keys are unique in left dataset\
>     \
> *   _many\_to\_one_\
>     \
>     вҖңm:1вҖқ: check if join keys are unique in right dataset\
>     \
\
Note\
\
This is currently not supported by the streaming engine.\
\
**nulls\_equal**\
\
Join on null values. By default null values will never produce matches.\
\
**coalesce**\
\
Coalescing behavior (merging of join columns).\
\
*   None: -> join specific.\
    \
*   True: -> Always coalesce join columns.\
    \
*   False: -> Never coalesce join columns.\
    \
\
Note\
\
Joining on any other expressions than `col` will turn off coalescing.\
\
**maintain\_order**{вҖҳnoneвҖҷ, вҖҳleftвҖҷ, вҖҳrightвҖҷ, вҖҳleft\_rightвҖҷ, вҖҳright\_leftвҖҷ}\
\
Which DataFrame row order to preserve, if any. Do not rely on any observed ordering without explicitly setting this parameter, as your code may break in a future release. Not specifying any ordering can improve performance Supported for inner, left, right and full joins\
\
*   _none_\
    \
    No specific ordering is desired. The ordering might differ across Polars versions or even between different runs.\
    \
*   _left_\
    \
    Preserves the order of the left DataFrame.\
    \
*   _right_\
    \
    Preserves the order of the right DataFrame.\
    \
*   _left\_right_\
    \
    First preserves the order of the left DataFrame, then the right.\
    \
*   _right\_left_\
    \
    First preserves the order of the right DataFrame, then the left.\
    \
\
See also\
\
[`join_asof`](api/polars.DataFrame.join_asof.html#polars.DataFrame.join_asof "polars.DataFrame.join_asof")\
\
Notes\
\
For joining on columns with categorical data, see [`polars.StringCache`](../api/polars.StringCache.html#polars.StringCache "polars.StringCache")\
.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],\
...         "bar": \[6.0, 7.0, 8.0\],\
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> other\_df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "apple": \["x", "y", "z"\],\
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "d"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.join(other\_df, on\="ham")\
shape: (2, 4)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ҷ apple в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ ---   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ f64 в”Ҷ str в”Ҷ str   в”Ӯ\

в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6.0 в”Ҷ a   в”Ҷ x     в”Ӯ\

\
_other: DataFrame_,\
\
