\
_left\_on: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr \= None_,\
\
_right\_on: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr \= None_,\
\
_on: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr \= None_,\
\
_by\_left: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Sequence\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_by\_right: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Sequence\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_by: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Sequence\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_strategy: AsofJoinStrategy \= 'backward'_,\
\
_suffix: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= '\_right'_,\
\
_tolerance: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [float](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#float "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | timedelta | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_allow\_parallel: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_force\_parallel: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= False_,\
\
_coalesce: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_allow\_exact\_matches: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_check\_sortedness: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L7187-L7536)\
\
Perform an asof join.\
\
This is similar to a left-join except that we match on nearest key rather than equal keys.\
\
Both DataFrames must be sorted by the `on` key (within each `by` group, if specified).\
\
For each row in the left DataFrame:\
\
> *   A вҖңbackwardвҖқ search selects the last row in the right DataFrame whose вҖҳonвҖҷ key is less than or equal to the leftвҖҷs key.\
>     \
> *   A вҖңforwardвҖқ search selects the first row in the right DataFrame whose вҖҳonвҖҷ key is greater than or equal to the leftвҖҷs key.\
>     \
> *   A вҖңnearestвҖқ search selects the last row in the right DataFrame whose value is nearest to the leftвҖҷs key. String keys are not currently supported for a nearest search.\
>     \
\
The default is вҖңbackwardвҖқ.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**other**\
\
Lazy DataFrame to join with.\
\
**left\_on**\
\
Join column of the left DataFrame.\
\
**right\_on**\
\
Join column of the right DataFrame.\
\
**on**\
\
Join column of both DataFrames. If set, `left_on` and `right_on` should be None.\
\
**by**\
\
join on these columns before doing asof join\
\
**by\_left**\
\
join on these columns before doing asof join\
\
**by\_right**\
\
join on these columns before doing asof join\
\
**strategy**{вҖҳbackwardвҖҷ, вҖҳforwardвҖҷ, вҖҳnearestвҖҷ}\
\
Join strategy.\
\
**suffix**\
\
Suffix to append to columns with a duplicate name.\
\
**tolerance**\
\
Numeric tolerance. By setting this the join will only be done if the near keys are within this distance. If an asof join is done on columns of dtype вҖңDateвҖқ, вҖңDatetimeвҖқ, вҖңDurationвҖқ or вҖңTimeвҖқ, use either a datetime.timedelta object or the following string language:\
\
> *   1ns (1 nanosecond)\
>     \
> *   1us (1 microsecond)\
>     \
> *   1ms (1 millisecond)\
>     \
> *   1s (1 second)\
>     \
> *   1m (1 minute)\
>     \
> *   1h (1 hour)\
>     \
> *   1d (1 calendar day)\
>     \
> *   1w (1 calendar week)\
>     \
> *   1mo (1 calendar month)\
>     \
> *   1q (1 calendar quarter)\
>     \
> *   1y (1 calendar year)\
>     \
> \
> Or combine them: вҖң3d12h4m25sвҖқ # 3 days, 12 hours, 4 minutes, and 25 seconds\
> \
> By вҖңcalendar dayвҖқ, we mean the corresponding time on the next day (which may not be 24 hours, due to daylight savings). Similarly for вҖңcalendar weekвҖқ, вҖңcalendar monthвҖқ, вҖңcalendar quarterвҖқ, and вҖңcalendar yearвҖқ.\
\
**allow\_parallel**\
\
Allow the physical plan to optionally evaluate the computation of both DataFrames up to the join in parallel.\
\
**force\_parallel**\
\
Force the physical plan to evaluate the computation of both DataFrames up to the join in parallel.\
\
**coalesce**\
\
Coalescing behavior (merging of `on` / `left_on` / `right_on` columns):\
\
*   True: -> Always coalesce join columns.\
    \
*   False: -> Never coalesce join columns.\
    \
\
Note that joining on any other expressions than `col` will turn off coalescing.\
\
**allow\_exact\_matches**\
\
Whether exact matches are valid join predicates.\
\
*   If True, allow matching with the same `on` value\
    \
    (i.e. less-than-or-equal-to / greater-than-or-equal-to)\
    \
*   If False, donвҖҷt match the same `on` value\
    \
    (i.e., strictly less-than / strictly greater-than).\
    \
\
**check\_sortedness**\
\
Check the sortedness of the asof keys. If the keys are not sorted Polars will error, or in case of вҖҳbyвҖҷ argument raise a warning. This might become a hard error in the future.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> from datetime import date\
\>>> gdp \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "date": pl.date\_range(\
...             date(2016, 1, 1),\
...             date(2020, 1, 1),\
...             "1y",\
...             eager\=True,\
...         ),\
...         "gdp": \[4164, 4411, 4566, 4696, 4827\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> gdp\
shape: (5, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ gdp  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---        в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2016-01-01 в”Ҷ 4164 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2017-01-01 в”Ҷ 4411 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2018-01-01 в”Ҷ 4566 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2020-01-01 в”Ҷ 4827 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
\>>> population \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "date": \[date(2016, 3, 1), date(2018, 8, 1), date(2019, 1, 1)\],\
...         "population": \[82.19, 82.66, 83.12\],\
...     }\
... ).sort("date")\
\>>> population\
shape: (3, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ population в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ f64        в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 82.19      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 82.66      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 83.12      в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Note how the dates donвҖҷt quite match. If we join them using `join_asof` and `strategy='backward'`, then each date from `population` which doesnвҖҷt have an exact match is matched with the closest earlier date from `gdp`:\
\
\>>> population.join\_asof(gdp, on\="date", strategy\="backward")\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ population в”Ҷ gdp  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ f64        в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 82.19      в”Ҷ 4164 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 82.66      в”Ҷ 4566 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 83.12      в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Note how:\
\
*   date `2016-03-01` from `population` is matched with `2016-01-01` from `gdp`;\
    \
*   date `2018-08-01` from `population` is matched with `2018-01-01` from `gdp`.\
    \
\
You can verify this by passing `coalesce=False`:\
\
\>>> population.join\_asof(gdp, on\="date", strategy\="backward", coalesce\=False)\
shape: (3, 4)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ population в”Ҷ date\_right в”Ҷ gdp  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ f64        в”Ҷ date       в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 82.19      в”Ҷ 2016-01-01 в”Ҷ 4164 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 82.66      в”Ҷ 2018-01-01 в”Ҷ 4566 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 83.12      в”Ҷ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
If we instead use `strategy='forward'`, then each date from `population` which doesnвҖҷt have an exact match is matched with the closest later date from `gdp`:\
\
\>>> population.join\_asof(gdp, on\="date", strategy\="forward")\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ population в”Ҷ gdp  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ f64        в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 82.19      в”Ҷ 4411 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 82.66      в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 83.12      в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Note how:\
\
*   date `2016-03-01` from `population` is matched with `2017-01-01` from `gdp`;\
    \
*   date `2018-08-01` from `population` is matched with `2019-01-01` from `gdp`.\
    \
\
Finally, `strategy='nearest'` gives us a mix of the two results above, as each date from `population` which doesnвҖҷt have an exact match is matched with the closest date from `gdp`, regardless of whether itвҖҷs earlier or later:\
\
\>>> population.join\_asof(gdp, on\="date", strategy\="nearest")\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ population в”Ҷ gdp  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ date       в”Ҷ f64        в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 82.19      в”Ҷ 4164 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 82.66      в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 83.12      в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Note how:\
\
*   date `2016-03-01` from `population` is matched with `2016-01-01` from `gdp`;\
    \
*   date `2018-08-01` from `population` is matched with `2019-01-01` from `gdp`.\
    \
\
They `by` argument allows joining on another column first, before the asof join. In this example we join by `country` first, then asof join by date, as above.\
\
\>>> gdp\_dates \= pl.date\_range(  \# fmt: skip\
...     date(2016, 1, 1), date(2020, 1, 1), "1y", eager\=True\
... )\
\>>> gdp2 \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "country": \["Germany"\] \* 5 + \["Netherlands"\] \* 5,\
...         "date": pl.concat(\[gdp\_dates, gdp\_dates\]),\
...         "gdp": \[4164, 4411, 4566, 4696, 4827, 784, 833, 914, 910, 909\],\
...     }\
... ).sort("country", "date")\
\>>>\
\>>> gdp2\
shape: (10, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ country     в”Ҷ date       в”Ҷ gdp  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---         в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str         в”Ҷ date       в”Ҷ i64  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2016-01-01 в”Ҷ 4164 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2017-01-01 в”Ҷ 4411 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2018-01-01 в”Ҷ 4566 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 4696 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2020-01-01 в”Ҷ 4827 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2016-01-01 в”Ҷ 784  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2017-01-01 в”Ҷ 833  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2018-01-01 в”Ҷ 914  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 910  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2020-01-01 в”Ҷ 909  в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> pop2 \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "country": \["Germany"\] \* 3 + \["Netherlands"\] \* 3,\
...         "date": \[\
...             date(2016, 3, 1),\
...             date(2018, 8, 1),\
...             date(2019, 1, 1),\
...             date(2016, 3, 1),\
...             date(2018, 8, 1),\
...             date(2019, 1, 1),\
...         \],\
...         "population": \[82.19, 82.66, 83.12, 17.11, 17.32, 17.40\],\
...     }\
... ).sort("country", "date")\
\>>>\
\>>> pop2\
shape: (6, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ country     в”Ҷ date       в”Ҷ population в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---         в”Ҷ ---        в”Ҷ ---        в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str         в”Ҷ date       в”Ҷ f64        в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 82.19      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 82.66      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Germany     в”Ҷ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 83.12      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2016-03-01 в”Ҷ 17.11      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2018-08-01 в”Ҷ 17.32      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Netherlands в”Ҷ 2019-01-01 в”Ҷ 17.4       в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\

в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
join\_where(\
\
_other: DataFrame_,\
\
_\*predicates: Expr | Iterable\[Expr\]_,\
\
_suffix: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= '\_right'_,\
\
) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L7767-L7847)\
\
Perform a join based on one or multiple (in)equality predicates.\
\
This performs an inner join, so only rows where all predicates are true are included in the result, and a row from either DataFrame may be included multiple times in the result.\
\
Note\
\
The row order of the input DataFrames is not preserved.\
\
Warning\
\
This functionality is experimental. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**other**\
\
DataFrame to join with.\
\
**\*predicates**\
\
(In)Equality condition to join the two tables on. When a column name occurs in both tables, the proper suffix must be applied in the predicate.\
\
**suffix**\
\
Suffix to append to columns with a duplicate name.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> east \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "id": \[100, 101, 102\],\
...         "dur": \[120, 140, 160\],\
...         "rev": \[12, 14, 16\],\
...         "cores": \[2, 8, 4\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> west \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "t\_id": \[404, 498, 676, 742\],\
...         "time": \[90, 130, 150, 170\],\
...         "cost": \[9, 13, 15, 16\],\
...         "cores": \[4, 2, 1, 4\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> east.join\_where(\
...     west,\
...     pl.col("dur") < pl.col("time"),\
...     pl.col("rev") < pl.col("cost"),\
... )\
shape: (5, 8)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ id  в”Ҷ dur в”Ҷ rev в”Ҷ cores в”Ҷ t\_id в”Ҷ time в”Ҷ cost в”Ҷ cores\_right в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---         в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64   в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ i64         в”Ӯ\

в”Ӯ 100 в”Ҷ 120 в”Ҷ 12  в”Ҷ 2     в”Ҷ 742  в”Ҷ 170  в”Ҷ 16   в”Ҷ 4           в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 101 в”Ҷ 140 в”Ҷ 14  в”Ҷ 8     в”Ҷ 676  в”Ҷ 150  в”Ҷ 15   в”Ҷ 1           в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 101 в”Ҷ 140 в”Ҷ 14  в”Ҷ 8     в”Ҷ 742  в”Ҷ 170  в”Ҷ 16   в”Ҷ 4           в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\

lazy() вҶ’ LazyFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L9495-L9530)\
\
Start a lazy query from this point. This returns a `LazyFrame` object.\
\
Operations on a `LazyFrame` are not executed until this is triggered by calling one of:\
\
*   [`.collect()`](../lazyframe/api/polars.LazyFrame.collect.html#polars.LazyFrame.collect "polars.LazyFrame.collect")\
    \
    (run on all data)\
    \
*   [`.explain()`](../lazyframe/api/polars.LazyFrame.explain.html#polars.LazyFrame.explain "polars.LazyFrame.explain")\
    \
    (print the query plan)\
    \
*   [`.show_graph()`](../lazyframe/api/polars.LazyFrame.show_graph.html#polars.LazyFrame.show_graph "polars.LazyFrame.show_graph")\
    \
    (show the query plan as graphviz graph)\
    \
*   [`.collect_schema()`](../lazyframe/api/polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema.html#polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema "polars.LazyFrame.collect_schema")\
    \
    (return the final frame schema)\
    \
\
Lazy operations are recommended because they allow for query optimization and additional parallelism.\
\
Returns:\
\
LazyFrame\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "a": \[None, 2, 3, 4\],\
...         "b": \[0.5, None, 2.5, 13\],\
...         "c": \[True, True, False, None\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.lazy()  \
<LazyFrame at ...>\
\

\

...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3, 4, 5\],\
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8, 9, 10\],\

в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\

в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
map\_rows(\
\
_function: Callable\[\[[tuple](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#tuple "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[Any, ...\]\], Any\]_,\
\
_return\_dtype: PolarsDataType | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_\*_,\
\
_inference\_size: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= 256_,\
\
) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L7849-L7949)\
\
Apply a custom/user-defined function (UDF) over the rows of the DataFrame.\
\
Warning\
\
This method is much slower than the native expressions API. Only use it if you cannot implement your logic otherwise.\
\
The UDF will receive each row as a tuple of values: `udf(row)`.\
\
Implementing logic using a Python function is almost always _significantly_ slower and more memory intensive than implementing the same logic using the native expression API because:\
\
*   The native expression engine runs in Rust; UDFs run in Python.\
    \
*   Use of Python UDFs forces the DataFrame to be materialized in memory.\
    \
*   Polars-native expressions can be parallelised (UDFs typically cannot).\
    \
*   Polars-native expressions can be logically optimised (UDFs cannot).\
    \
\
Wherever possible you should strongly prefer the native expression API to achieve the best performance.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**function**\
\
Custom function or lambda.\
\
**return\_dtype**\
\
Output type of the operation. If none given, Polars tries to infer the type.\
\
**inference\_size**\
\
Only used in the case when the custom function returns rows. This uses the first `n` rows to determine the output schema.\
\
Notes\
\
*   The frame-level `map_rows` cannot track column names (as the UDF is a black-box that may arbitrarily drop, rearrange, transform, or add new columns); if you want to apply a UDF such that column names are preserved, you should use the expression-level `map_elements` syntax instead.\
    \
*   If your function is expensive and you donвҖҷt want it to be called more than once for a given input, consider applying an `@lru_cache` decorator to it. If your data is suitable you may achieve _significant_ speedups.\
    \
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame({"foo": \[1, 2, 3\], "bar": \[\-1, 5, 8\]})\
\
Return a DataFrame by mapping each row to a tuple:\
\
\>>> df.map\_rows(lambda t: (t\[0\] \* 2, t\[1\] \* 3))\
shape: (3, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ column\_0 в”Ҷ column\_1 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---      в”Ҷ ---      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64      в”Ҷ i64      в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2        в”Ҷ -3       в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 4        в”Ҷ 15       в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 6        в”Ҷ 24       в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
However, it is much better to implement this with a native expression:\
\
\>>> df.select(\
...     pl.col("foo") \* 2,\
...     pl.col("bar") \* 3,\
... )  \
\
Return a DataFrame with a single column by mapping each row to a scalar:\
\
\>>> df.map\_rows(lambda t: (t\[0\] \* 2 + t\[1\]))\
shape: (3, 1)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ map в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 9   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 14  в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
In this case it is better to use the following native expression:\
\
\>>> df.select(pl.col("foo") \* 2 + pl.col("bar"))  \
\

\
melt(\
\
_id\_vars: ColumnNameOrSelector | Sequence\[ColumnNameOrSelector\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_value\_vars: ColumnNameOrSelector | Sequence\[ColumnNameOrSelector\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_variable\_name: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_value\_name: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L11847-L11888)\
\
Unpivot a DataFrame from wide to long format.\
\
Optionally leaves identifiers set.\
\
This function is useful to massage a DataFrame into a format where one or more columns are identifier variables (id\_vars) while all other columns, considered measured variables (value\_vars), are вҖңunpivotedвҖқ to the row axis leaving just two non-identifier columns, вҖҳvariableвҖҷ and вҖҳvalueвҖҷ.\
\
Deprecated since version 1.0.0: Please use [`unpivot()`](api/polars.DataFrame.unpivot.html#polars.DataFrame.unpivot "polars.DataFrame.unpivot")\
 instead.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**id\_vars**\
\
Column(s) or selector(s) to use as identifier variables.\
\
**value\_vars**\
\
Column(s) or selector(s) to use as values variables; if `value_vars` is empty all columns that are not in `id_vars` will be used.\
\
**variable\_name**\
\
Name to give to the `variable` column. Defaults to вҖңvariableвҖқ\
\
**value\_name**\
\
Name to give to the `value` column. Defaults to вҖңvalueвҖқ\
\
merge\_sorted(\
\
_other: DataFrame_,\
\
_key: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
_,\
\
) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L11574-L11646)\
\
Take two sorted DataFrames and merge them by the sorted key.\
\
The output of this operation will also be sorted. It is the callers responsibility that the frames are sorted in ascending order by that key otherwise the output will not make sense.\
\
The schemas of both DataFrames must be equal.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**other**\
\
Other DataFrame that must be merged\
\
**key**\
\
Key that is sorted.\
\
Notes\
\
No guarantee is given over the output row order when the key is equal between the both dataframes.\
\
The key must be sorted in ascending order.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df0 \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {"name": \["steve", "elise", "bob"\], "age": \[42, 44, 18\]}\
... ).sort("age")\
\>>> df0\
shape: (3, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ name  в”Ҷ age в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---   в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str   в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ bob   в”Ҷ 18  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ steve в”Ҷ 42  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ elise в”Ҷ 44  в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> df1 \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {"name": \["anna", "megan", "steve", "thomas"\], "age": \[21, 33, 42, 20\]}\
... ).sort("age")\
\>>> df1\
shape: (4, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ name   в”Ҷ age в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---    в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str    в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ thomas в”Ҷ 20  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ anna   в”Ҷ 21  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ megan  в”Ҷ 33  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ steve  в”Ҷ 42  в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> df0.merge\_sorted(df1, key\="age")\
shape: (7, 2)\

n\_chunks(_strategy: Literal\['first', 'all'\] \= 'first'_) вҶ’ [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [list](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#list "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[[int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
\][\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L9847-L9881)\
\
Get number of chunks used by the ChunkedArrays of this DataFrame.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**strategy**{вҖҳfirstвҖҷ, вҖҳallвҖҷ}\
\
Return the number of chunks of the вҖҳfirstвҖҷ column, or вҖҳallвҖҷ columns in this DataFrame.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "a": \[1, 2, 3, 4\],\
...         "b": \[0.5, 4, 10, 13\],\
...         "c": \[True, True, False, True\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.n\_chunks()\

\>>> df.n\_chunks(strategy\="all")\
\[1, 1, 1\]\
\
n\_unique(_subset: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr | Sequence\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | Expr\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_) вҶ’ [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L10455-L10523)\
\
Return the number of unique rows, or the number of unique row-subsets.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**subset**\
\
One or more columns/expressions that define what to count; omit to return the count of unique rows.\
\
Notes\
\
This method operates at the `DataFrame` level; to operate on subsets at the expression level you can make use of struct-packing instead, for example:\
\
\>>> expr\_unique\_subset \= pl.struct("a", "b").n\_unique()\
\
If instead you want to count the number of unique values per-column, you can also use expression-level syntax to return a new frame containing that result:\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     \[\[1, 2, 3\], \[1, 2, 4\]\], schema\=\["a", "b", "c"\], orient\="row"\
... )\
\>>> df\_nunique \= df.select(pl.all().n\_unique())\
\
In aggregate context there is also an equivalent method for returning the unique values per-group:\
\
\>>> df\_agg\_nunique \= df.group\_by("a").n\_unique()\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "a": \[1, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5\],\
...         "b": \[0.5, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 3.0, 3.0\],\
...         "c": \[True, True, True, False, True, True\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.n\_unique()\
5\
\
Simple columns subset.\
\
\>>> df.n\_unique(subset\=\["b", "c"\])\
4\
\
Expression subset.\
\
\>>> df.n\_unique(\
...     subset\=\[\
...         (pl.col("a") // 2),\
...         (pl.col("c") | (pl.col("b") \>= 2)),\
...     \],\
... )\
3\
\
null\_count() вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L10566-L10589)\

в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
partition\_by(\
\
_by: ColumnNameOrSelector | Sequence\[ColumnNameOrSelector\]_,\
\
_\*more\_by: ColumnNameOrSelector_,\
\
_maintain\_order: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_include\_key: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_as\_dict: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= False_,\
\
) вҶ’ [list](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#list "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[DataFrame\] | [dict](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#dict "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[[tuple](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#tuple "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[[object](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#object "(in Python v3.13)")\
, ...\], DataFrame\][\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L9194-L9346)\
\
Group by the given columns and return the groups as separate dataframes.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**by**\
\
Column name(s) or selector(s) to group by.\
\
**\*more\_by**\
\
Additional names of columns to group by, specified as positional arguments.\
\
**maintain\_order**\
\
Ensure that the order of the groups is consistent with the input data. This is slower than a default partition by operation.\
\
**include\_key**\
\
Include the columns used to partition the DataFrame in the output.\
\
**as\_dict**\
\
Return a dictionary instead of a list. The dictionary keys are tuples of the distinct group values that identify each group.\
\
Examples\
\
Pass a single column name to partition by that column.\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "a": \["a", "b", "a", "b", "c"\],\
...         "b": \[1, 2, 1, 3, 3\],\
...         "c": \[5, 4, 3, 2, 1\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.partition\_by("a")  \
\[shape: (2, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 5   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ,\
shape: (2, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ\

\
\>>> import polars.selectors as cs\

в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 5   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ,\
('b',): shape: (2, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ,\
('c',): shape: (1, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ}\
\
pipe(\
\
_function: Callable\[Concatenate\[DataFrame, P\], T\]_,\
\
_\*args: P.args_,\
\
_\*\*kwargs: P.kwargs_,\
\
) вҶ’ T[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L6286-L6351)\
\
Offers a structured way to apply a sequence of user-defined functions (UDFs).\
\
Parameters:\
\
**function**\
\
Callable; will receive the frame as the first parameter, followed by any given args/kwargs.\
\
**\*args**\
\
Arguments to pass to the UDF.\
\
**\*\*kwargs**\
\
Keyword arguments to pass to the UDF.\
\
Notes\
\
It is recommended to use LazyFrame when piping operations, in order to fully take advantage of query optimization and parallelization. See [`df.lazy()`](api/polars.DataFrame.lazy.html#polars.DataFrame.lazy "polars.DataFrame.lazy")\
.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> def cast\_str\_to\_int(data, col\_name):\
...     return data.with\_columns(pl.col(col\_name).cast(pl.Int64))\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame({"a": \[1, 2, 3, 4\], "b": \["10", "20", "30", "40"\]})\
\>>> df.pipe(cast\_str\_to\_int, col\_name\="b")\
shape: (4, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 10  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 20  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 30  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 4   в”Ҷ 40  в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame({"b": \[1, 2\], "a": \[3, 4\]})\
\>>> df\
shape: (2, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 4   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> df.pipe(lambda tdf: tdf.select(sorted(tdf.columns)))\
shape: (2, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 4   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
pivot(\
\
_on: ColumnNameOrSelector | Sequence\[ColumnNameOrSelector\]_,\
\
_\*_,\
\
_index: ColumnNameOrSelector | Sequence\[ColumnNameOrSelector\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_values: ColumnNameOrSelector | Sequence\[ColumnNameOrSelector\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_aggregate\_function: PivotAgg | Expr | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_maintain\_order: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
_sort\_columns: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= False_,\
\
_separator: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= '\_'_,\
\
) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L8731-L8962)\
\
Create a spreadsheet-style pivot table as a DataFrame.\
\
Only available in eager mode. See вҖңExamplesвҖқ section below for how to do a вҖңlazy pivotвҖқ if you know the unique column values in advance.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**on**\
\
The column(s) whose values will be used as the new columns of the output DataFrame.\
\
**index**\
\
The column(s) that remain from the input to the output. The output DataFrame will have one row for each unique combination of the `index`вҖҷs values. If None, all remaining columns not specified on `on` and `values` will be used. At least one of `index` and `values` must be specified.\
\
**values**\
\
The existing column(s) of values which will be moved under the new columns from index. If an aggregation is specified, these are the values on which the aggregation will be computed. If None, all remaining columns not specified on `on` and `index` will be used. At least one of `index` and `values` must be specified.\
\
**aggregate\_function**\
\
Choose from:\
\
*   None: no aggregation takes place, will raise error if multiple values are in group.\
    \
*   A predefined aggregate function string, one of {вҖҳminвҖҷ, вҖҳmaxвҖҷ, вҖҳfirstвҖҷ, вҖҳlastвҖҷ, вҖҳsumвҖҷ, вҖҳmeanвҖҷ, вҖҳmedianвҖҷ, вҖҳlenвҖҷ}\
    \
*   An expression to do the aggregation.\
    \
\
**maintain\_order**\
\
Ensure the values of `index` are sorted by discovery order.\
\
**sort\_columns**\
\
Sort the transposed columns by name. Default is by order of discovery.\
\
**separator**\
\
Used as separator/delimiter in generated column names in case of multiple `values` columns.\
\
Returns:\
\
DataFrame\
\
Notes\
\
In some other frameworks, you might know this operation as `pivot_wider`.\
\
Examples\
\
You can use `pivot` to reshape a dataframe from вҖңlongвҖқ to вҖңwideвҖқ format.\
\
For example, suppose we have a dataframe of test scores achieved by some students, where each row represents a distinct test.\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "name": \["Cady", "Cady", "Karen", "Karen"\],\
...         "subject": \["maths", "physics", "maths", "physics"\],\
...         "test\_1": \[98, 99, 61, 58\],\
...         "test\_2": \[100, 100, 60, 60\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df\
shape: (4, 4)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ name  в”Ҷ subject в”Ҷ test\_1 в”Ҷ test\_2 в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---   в”Ҷ ---     в”Ҷ ---    в”Ҷ ---    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str   в”Ҷ str     в”Ҷ i64    в”Ҷ i64    в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ Cady  в”Ҷ maths   в”Ҷ 98     в”Ҷ 100    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Cady  в”Ҷ physics в”Ҷ 99     в”Ҷ 100    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Karen в”Ҷ maths   в”Ҷ 61     в”Ҷ 60     в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Karen в”Ҷ physics в”Ҷ 58     в”Ҷ 60     в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Using `pivot`, we can reshape so we have one row per student, with different subjects as columns, and their `test_1` scores as values:\
\
\>>> df.pivot("subject", index\="name", values\="test\_1")\
shape: (2, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ name  в”Ҷ maths в”Ҷ physics в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---   в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---     в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str   в”Ҷ i64   в”Ҷ i64     в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ Cady  в”Ҷ 98    в”Ҷ 99      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Karen в”Ҷ 61    в”Ҷ 58      в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
You can use selectors too - here we include all test scores in the pivoted table:\
\
\>>> import polars.selectors as cs\
\>>> df.pivot("subject", values\=cs.starts\_with("test"))\
shape: (2, 5)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ name  в”Ҷ test\_1\_maths в”Ҷ test\_1\_physics в”Ҷ test\_2\_maths в”Ҷ test\_2\_physics в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---   в”Ҷ ---          в”Ҷ ---            в”Ҷ ---          в”Ҷ ---            в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str   в”Ҷ i64          в”Ҷ i64            в”Ҷ i64          в”Ҷ i64            в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ Cady  в”Ҷ 98           в”Ҷ 99             в”Ҷ 100          в”Ҷ 100            в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ Karen в”Ҷ 61           в”Ҷ 58             в”Ҷ 60           в”Ҷ 60             в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
If you end up with multiple values per cell, you can specify how to aggregate them with `aggregate_function`:\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "ix": \[1, 1, 2, 2, 1, 2\],\
...         "col": \["a", "a", "a", "a", "b", "b"\],\
...         "foo": \[0, 1, 2, 2, 7, 1\],\
...         "bar": \[0, 2, 0, 0, 9, 4\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.pivot("col", index\="ix", aggregate\_function\="sum")\
shape: (2, 5)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ ix  в”Ҷ foo\_a в”Ҷ foo\_b в”Ҷ bar\_a в”Ҷ bar\_b в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64   в”Ҷ i64   в”Ҷ i64   в”Ҷ i64   в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 1     в”Ҷ 7     в”Ҷ 2     в”Ҷ 9     в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 4     в”Ҷ 1     в”Ҷ 0     в”Ҷ 4     в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
You can also pass a custom aggregation function using [`polars.element()`](../expressions/api/polars.element.html#polars.element "polars.element")\
:\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "col1": \["a", "a", "a", "b", "b", "b"\],\
...         "col2": \["x", "x", "x", "x", "y", "y"\],\
...         "col3": \[6, 7, 3, 2, 5, 7\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.pivot(\
...     "col2",\
...     index\="col1",\
...     values\="col3",\
...     aggregate\_function\=pl.element().tanh().mean(),\
... )\
shape: (2, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ col1 в”Ҷ x        в”Ҷ y        в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---      в”Ҷ ---      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str  в”Ҷ f64      в”Ҷ f64      в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ a    в”Ҷ 0.998347 в”Ҷ null     в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ b    в”Ҷ 0.964028 в”Ҷ 0.999954 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Note that `pivot` is only available in eager mode. If you know the unique column values in advance, you can use [`polars.LazyFrame.group_by()`](../lazyframe/api/polars.LazyFrame.group_by.html#polars.LazyFrame.group_by "polars.LazyFrame.group_by")\
 to get the same result as above in lazy mode:\
\
\>>> index \= pl.col("col1")\
\>>> on \= pl.col("col2")\
\>>> values \= pl.col("col3")\
\>>> unique\_column\_values \= \["x", "y"\]\
\>>> aggregate\_function \= lambda col: col.tanh().mean()\
\>>> df.lazy().group\_by(index).agg(\
...     aggregate\_function(values.filter(on \== value)).alias(value)\
...     for value in unique\_column\_values\
... ).collect()  \
shape: (2, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ col1 в”Ҷ x        в”Ҷ y        в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---      в”Ҷ ---      в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str  в”Ҷ f64      в”Ҷ f64      в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ a    в”Ҷ 0.998347 в”Ҷ null     в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ b    в”Ҷ 0.964028 в”Ҷ 0.999954 в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
_property_ plot_: DataFramePlot_[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L598-L693)\
\
Create a plot namespace.\
\
Warning\
\
This functionality is currently considered **unstable**. It may be changed at any point without it being considered a breaking change.\
\
Changed in version 1.6.0: In prior versions of Polars, HvPlot was the plotting backend. If you would like to restore the previous plotting functionality, all you need to do is add `import hvplot.polars` at the top of your script and replace `df.plot` with `df.hvplot`.\
\
Polars does not implement plotting logic itself, but instead defers to [Altair](https://altair-viz.github.io/)\
:\
\
*   `df.plot.line(**kwargs)` is shorthand for `alt.Chart(df).mark_line(tooltip=True).encode(**kwargs).interactive()`\
    \
*   `df.plot.point(**kwargs)` is shorthand for `alt.Chart(df).mark_point(tooltip=True).encode(**kwargs).interactive()` (and `plot.scatter` is provided as an alias)\
    \
*   `df.plot.bar(**kwargs)` is shorthand for `alt.Chart(df).mark_bar(tooltip=True).encode(**kwargs).interactive()`\
    \
*   for any other attribute `attr`, `df.plot.attr(**kwargs)` is shorthand for `alt.Chart(df).mark_attr(tooltip=True).encode(**kwargs).interactive()`\
    \
\
For configuration, we suggest reading [Chart Configuration](https://altair-viz.github.io/altair-tutorial/notebooks/08-Configuration.html)\
. For example, you can:\
\
*   Change the width/height/title with `.properties(width=500, height=350, title="My amazing plot")`.\
    \
*   Change the x-axis label rotation with `.configure_axisX(labelAngle=30)`.\
    \
*   Change the opacity of the points in your scatter plot with `.configure_point(opacity=.5)`.\
    \
\
Examples\
\
Scatter plot:\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "length": \[1, 4, 6\],\
...         "width": \[4, 5, 6\],\
...         "species": \["setosa", "setosa", "versicolor"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.plot.point(x\="length", y\="width", color\="species")  \
\
Set the x-axis title by using `altair.X`:\
\
\>>> import altair as alt\
\>>> df.plot.point(\
...     x\=alt.X("length", title\="Length"), y\="width", color\="species"\
... )  \
\
Line plot:\
\
\>>> from datetime import date\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "date": \[date(2020, 1, 2), date(2020, 1, 3), date(2020, 1, 4)\] \* 2,\
...         "price": \[1, 4, 6, 1, 5, 2\],\
...         "stock": \["a", "a", "a", "b", "b", "b"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.plot.line(x\="date", y\="price", color\="stock")  \
\
Bar plot:\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "day": \["Mon", "Tue", "Wed", "Thu", "Fri", "Sat", "Sun"\] \* 2,\
...         "group": \["a"\] \* 7 + \["b"\] \* 7,\
...         "value": \[1, 3, 2, 4, 5, 6, 1, 1, 3, 2, 4, 5, 1, 2\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.plot.bar(\
...     x\="day", y\="value", color\="day", column\="group"\
... )  \
\
Or, to make a stacked version of the plot above:\
\
\>>> df.plot.bar(x\="day", y\="value", color\="group")  \
\
product() вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L10219-L10250)\

...     }\
... )\
\
\>>> df.product()\

quantile(\
\
_quantile: [float](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#float "(in Python v3.13)")\
_,\
\
_interpolation: RollingInterpolationMethod \= 'nearest'_,\
\
) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L10252-L10284)\
\
Aggregate the columns of this DataFrame to their quantile value.\
\
Parameters:\
\

\
Quantile between 0.0 and 1.0.\
\
**interpolation**{вҖҳnearestвҖҷ, вҖҳhigherвҖҷ, вҖҳlowerвҖҷ, вҖҳmidpointвҖҷ, вҖҳlinearвҖҷ}\
\
Interpolation method.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],\
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8\],\
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.quantile(0.5, "nearest")\

rechunk() вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L10557-L10564)\
\
Rechunk the data in this DataFrame to a contiguous allocation.\

This will make sure all subsequent operations have optimal and predictable performance.\

remove(\
\
_\*predicates: IntoExprColumn | Iterable\[IntoExprColumn\] | [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | [list](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#list "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[[bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] | np.ndarray\[Any, Any\]_,\
\
_\*\*constraints: Any_,\
\
) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L5103-L5240)\
\
Remove rows, dropping those that match the given predicate expression(s).\
\
The original order of the remaining rows is preserved.\
\
Rows where the filter predicate does not evaluate to True are retained (this includes rows where the predicate evaluates as `null`).\
\
Parameters:\
\
**predicates**\
\
Expression that evaluates to a boolean Series.\
\
**constraints**\
\
Column filters; use `name = value` to filter columns using the supplied value. Each constraint behaves the same as `pl.col(name).eq(value)`, and is implicitly joined with the other filter conditions using `&`.\
\
See also\
\
[`filter`](api/polars.DataFrame.filter.html#polars.DataFrame.filter "polars.DataFrame.filter")\
\
Notes\
\
If you are transitioning from Pandas, and performing filter operations based on the comparison of two or more columns, please note that in Polars any comparison involving `null` values will result in a `null` result, _not_ boolean True or False. As a result, these rows will not be removed. Ensure that null values are handled appropriately to avoid unexpected behaviour (see examples below).\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "foo": \[2, 3, None, 4, 0\],\
...         "bar": \[5, 6, None, None, 0\],\
...         "ham": \["a", "b", None, "c", "d"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\
Remove rows matching a condition:\
\
\>>> df.remove(pl.col("bar") \>= 5)\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 4    в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ c    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 0    в”Ҷ 0    в”Ҷ d    в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Discard rows based on multiple conditions, combined with and/or operators:\
\
\>>> df.remove(\
...     (pl.col("foo") \>= 0) & (pl.col("bar") \>= 0),\
... )\
shape: (2, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 4    в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ c    в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
\>>> df.remove(\
...     (pl.col("foo") \>= 0) | (pl.col("bar") \>= 0),\
... )\
shape: (1, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Provide multiple constraints using `*args` syntax:\
\
\>>> df.remove(\
...     pl.col("ham").is\_not\_null(),\
...     pl.col("bar") \>= 0,\
... )\
shape: (2, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 4    в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ c    в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Provide constraints(s) using `**kwargs` syntax:\
\
\>>> df.remove(foo\=0, bar\=0)\
shape: (4, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ foo  в”Ҷ bar  в”Ҷ ham  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ҷ ---  в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64  в”Ҷ i64  в”Ҷ str  в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 2    в”Ҷ 5    в”Ҷ a    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 3    в”Ҷ 6    в”Ҷ b    в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ null в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ null в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 4    в”Ҷ null в”Ҷ c    в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
Remove rows by comparing two columns against each other:\
\
\>>> df.remove(\
...     pl.col("foo").ne\_missing(pl.col("bar")),\
... )\
shape: (2, 3)\

rename(\
\
_mapping: [dict](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#dict "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
, [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
\] | [Callable](https://docs.python.org/3/library/typing.html#typing.Callable "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
\], [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
\]_,\
\
_\*_,\
\
_strict: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= True_,\
\
) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L4816-L4860)\
\
Rename column names.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**mapping**\
\
Key value pairs that map from old name to new name, or a function that takes the old name as input and returns the new name.\
\
**strict**\
\
Validate that all column names exist in the current schema, and throw an exception if any do not. (Note that this parameter is a no-op when passing a function to `mapping`).\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {"foo": \[1, 2, 3\], "bar": \[6, 7, 8\], "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\]}\
... )\
\>>> df.rename({"foo": "apple"})\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ apple в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---   в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64   в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1     в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2     в”Ҷ 7   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 3     в”Ҷ 8   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\>>> df.rename(lambda column\_name: "c" + column\_name\[1:\])\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ coo в”Ҷ car в”Ҷ cam в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ\

replace\_column(_index: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")\
_, _column: Series_) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L5478-L5516)\
\
Replace a column at an index location.\
\
This operation is in place.\
\
Parameters:\
\
**index**\
\
Column index.\
\
**column**\
\
Series that will replace the column.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],\
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8\],\
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> s \= pl.Series("apple", \[10, 20, 30\])\
\>>> df.replace\_column(0, s)\
shape: (3, 3)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ apple в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ ---   в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ i64   в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ 10    в”Ҷ 6   в”Ҷ a   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 20    в”Ҷ 7   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ 30    в”Ҷ 8   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
reverse() вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L4790-L4814)\
\
Reverse the DataFrame.\
\
Examples\
\
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(\
...     {\
...         "key": \["a", "b", "c"\],\
...         "val": \[1, 2, 3\],\
...     }\
... )\
\>>> df.reverse()\
shape: (3, 2)\
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\
в”Ӯ key в”Ҷ val в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ str в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ\
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў\
в”Ӯ c   в”Ҷ 3   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ b   в”Ҷ 2   в”Ӯ\
в”Ӯ a   в”Ҷ 1   в”Ӯ\
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ\
\
rolling(\
\
_index\_column: IntoExpr_,\
\
_\*_,\
\
_period: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | timedelta_,\
\
_offset: [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
 | timedelta | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
_closed: ClosedInterval \= 'right'_,\
\
_group\_by: IntoExpr | Iterable\[IntoExpr\] | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")\
 \= None_,\
\
) вҶ’ RollingGroupBy[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L6616-L6768)\
\
Create rolling groups based on a temporal or integer column.\
\
Different from a `group_by_dynamic` the windows are now determined by the individual values and are not of constant intervals. For constant intervals use [`DataFrame.group_by_dynamic()`](api/polars.DataFrame.group_by_dynamic.html#polars.DataFrame.group_by_dynamic "polars.DataFrame.group_by_dynamic")\
.\
\
If you have a time series `<t_0, t_1, ..., t_n>`, then by default the windows created will be\
\
> *   (t\_0 - period, t\_0\]\
>     \
> *   (t\_1 - period, t\_1\]\
>     \
> *   вҖҰ\
>     \
> *   (t\_n - period, t\_n\]\
>     \
\
whereas if you pass a non-default `offset`, then the windows will be\
\
> *   (t\_0 + offset, t\_0 + offset + period\]
>     
> *   (t\_1 + offset, t\_1 + offset + period\]
>     
> *   вҖҰ
>     
> *   (t\_n + offset, t\_n + offset + period\]
>     

The `period` and `offset` arguments are created either from a timedelta, or by using the following string language:

*   1ns (1 nanosecond)
    
*   1us (1 microsecond)
    
*   1ms (1 millisecond)
    
*   1s (1 second)
    
*   1m (1 minute)
    
*   1h (1 hour)
    
*   1d (1 calendar day)
    
*   1w (1 calendar week)
    
*   1mo (1 calendar month)
    
*   1q (1 calendar quarter)
    
*   1y (1 calendar year)
    
*   1i (1 index count)
    

Or combine them: вҖң3d12h4m25sвҖқ # 3 days, 12 hours, 4 minutes, and 25 seconds

By вҖңcalendar dayвҖқ, we mean the corresponding time on the next day (which may not be 24 hours, due to daylight savings). Similarly for вҖңcalendar weekвҖқ, вҖңcalendar monthвҖқ, вҖңcalendar quarterвҖқ, and вҖңcalendar yearвҖқ.

Parameters:

**index\_column**

Column used to group based on the time window. Often of type Date/Datetime. This column must be sorted in ascending order (or, if `group_by` is specified, then it must be sorted in ascending order within each group).

In case of a rolling operation on indices, dtype needs to be one of {UInt32, UInt64, Int32, Int64}. Note that the first three get temporarily cast to Int64, so if performance matters use an Int64 column.

**period**

Length of the window - must be non-negative.

**offset**

Offset of the window. Default is `-period`.

**closed**{вҖҳrightвҖҷ, вҖҳleftвҖҷ, вҖҳbothвҖҷ, вҖҳnoneвҖҷ}

Define which sides of the temporal interval are closed (inclusive).

**group\_by**

Also group by this column/these columns

Returns:

RollingGroupBy

Object you can call `.agg` on to aggregate by groups, the result of which will be sorted by `index_column` (but note that if `group_by` columns are passed, it will only be sorted within each group).

See also

[`group_by_dynamic`](api/polars.DataFrame.group_by_dynamic.html#polars.DataFrame.group_by_dynamic "polars.DataFrame.group_by_dynamic")

Examples

\>>> dates \= \[\
...     "2020-01-01 13:45:48",\
...     "2020-01-01 16:42:13",\
...     "2020-01-01 16:45:09",\
...     "2020-01-02 18:12:48",\
...     "2020-01-03 19:45:32",\
...     "2020-01-08 23:16:43",\
... \]
\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame({"dt": dates, "a": \[3, 7, 5, 9, 2, 1\]}).with\_columns(
...     pl.col("dt").str.strptime(pl.Datetime).set\_sorted()
... )
\>>> out \= df.rolling(index\_column\="dt", period\="2d").agg(
...     \[\
...         pl.sum("a").alias("sum\_a"),\
...         pl.min("a").alias("min\_a"),\
...         pl.max("a").alias("max\_a"),\
...     \]
... )
\>>> assert out\["sum\_a"\].to\_list() \== \[3, 10, 15, 24, 11, 1\]
\>>> assert out\["max\_a"\].to\_list() \== \[3, 7, 7, 9, 9, 1\]
\>>> assert out\["min\_a"\].to\_list() \== \[3, 3, 3, 3, 2, 1\]
\>>> out
shape: (6, 4)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ dt                  в”Ҷ sum\_a в”Ҷ min\_a в”Ҷ max\_a в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---                 в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---   в”Ҷ ---   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ datetime\[Ојs\]        в”Ҷ i64   в”Ҷ i64   в”Ҷ i64   в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 2020-01-01 13:45:48 в”Ҷ 3     в”Ҷ 3     в”Ҷ 3     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2020-01-01 16:42:13 в”Ҷ 10    в”Ҷ 3     в”Ҷ 7     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2020-01-01 16:45:09 в”Ҷ 15    в”Ҷ 3     в”Ҷ 7     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2020-01-02 18:12:48 в”Ҷ 24    в”Ҷ 3     в”Ҷ 9     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2020-01-03 19:45:32 в”Ҷ 11    в”Ҷ 2     в”Ҷ 9     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2020-01-08 23:16:43 в”Ҷ 1     в”Ҷ 1     в”Ҷ 1     в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

If you use an index count in `period` or `offset`, then itвҖҷs based on the values in `index_column`:

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame({"int": \[0, 4, 5, 6, 8\], "value": \[1, 4, 2, 4, 1\]})
\>>> df.rolling("int", period\="3i").agg(pl.col("int").alias("aggregated"))
shape: (5, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ int в”Ҷ aggregated в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ ---        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ list\[i64\]  в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 0   в”Ҷ \[0\]        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 4   в”Ҷ \[4\]        в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 5   в”Ҷ \[4, 5\]     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 6   в”Ҷ \[4, 5, 6\]  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 8   в”Ҷ \[6, 8\]     в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

If you want the index count to be based on row number, then you may want to combine `rolling` with [`with_row_index()`](api/polars.DataFrame.with_row_index.html#polars.DataFrame.with_row_index "polars.DataFrame.with_row_index")
.

row(

_index: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_\*_,

_by\_predicate: Expr | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_named: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

) вҶ’ [tuple](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#tuple "(in Python v3.13)")
\[Any, ...\] | [dict](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#dict "(in Python v3.13)")
\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
, Any\][\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L10774-L10878)

Get the values of a single row, either by index or by predicate.

Parameters:

**index**

Row index.

**by\_predicate**

Select the row according to a given expression/predicate.

**named**

Return a dictionary instead of a tuple. The dictionary is a mapping of column name to row value. This is more expensive than returning a regular tuple, but allows for accessing values by column name.

Returns:

tuple (default) or dictionary of row values

Warning

You should NEVER use this method to iterate over a DataFrame; if you require row-iteration you should strongly prefer use of `iter_rows()` instead.

See also

[`iter_rows`](api/polars.DataFrame.iter_rows.html#polars.DataFrame.iter_rows "polars.DataFrame.iter_rows")

Row iterator over frame data (does not materialise all rows).

[`rows`](api/polars.DataFrame.rows.html#polars.DataFrame.rows "polars.DataFrame.rows")

Materialise all frame data as a list of rows (potentially expensive).

[`item`](api/polars.DataFrame.item.html#polars.DataFrame.item "polars.DataFrame.item")

Return dataframe element as a scalar.

Notes

The `index` and `by_predicate` params are mutually exclusive. Additionally, to ensure clarity, the `by_predicate` parameter must be supplied by keyword.

When using `by_predicate` it is an error condition if anything other than one row is returned; more than one row raises `TooManyRowsReturnedError`, and zero rows will raise `NoRowsReturnedError` (both inherit from `RowsError`).

Examples

Specify an index to return the row at the given index as a tuple.

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.row(2)
(3, 8, 'c')

Specify `named=True` to get a dictionary instead with a mapping of column names to row values.

\>>> df.row(2, named\=True)
{'foo': 3, 'bar': 8, 'ham': 'c'}

Use `by_predicate` to return the row that matches the given predicate.

\>>> df.row(by\_predicate\=(pl.col("ham") \== "b"))
(2, 7, 'b')

rows(

_\*_,

_named: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

) вҶ’ [list](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#list "(in Python v3.13)")
\[[tuple](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#tuple "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[[Any](https://docs.python.org/3/library/typing.html#typing.Any "(in Python v3.13)")\
, ...\]\] | [list](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#list "(in Python v3.13)")
\[[dict](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#dict "(in Python v3.13)")\
\[[str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")\
, [Any](https://docs.python.org/3/library/typing.html#typing.Any "(in Python v3.13)")\
\]\][\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L10886-L10949)

Returns all data in the DataFrame as a list of rows of python-native values.

By default, each row is returned as a tuple of values given in the same order as the frame columns. Setting `named=True` will return rows of dictionaries instead.

Parameters:

**named**

Return dictionaries instead of tuples. The dictionaries are a mapping of column name to row value. This is more expensive than returning a regular tuple, but allows for accessing values by column name.

Returns:

list of row value tuples (default), or list of dictionaries (if `named=True`).

Warning

Row-iteration is not optimal as the underlying data is stored in columnar form; where possible, prefer export via one of the dedicated export/output methods. You should also consider using `iter_rows` instead, to avoid materialising all the data at once; there is little performance difference between the two, but peak memory can be reduced if processing rows in batches.

See also

[`iter_rows`](api/polars.DataFrame.iter_rows.html#polars.DataFrame.iter_rows "polars.DataFrame.iter_rows")

Row iterator over frame data (does not materialise all rows).

[`rows_by_key`](api/polars.DataFrame.rows_by_key.html#polars.DataFrame.rows_by_key "polars.DataFrame.rows_by_key")

Materialises frame data as a key-indexed dictionary.

Notes

If you have `ns`\-precision temporal values you should be aware that Python natively only supports up to `Ојs`\-precision; `ns`\-precision values will be truncated to microseconds on conversion to Python. If this matters to your use-case you should export to a different format (such as Arrow or NumPy).

Examples

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "x": \["a", "b", "b", "a"\],
...         "y": \[1, 2, 3, 4\],
...         "z": \[0, 3, 6, 9\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.rows()
\[('a', 1, 0), ('b', 2, 3), ('b', 3, 6), ('a', 4, 9)\]
\>>> df.rows(named\=True)
\[{'x': 'a', 'y': 1, 'z': 0},\
 {'x': 'b', 'y': 2, 'z': 3},\
 {'x': 'b', 'y': 3, 'z': 6},\
 {'x': 'a', 'y': 4, 'z': 9}\]

rows\_by\_key(

_key: ColumnNameOrSelector | Sequence\[ColumnNameOrSelector\]_,

_\*_,

_named: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_include\_key: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_unique: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

) вҶ’ [dict](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#dict "(in Python v3.13)")
\[Any, Any\][\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L10991-L11117)

Returns all data as a dictionary of python-native values keyed by some column.

This method is like `rows`, but instead of returning rows in a flat list, rows are grouped by the values in the `key` column(s) and returned as a dictionary.

Note that this method should not be used in place of native operations, due to the high cost of materializing all frame data out into a dictionary; it should be used only when you need to move the values out into a Python data structure or other object that cannot operate directly with Polars/Arrow.

Parameters:

**key**

The column(s) to use as the key for the returned dictionary. If multiple columns are specified, the key will be a tuple of those values, otherwise it will be a string.

**named**

Return dictionary rows instead of tuples, mapping column name to row value.

**include\_key**

Include key values inline with the associated data (by default the key values are omitted as a memory/performance optimisation, as they can be reoconstructed from the key).

**unique**

Indicate that the key is unique; this will result in a 1:1 mapping from key to a single associated row. Note that if the key is _not_ actually unique the last row with the given key will be returned.

See also

[`rows`](api/polars.DataFrame.rows.html#polars.DataFrame.rows "polars.DataFrame.rows")

Materialize all frame data as a list of rows (potentially expensive).

[`iter_rows`](api/polars.DataFrame.iter_rows.html#polars.DataFrame.iter_rows "polars.DataFrame.iter_rows")

Row iterator over frame data (does not materialize all rows).

[`to_dict`](api/polars.DataFrame.to_dict.html#polars.DataFrame.to_dict "polars.DataFrame.to_dict")

Convert DataFrame to a dictionary mapping column name to values.

Notes

If you have `ns`\-precision temporal values you should be aware that Python natively only supports up to `Ојs`\-precision; `ns`\-precision values will be truncated to microseconds on conversion to Python. If this matters to your use-case you should export to a different format (such as Arrow or NumPy).

Examples

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "w": \["a", "b", "b", "a"\],
...         "x": \["q", "q", "q", "k"\],
...         "y": \[1.0, 2.5, 3.0, 4.5\],
...         "z": \[9, 8, 7, 6\],
...     }
... )

Group rows by the given key column(s):

\>>> df.rows\_by\_key(key\=\["w"\])
defaultdict(<class 'list'>,
    {'a': \[('q', 1.0, 9), ('k', 4.5, 6)\],
     'b': \[('q', 2.5, 8), ('q', 3.0, 7)\]})

Return the same row groupings as dictionaries:

\>>> df.rows\_by\_key(key\=\["w"\], named\=True)
defaultdict(<class 'list'>,
    {'a': \[{'x': 'q', 'y': 1.0, 'z': 9},\
           {'x': 'k', 'y': 4.5, 'z': 6}\],
     'b': \[{'x': 'q', 'y': 2.5, 'z': 8},\
           {'x': 'q', 'y': 3.0, 'z': 7}\]})

Return row groupings, assuming keys are unique:

\>>> df.rows\_by\_key(key\=\["z"\], unique\=True)
{9: ('a', 'q', 1.0),
 8: ('b', 'q', 2.5),
 7: ('b', 'q', 3.0),
 6: ('a', 'k', 4.5)}

Return row groupings as dictionaries, assuming keys are unique:

\>>> df.rows\_by\_key(key\=\["z"\], named\=True, unique\=True)
{9: {'w': 'a', 'x': 'q', 'y': 1.0},
 8: {'w': 'b', 'x': 'q', 'y': 2.5},
 7: {'w': 'b', 'x': 'q', 'y': 3.0},
 6: {'w': 'a', 'x': 'k', 'y': 4.5}}

Return dictionary rows grouped by a compound key, including key values:

\>>> df.rows\_by\_key(key\=\["w", "x"\], named\=True, include\_key\=True)
defaultdict(<class 'list'>,
    {('a', 'q'): \[{'w': 'a', 'x': 'q', 'y': 1.0, 'z': 9}\],
     ('b', 'q'): \[{'w': 'b', 'x': 'q', 'y': 2.5, 'z': 8},\
                  {'w': 'b', 'x': 'q', 'y': 3.0, 'z': 7}\],
     ('a', 'k'): \[{'w': 'a', 'x': 'k', 'y': 4.5, 'z': 6}\]})

sample(

_n: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Series | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_\*_,

_fraction: [float](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#float "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Series | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_with\_replacement: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_shuffle: [bool](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#bool "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= False_,

_seed: [int](https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#int "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L10591-L10661)

Sample from this DataFrame.

Parameters:

**n**

Number of items to return. Cannot be used with `fraction`. Defaults to 1 if `fraction` is None.

**fraction**

Fraction of items to return. Cannot be used with `n`.

**with\_replacement**

Allow values to be sampled more than once.

**shuffle**

If set to True, the order of the sampled rows will be shuffled. If set to False (default), the order of the returned rows will be neither stable nor fully random.

**seed**

Seed for the random number generator. If set to None (default), a random seed is generated for each sample operation.

Examples

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.sample(n\=2, seed\=0)  
shape: (2, 3)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ҷ ham в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ҷ str в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ҷ c   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ҷ b   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

_property_ schema_: Schema_[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L907-L924)

Get an ordered mapping of column names to their data type.

Examples

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6.0, 7.0, 8.0\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.schema
Schema({'foo': Int64, 'bar': Float64, 'ham': String})

select(

_\*exprs: IntoExpr | Iterable\[IntoExpr\]_,

_\*\*named\_exprs: IntoExpr_,

) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L9532-L9632)

Select columns from this DataFrame.

Parameters:

**\*exprs**

Column(s) to select, specified as positional arguments. Accepts expression input. Strings are parsed as column names, other non-expression inputs are parsed as literals.

**\*\*named\_exprs**

Additional columns to select, specified as keyword arguments. The columns will be renamed to the keyword used.

Examples

Pass the name of a column to select that column.

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8\],
...         "ham": \["a", "b", "c"\],
...     }
... )
\>>> df.select("foo")
shape: (3, 1)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Multiple columns can be selected by passing a list of column names.

\>>> df.select(\["foo", "bar"\])
shape: (3, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Multiple columns can also be selected using positional arguments instead of a list. Expressions are also accepted.

\>>> df.select(pl.col("foo"), pl.col("bar") + 1)
shape: (3, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 9   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Use keyword arguments to easily name your expression inputs.

\>>> df.select(threshold\=pl.when(pl.col("foo") \> 2).then(10).otherwise(0))
shape: (3, 1)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ threshold в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i32       в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 0         в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 0         в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 10        в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

Expressions with multiple outputs can be automatically instantiated as Structs by enabling the setting `Config.set_auto_structify(True)`:

\>>> with pl.Config(auto\_structify\=True):
...     df.select(
...         is\_odd\=(pl.col(pl.Int64) % 2 \== 1).name.suffix("\_is\_odd"),
...     )
shape: (3, 1)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ is\_odd       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ ---          в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ struct\[2\]    в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ {true,false} в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ {false,true} в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ {true,false} в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

select\_seq(

_\*exprs: IntoExpr | Iterable\[IntoExpr\]_,

_\*\*named\_exprs: IntoExpr_,

) вҶ’ DataFrame[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L9634-L9657)

Select columns from this DataFrame.

This will run all expression sequentially instead of in parallel. Use this when the work per expression is cheap.

Parameters:

**\*exprs**

Column(s) to select, specified as positional arguments. Accepts expression input. Strings are parsed as column names, other non-expression inputs are parsed as literals.

**\*\*named\_exprs**

Additional columns to select, specified as keyword arguments. The columns will be renamed to the keyword used.

See also

[`select`](../expressions/api/polars.select.html#polars.select "polars.select")

serialize(

_file: IOBase | [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | Path | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
 \= None_,

_\*_,

_format: SerializationFormat \= 'binary'_,

) вҶ’ [bytes](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#bytes "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [str](https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#str "(in Python v3.13)")
 | [None](https://docs.python.org/3/library/constants.html#None "(in Python v3.13)")
[\[source\]](https://github.com/pola-rs/polars/blob/py-1.24.0/py-polars/polars/dataframe/frame.py#L2587-L2649)

Serialize this DataFrame to a file or string in JSON format.

Parameters:

**file**

File path or writable file-like object to which the result will be written. If set to `None` (default), the output is returned as a string instead.

**format**

The format in which to serialize. Options:

*   `"binary"`: Serialize to binary format (bytes). This is the default.
    
*   `"json"`: Serialize to JSON format (string).
    

Notes

Serialization is not stable across Polars versions: a LazyFrame serialized in one Polars version may not be deserializable in another Polars version.

Examples

Serialize the DataFrame into a binary representation.

\>>> df \= pl.DataFrame(
...     {
...         "foo": \[1, 2, 3\],
...         "bar": \[6, 7, 8\],
...     }
... )
\>>> bytes \= df.serialize()
\>>> type(bytes)
<class 'bytes'>

The bytes can later be deserialized back into a DataFrame.

\>>> import io
\>>> pl.DataFrame.deserialize(io.BytesIO(bytes))
shape: (3, 2)
в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ foo в”Ҷ bar в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ --- в”Ҷ --- в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ i64 в”Ҷ i64 в”Ӯ
в•һв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Әв•җв•җв•җв•җв•җв•Ў
в”Ӯ 1   в”Ҷ 6   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 2   в”Ҷ 7   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ 3   в”Ҷ 8   в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ
